In Tokyo, a renowned musical figure, Mamoru Samuragochi, aged 50, was widely acclaimed as a prodigious composer whose works graced popular video games and the skating routine of a leading Olympian. He was hailed as Japan's contemporary Beethoven, due to his deafness. However, it has been revealed that his magnum opus was a carefully crafted deception. On Thursday, Japan was shocked to discover that one of its most revered musicians had orchestrated a complex fraud, with someone else secretly penning his most celebrated compositions since the 1990s. The public, captivated for years by Western classical music, responded with regret, fury, and even the threat of legal action following Mr. Samuragochi's confession of his ghostwriting arrangement. The outrage intensified when the ghostwriter himself emerged, accusing Mr. Samuragochi of fabricating his hearing disability, presumably to garner public sympathy and cultivate his Beethoven persona. The scandal erupted on Wednesday, when Mr. Samuragochi publicly admitted that another person had penned his most iconic works, including Symphony No. 1 "Hiroshima," a classical music sensation in Japan, themed around the 1945 atomic bombing of his hometown; the Resident Evil and Onimusha video game themes; and Sonatina for Violin, slated for use by Japanese figure skater Daisuke Takahashi in the upcoming Sochi Olympics.
A group of academic feminists have expressed opposition to proposals to criminalize street harassment in France, arguing that such legislation could unfairly target men with migrant backgrounds. In a letter to Equality Minister Marlène Schiappa, these academics contend that racialised, working-class men already face disproportionate police violence and oppression, and that training perpetrators would be a more effective solution. The academics argue that creating a new offense for street harassment would merely intensify the repression and control of men from disadvantaged groups. The letter, published by Libération, also criticizes the proposed legislation for focusing solely on street harassment, ignoring the fact that women can also be abused in their homes and workplaces. The academics express concern that criminalizing street harassment would only serve to highlight what forms of sexism are unacceptable, while keeping abuse in upscale districts and corporate offices concealed. In September, Minister Schiappa outlined that the new legislation would cover situations where a man follows a woman on a train, repeatedly asking for her telephone number, making her feel oppressed, which would be classified as street harassment. This legislation follows a series of studies revealing the prevalence of street harassment in certain parts of France. A 2015 study conducted in the migrant-heavy districts of Seine-Saint-Denis and Essonne, carried out by the High Council for Equality between Women and Men (HCEfh), concluded that 100% of women had experienced sexual harassment or assault at least once in their lives. In May, Breitbart London reported on areas of Paris becoming virtual "no-go" zones for women, who reported being subjected to verbal abuse by migrants. Local media described how, over the previous 12 months, the east Paris district of Chapelle-Pajol, which has seen an influx of immigrants and drug dealers, has become a hotspot for groups of young men harassing and even assaulting women who pass by.
Immediately address the issue: Cisco has disclosed that several variants of its Adaptive Security Appliance (ASA) devices are susceptible to a remote code execution flaw. The root cause lies in the manner ASA products reassemble fragmented Internet Key Exchange (IKE) packets. A defect in Cisco's implementation of the fragmentation protocol results in bounds-checking errors. As detailed in a post by Exodus Intel (with a nod to @SwiftOnSecurity), the bug enables an attacker to overflow a heap buffer with unauthorized data, thereby creating a remote code execution vulnerability. The affected ASA models include the 5500, 5500-X, ASA Services Module for Catalyst 6500 switches and 7600 Series routers, the ASA 1000V Cloud Firewall, the Adaptive Security Virtual Appliance, the Firepower 9300 ASA module, and the ISA 3000. Both IPv4 and IPv6 traffic can trigger the vulnerability. According to Exodus Intelligence, the code issue arises because although the fragment length is 16 bits, Cisco restricts its queues to 8 bits. Attackers can manipulate this limitation by creating a reassembly queue where one of the fragments has a length less than the default fragment header size of 8 bytes, thereby underflowing the copy length during reassembly. This action merely forces a reboot of the targeted system, but Exodus Intel demonstrates how this can be leveraged to insert attacker code into a specified location in writable memory, granting the attacker control over the device. Cisco has issued a patch for the affected software versions.
In a pub, there are six companions. The first one remarks, 'My glass is half empty, it's time for another refill.' The second one counters, 'My glass is half full, I'm content for the moment.' The third one points out, 'There's a queue at the bar, let's wait a bit.' The fourth one suggests, 'We're going to wait anyway, so we might as well go up and order two rounds, let's get quite tipsy while we're here.' The fifth one rises and departs, as he's not in the mood for disputes, waiting, or excessive drinking. The sixth one finishes off everyone's drinks while they deliberate on their next move. The lesson here? The pessimist is perpetually wanting more, the optimist can be irritatingly content, the realist is merely annoying, the cynic incites conflicts, the quitter is insignificant, and the opportunist has all the enjoyable experiences. Therefore, the next time you're out for drinks, argue less and have more fun, because if you don't, someone else will, at your expense.

Malaysian authorities have apprehended four individuals on suspicion of terrorist connections between August 2nd and September 17th. Among the arrested are three foreign nationals who have since been expelled from the country. A Bangladeshi restaurant owner, under investigation for allegedly facilitating the illegal transport of weapons for international terror organizations, was one of those detained. Interpol had issued a "Red Notice" for this individual. A Nepalese citizen, who managed an entertainment venue, was also arrested on charges of forging travel documents for members of international terror groups. A Moroccan man, believed to be associated with Islamic State, is another suspect. He had previously been detained by Turkish authorities for attempting to enter Syria illegally. The fourth individual arrested is a Malaysian citizen who was employed as a personal driver for a businessman. He is suspected of having ties to Muhammad Wanndy Mohamad Jedy, a person police claim has been actively promoting Islamic State activities on his Facebook page.
Prepare for your adult children's return home permanently. Take down the door knockers and close the shutters, giving the appearance that no one is home. A recent study by Fidelity Investments and Stanford Center on Longevity, involving 9,000 employees, revealed that one out of nine baby boomer parents have experienced this situation in the past year. The return of the so-called "boomerang kids" may save on rent and household expenses, but the parents seem to bear the brunt of the strain: 68% reported increased stress levels, 53% admitted to being less happy, and another 53% claimed they had less leisure time. Additionally, more than three-quarters (76%) reported higher expenses. Even older millennials are turning to their parents as a housing option, with a 2.7 times higher likelihood of living in their parents' homes compared to those under 55 years old in 1999, according to data from real estate site Trulia. Generation-Xers, currently in their mid-30s to early 50s, were 2.2 times more likely to live with their parents. Katie Taylor, vice president of thought leadership at Fidelity, advises parents to be realistic about their financial situation. "No parent is going to want to say no to a child who needs help, but certainly being realistic about the financial situation is important," she said. An increasing number of American adults are living with their parents and grandparents, with 19% of the U.S. population (approximately 61 million people) residing in multigenerational households, up from 17% (42 million) in 2009 and 12% (27.5 million) in 1980, according to the Pew Research Center. However, not all millennials are as often accused of being lazy or entitled. Approximately one in four 25- to 34-year-olds living at home without employment or education do so due to health issues or caregiving responsibilities. Moreover, more than a third of Americans, including millennials, anticipate providing financial assistance to their parents in the near future, according to another survey. Some are even making efforts to help their parents save for retirement.

Unpublished photographs from the Second Boer War, depicting battle scenes, have been discovered in a Derbyshire home. These images, along with medals and other artifacts, will be auctioned off later in July by Hanson's Auctioneers. The auctioneer, Charles Hanson, described the find as a "time capsule" that offers new insights into the war. The images were taken by Robert Oliver, a survivor of the 1899-1902 conflict. The photographs provide a grim glimpse into the reality of war, depicting dead soldiers in fields, funeral processions, and even a Boer War dog. One image shows a British soldier's coffin being lowered into the ground. The collection also includes personal items such as hats, gloves, and medals. One intriguing item is a photograph of a dog, dressed in a cap and smoking a pipe, about whom little is known. Robert Oliver, the photographer, had an adventurous youth. At 16, he ran away and ended up working as a lumberjack in Canada. He later joined the Staffordshire Police, earning a reputation for being both funny and strict. He also owned and ran the Devonshire Pub in Hartington, Derbyshire. The auction will take place on 25 July.

The Hague (Reuters) - In a landmark decision, an international arbitration court on Thursday ruled in favor of Slovenia in a longstanding maritime dispute with Croatia, granting it direct access to international waters in the Adriatic Sea. The Permanent Court of Arbitration's decision is final and binding, although Croatia, which withdrew from the proceedings in 2015, has stated it will disregard the ruling. The presiding Judge Gilbert Guillaume declared that Slovenia should enjoy "uninterrupted access" to the sea it shares with Croatia, as determined in the case between the European Union neighbors. Croatian Prime Minister Andrej Plenkovic responded, stating, "This decision is not legally binding for us in any way and we have no intention to implement it." Slovenia's government expressed satisfaction with the ruling, calling it "definitive and legally binding." Prime Minister Miro Cerar told a news conference, "Slovenia will continue its good cooperation with Croatia and will not take any action that would exacerbate our relationship." The countries have been at odds over a contested section of their sea and land border since both declared independence from the former Yugoslavia in 1991. The dispute, centered on the bay of Piran, delayed Croatia's EU accession for many years. Only after both parties agreed to arbitration was Zagreb admitted to the bloc in 2013. The court has now determined that Slovenia will be granted the majority of the Piran bay area as its territorial waters. Additionally, the tribunal established a 2.5 nautical-mile wide and approximately 10 nautical-mile long corridor through Croatian waters to provide Slovenia with long-sought direct access to international waters. The court ruled, "The zone shall give freedom of communication to all ships and aircraft, civil and military, of any state for the purpose of access to Slovenia." Croatia withdrew from the arbitration procedures in 2015 following the leak of a tape showing a Slovenian judge on the panel exchanging confidential information with the Ljubljana government. The judge involved subsequently resigned, and the court decided to continue with the case, asserting that the incident had
REC Silicon ASA (STO:RECO) announced on Friday that it will not meet its previous guidance for third-quarter (Q3) polysilicon production and sales due to the ongoing solar trade war between the US and China and the recent decline in photovoltaic (PV) market conditions. As a result, the company expects its Moses Lake facility in Washington to operate at approximately half capacity by October 1, 2016, with production levels remaining lower until market conditions improve. REC Silicon now projects Q3 polysilicon sales volumes, excluding fines and powders, to be approximately 1,800 tonnes. The company anticipates July-September revenues to range between USD 45 million (EUR 40m) and USD 50 million, a decrease from USD 71.1 million in the previous quarter due to lower Fluidised Bed Reactor (FBR) sales volumes. The company's Q3 total polysilicon production volumes are forecasted to reach 3,900 tonnes, falling short of the previous guidance for 4,490 tonnes. FBR production is expected to be 3,300 tonnes, compared to the prior projection for 3,830 tonnes. Additionally, REC Silicon is in discussions with its joint venture partner to defer beyond 2018 the second and third capital contributions, totaling USD 169 million, required for the construction of a FBR polysilicon plant in Yulin, China. The company stated it will not be able to make these contributions until the trade war is resolved. (USD 1.0 = EUR 0.892)
A minister at Phillips Exeter Academy proposed that a student accused of sexual misconduct bake bread weekly for his alleged victim as a form of atonement, according to The Boston Globe. This unusual arrangement was reported by The Globe's Spotlight team, amid increased scrutiny of how New England's prestigious boarding schools manage campus sexual misconduct. In May, The Globe disclosed that a renowned teacher and administrator at Phillips Exeter had admitted to past sexual misconduct, but the school had not disclosed this information to students and alumni. Last fall, 17-year-old student Michaella Henry informed school officials that a male student had placed his hands under her shirt and grabbed her bottom, despite her repeatedly saying "No." Instead of involving the police, school Rev. Robert Thompson convened a meeting with the accused student, Chukwudi "Chudi" Ikpeazu, and Henry to resolve the matter. The outcome of this meeting was an agreement that Ikpeazu would bake a weekly serving of "monkey bread" and deliver it to Henry. Additionally, the minister urged Ikpeazu to perform an "act of penance" by baking bread and delivering it to Henry for the remainder of the year. Rev. Thompson later commended Henry for accepting the arrangement, stating, "You did a great service for Chudi, because you gave him an opportunity to express his regret and to take responsibility for what he had done." However, this arrangement only added to Henry's stress, as she was required to meet with Ikpeazu weekly. Henry eventually reported the incident to the police in the spring, and Ikpeazu is scheduled for arraignment on a misdemeanor charge of sexual assault in August, according to The Globe. You can find the full story in The Boston Globe.
Graduates from the class of 2015 exited campus carrying an average of $30,000 in student debt, a 4% increase from the previous year, as per a report published by The Institute for College Access and Success (TICAS) on Tuesday. TICAS president Lauren Asher expressed concern, stating, "We must strive to make college more affordable and reduce the burden of debt for students and their families." Average student debt in California was $22,000, the third lowest in the nation. However, the rate of increase in California is consistent with the national trend. Notably, National University graduates leave with almost $53,000 in debt, leading the California colleges. At University of California campuses, student debt ranged from $17,869 at U.C. Berkeley to $22,580 at U.C. Santa Cruz. On the other hand, at California State University campuses, debt among graduates ranged from $10,872 at Fresno State to $23,973 at Humboldt State. The report, however, omits data from for-profit colleges, as these institutions often do not disclose the amount of debt their students accrue. Diane Cheng, TICAS associate research director, notes, "The state averages might be even higher than they appear." This is because the state averages are based on voluntary reporting from colleges about their graduates' combined federal and private loan debt. Schools with high debt levels may choose not to disclose data, and schools that do report may not be aware of all their students' private loans. TICAS has analyzed data from the U.S. Department of Education to reveal that in 2012, student debt for graduates at for-profit colleges was approximately $40,000. The report suggests several recommendations, including using financial need as the primary factor for awarding publicly funded grants for college students to reduce reliance on loans, informing students of their college loans to aid in decision-making, and following California's lead by requiring colleges to inform students about untapped federal aid before approving private loan requests.

The Department of Justice (DOJ) is advocating for the inclusion of a question about citizenship status in the 2020 census forms, as stated in a letter from DOJ lawyer Arthur Gary to Census Bureau official Dr. Ron Jarmin, dated December 12th. The letter suggests that the bureau should incorporate this question to facilitate the enforcement of the Voting Rights Act, stating, "To effectively enforce these requirements, the Department requires a reliable estimation of the citizen voting-age population in localities where voting rights violations are suspected or alleged." The Census Bureau has confirmed the receipt of the letter, indicating that the request will follow the standard process for any potential question. The letter's emergence coincides with numerous reports suggesting that the Trump administration may include an immigration-related question in the 2020 census. Critics argue that such a question could deter responses, while supporters contend it would safeguard the integrity of future elections.
Fulham Football Club is pleased to announce the signing of defensive midfielder Mickael Tavares on a short-term deal, effective from October 5, 2012. The 29-year-old French-born Senegalese international joins the club as a free agent. Tavares worked under Martin Jol at Hamburger SV during the 2008/09 Bundesliga season and boasts 25 caps for Senegal's national team. He started his senior career at SC Abbeville, scoring nine goals in 26 games during the 2002/03 season. Subsequently, he played for FC Nantes, FC Tours, and Slavia Prague, where he featured in the Champions League. After spending two seasons in Prague, Tavares moved to Jol's Hamburg in 2009. During his tenure with the German club, he was loaned to FC Nuremberg and Middlesbrough. He made 12 appearances for Middlesbrough in the Championship during the 2010/11 season before returning to Hamburg. Tavares is now a free agent after departing Hamburg this summer.

Bill Gates, co-founder of Microsoft and philanthropist, announced on Sunday that the Bill & Melinda Gates Foundation will increase its funding to combat malaria, with a 30% rise in the budget dedicated to this cause. This will result in over $200 million being spent annually on malaria eradication efforts, in addition to the foundation's existing contributions to the Global Fund to Fight AIDS, Tuberculosis, and Malaria. The Gates Foundation is expected to allocate more than $500 million this year towards fighting various diseases, including pneumonia and diarrheal and parasitic diseases in impoverished nations. Gates expressed optimism that malaria could be eradicated during his lifetime, stating this during a global health conference in New Orleans. The foundation's strategy includes the development of a drug or vaccine to eliminate malaria in asymptomatic carriers. In relation to malaria, which claims over 600,000 lives each year, the foundation will provide a $156 million grant to the PATH Malaria Vaccine Initiative (MVI) to develop new vaccines that disrupt the malarial parasite's transmission cycle. Steve Davis, PATH's president and CEO, commented that this grant will enable PATH to continue its work in implementing a strategy aimed at controlling, eliminating, and ultimately eradicating malaria. In addition to malaria, the Gates Foundation has pledged $50 million for research into Ebola treatments, tests, and vaccines. Gates emphasized that a larger effort is needed to halt the current Ebola outbreak, which has resulted in approximately 5,000 deaths across eight countries this year. He urged all countries to enhance their healthcare systems and invest in the development of new drugs and vaccines. Gates also warned that in the coming decades, we may face an epidemic more transmissible than the current Ebola outbreak and urged all nations to prepare accordingly.

Discover a less-known capability of Near Field Communications (NFC): generating power. While it's not enough to replace your electric service, it does provide a small amount of power suitable for powering a Small E Ink display. Liliputing uncovered this intriguing detail on NFC Brief, and although it may seem gimmicky, there are potential practical applications. E Ink displays only need power when the screen is updated with new information. So, you could tap an NFC-enabled smartphone to a special E Ink display, wirelessly transferring both the data and the power to display it. For instance, consider a demonstration video showcasing this concept. The special NFC tag was developed jointly by Intel Labs, the University of Washington, and the University of Massachusetts Amherst. At present, there's no commercial product utilizing this technology, but the idea and demonstration are captivating. Imagine secondary displays in your car, on your desk, or even built into the backs of laptop bags. These displays could show static, yet useful information without the need for additional power.
Overweight schoolchildren, particularly those who remain so from kindergarten through fifth grade, may exhibit poorer math skills and lower social and interpersonal skills compared to their leaner peers. A study published in the June 14 issue of Child Development, which involved 6,250 children from a nationally representative ongoing government study, found this correlation. Researchers gathered data on the children's social skills, emotional well-being, and academic abilities, as well as their heights and weights at five different points throughout the study. They discovered that persistently obese children, starting from kindergarten, performed significantly worse on math tests by first grade. For boys who became obese later, in third or fifth grade, no significant drop in math scores was observed, but girls who became obese at later ages showed a temporary decline in math skills. However, the negative effects of obesity extend beyond math performance. The study found that girls who were persistently obese also had fewer social and interpersonal skills. Boys and girls who were obese throughout the study reported feeling sadder, lonelier, and more anxious, which could have contributed to their math performance. Study author Sara Gable, an associate professor of nutrition and exercise physiology at the University of Missouri-Columbia, stated that childhood obesity, especially obesity that persists throughout the elementary grades, can harm children's social and emotional well-being and academic performance. Dr. Becky Hashim, a clinical child psychologist, suggests that the relationship between obesity and social, emotional, and academic problems is complex. Being overweight could potentially weaken social skills if a child is isolated due to bullying or the stigma of being overweight. On the other hand, children with poor social skills might turn to food for comfort, leading to weight gain. In other words, it's a cyclical issue. Hashim also noted that feelings of sadness, loneliness, or anxiety in and of themselves may hinder school performance, making it more difficult to pay attention and ask questions.
Multitudes of rats have invaded villages in southern Myanmar, leading the authorities to offer residents 3p (equivalent to 4 US cents) for each rat they eradicate. The villagers have been employing makeshift weapons such as sticks, slingshots, and rocks in their efforts to combat the infestation. According to a local news agency, they have already eliminated over 4,000 rodents. Although the primary concern is the potential diseases these rats may spread, the villagers are also apprehensive about the possible indications of other calamities. As Regional MP Phyo Zaw Shwe told AFP news agency, "locals are also worried about floods or earthquakes because of traditional beliefs that these animals can predict bad weather." This belief might not be entirely unfounded. A study by Japanese scientists has suggested that rats might be sensitive to electromagnetic waves that precede earthquakes, as reported by AFP. The rodents' carcasses have been sent for testing, but no diseases have been detected so far. Local officials attribute the infestation to the heavy rainfall in Myanmar's Ayeyarwady region, which has caused significant food shortages. This is not the first time a rat plague has posed a threat to villages in Myanmar. In 2008, thousands of people in the north-western Chin State faced the risk of starvation due to the rodents consuming bamboo fruits and then food crops. This phenomenon occurs approximately once every 50 years. When the plague struck in the 1950s, it is estimated that 15,000 people perished from starvation.

Thirteen states this year have experienced their unemployment rates reaching record lows, a feat not achieved since the federal government began tracking state-level data over four decades ago. Eight years following the end of the most severe recession in recent history, a diverse range of states, from the traditionally liberal like Hawaii and California, to the conservative states such as Idaho and Texas, are currently experiencing economic growth. In October, the unemployment rates in Alabama, Hawaii, Maine, Mississippi, Tennessee, Texas, and Washington matched or surpassed their all-time lows, as reported by the Bureau of Labor Statistics (BLS) in their monthly report issued last Friday. Additionally, California, Colorado, Idaho, North Dakota, and Oregon hit new lows earlier this year. Conversely, in 2010, during the heart of the Great Recession, six states - California, Colorado, Florida, Georgia, Nevada, and North Carolina - recorded their highest unemployment rates ever. Oregon, Rhode Island, and Kansas set their own record highs in 2009. Currently, the national unemployment rate stands at 4.1 percent, the lowest it has been since December 2000, when it was 3.9 percent. Thirteen states have unemployment rates significantly lower than the national average, while fifteen states have rates significantly higher. Hawaii holds the distinction of having the lowest unemployment rate in the nation, at 2.2 percent in October, followed by North Dakota (2.5 percent), Colorado, Nebraska, and New Hampshire (all at 2.7 percent). On the other hand, Alaska's unemployment rate remains the highest in the nation at 7.2 percent, followed by the District of Columbia (6.6 percent) and New Mexico (6.1 percent). In the past year, Alabama's unemployment rate has decreased the most, dropping by 2.5 percentage points, as reported by the BLS. Tennessee's unemployment rate has fallen by 2 percentage points, from 5 percent to 3 percent. Only two states - Alaska and South Dakota - and the District of Columbia have seen their unemployment rates increase over the past 12 months.

The cause of death was carbon monoxide poisoning from a gas-powered generator, as confirmed by local police officials. According to the Princess Anne Police Chief, Scott Keller, the children were found in their beds, appearing to be asleep. Delmarva Power, the utility company, stated that they had disconnected power to Rodney Todd's home in Princess Anne, Maryland, as it was illegally connected to the power grid. The company emphasized that the power was not disconnected due to non-payment. After the power was disconnected, Todd purchased a generator to heat his home, as reported by his stepfather, Lloyd Edwards. Russ Paulsen, executive director of community preparedness at the American Red Cross, pointed out that unpaid electric bills often force people to resort to alternative means of heating and lighting their homes, sometimes with fatal consequences. He noted that impoverished neighborhoods are six times more likely to experience house fires than wealthier ones, and a lack of smoke detectors in these areas increases the danger. The Red Cross distributes smoke detectors for free and provides aid to survivors of house or apartment fires and carbon monoxide poisoning. Paulsen mentioned that each smoke detector reduces the risk of death by fire by half. Carbon monoxide, Paulsen explained, clouds thinking and puts one to sleep, preventing them from waking up. Authorities are currently investigating the deaths and have obtained records related to Todd's home from Delmarva Power. Friends and family described Todd as a dedicated father who was struggling to provide for his children. Tyisha Luneice Chambers, the children's mother, expressed her despair, stating, "If I had known he was without electricity, I would have helped." Todd worked at a kitchen at the nearby University of Maryland Eastern Shore. In previous years, he had requested assistance with his heating bill from Somerset County, but this year, he did not apply for help, according to Tom VanLandingham, who directs its Office of Home Energy Programs. The identities of the children were confirmed by Bonnie Edwards, who claimed to be their grandmother. She identified the two boys as Cameron, 13, and ZhiHeem
In the wake of the Paris terrorist attacks, a significant number of Republican governors across more than two dozen states have expressed their disapproval towards Syrian refugees, stating that they are not welcome within their state borders, despite the lack of authority governors hold to enforce such bans. In contrast, Washington Governor Jay Inslee issued a warm welcome to refugees from Syria and other countries. Recalling the internment of Japanese people during World War II out of fear of disloyalty, Inslee expressed regret for the country's past actions and emphasized the importance of not succumbing to fear in the present. Washington has admitted 2,352 Syrian refugees since 2003, with 38 of them settling in the state, primarily in Seattle and Kent. While the number of Syrian refugees in Washington is relatively small, the state has welcomed a total of 32,898 refugees since 2003, making it the seventh-highest state in terms of refugee intake, according to data from the U.S. Department of State. California leads the way with 88,032 refugees, followed by Texas, New York, Florida, Minnesota, Arizona, and Washington. At the opposite end of the spectrum, only one refugee has settled in Wyoming. Many of the refugees who have settled in Washington are from the Middle East or majority-Muslim countries, with Somalia and Iraq being the third and fourth largest refugee groups, respectively. Seattle has welcomed the most refugees of any city in Washington, with nearly one-third of the total number of refugees settling there. Tukwila and Kent stand out for their high refugee population relative to their size, with close to 4 percent of each city's total population being refugees. A formal currency union between an independent Scotland and the UK, as proposed by keeping the pound, is unlikely due to stringent conditions imposed by the UK, according to John Kay, a former economic advisor to Alex Salmond. Kay, a former member of the Council of Economic Advisers, expressed to MSPs that negotiations over a currency deal would be challenging, possibly intractable for Scotland. Alex Salmond has yet to present a plan B for Scotland's currency. Meanwhile, a former chief economist for Scotland warned that no UK chancellor would jeopardize taxpayers' interests in such an arrangement. The SNP government aims to maintain the pound in a monetary union with the UK post-independence, but this idea has been rejected by Chancellor George Osborne and his Labour counterpart, Ed Balls. Kay further explained to Holyrood’s finance committee that the conventional wisdom, particularly in the eurozone, is that a currency union requires fiscal backing. However, he personally believes this is not necessary, yet acknowledges that this belief is widely held among market participants and political circles. Should Scotland vote for independence and enter negotiations over monetary union, Kay predicts that the UK Treasury would impose conditions that a Scottish Government might find difficult to accept. The rest of the UK would seek control over Scotland's banking system and fiscal policy, which they would likely refuse to relinquish. If Scotland were to agree to the UK's demands, it would effectively surrender most of the "economic policy levers it hoped to gain by independence." The committee was gathering evidence on Scotland's public finances following the referendum. Gavin McCrone, a former chief economist at the Scottish Office, added that a UK chancellor, without electoral responsibility for Scotland, would unlikely risk taxpayers in the rest of the country for Scottish debt or bad debt. McCrone believes this is the primary reason for the rejection of currency union by Osborne and others. Yet, he acknowledges that negotiations would still take place.

The Supreme Court has referred the safety, efficacy, and justification of fixed dose combination (FDC) drugs to the Drugs Technical Advisory Board (DTAB) for re-evaluation. The DTAB, or a sub-committee it appoints, will conduct an examination, hear all relevant parties, and submit a report to the government within six months. The court's order does not affect the 15 FDCs licensed before 1988 and maintains the status quo for the 329 FDCs being reviewed. The All India Drugs Action Network praised the decision, stating that it paves the way for the government to eliminate numerous irrational, unscientific, and hazardous FDCs in India. Approximately half of the 329 FDCs under review are considered irrational, and the network suggests the government should proactively remove other irrational FDCs for patient safety. Pfizer Ltd, whose Corex cough syrup was among the FDC drugs banned by the government, expressed support for the government's goal of eliminating irrational combinations and unapproved medicines through consultation. In January, the government appealed against a December 2016 ruling by the Delhi High Court that quashed its notification banning 344 FDC drugs due to health risks and lack of therapeutic justification. The Supreme Court had previously stayed all high court proceedings against the ban on 344 FDC drugs in March. An FDC drug contains multiple active ingredients in a fixed dosage ratio. The ban affected around 6,000 brands from major pharmaceutical companies like Pfizer Ltd, Wockhardt Ltd, Alkem Laboratories Ltd, Cipla Ltd, Sanofi India Ltd, and Sun Pharmaceutical Industries Ltd. The ban was enforced following a report by a six-member committee headed by Chandrakant Kokate, vice-chancellor of KLE University, Karnataka. The Kokate panel, which submitted its report on January 20, 2015, labeled 963 FDCs as irrational, posing health threats. The Delhi High Court had previously quashed the notification, arguing that the government had failed to consult statutory authorities like DTAB and the Drugs Consultative Committee before the ban.

This potential deceleration may displease some Bank of England officials who are advocating for the first interest rate increase in a decade. The survey indicates that the economy may have regained some speed during the second quarter, possibly expanding at a quarterly rate of approximately 0.4 percent, which is double the pace of the first quarter. However, the latest survey casts doubt on this assumption. As JPMorgan economist Allan Monks noted, the weakness in the UK PMI occurs at a time when the broader European PMIs have significantly improved. The pessimistic mood among services firms might be due to uncertainty following the June election, where Prime Minister Theresa May lost her parliamentary majority, ongoing Brexit negotiations, and the overall economic outlook, according to IHS Markit. A third consecutive monthly drop in car sales in June, albeit from record highs, underscores the slowdown among consumers. Separate official data shows that productivity, a long-standing issue for Britain, declined in the first quarter of the year, marking the first decline since late 2015. In a declassified report published by the State Department on May 14, 1964, it was noted that India had the capability to initiate nuclear weapons development as early as 1964. This report, along with several others, was published by the National Security Archive and the Nuclear Proliferation International History Project on May 18. The report highlighted frequent changes in the fuel core of the Canadian-Indian Reactor (CIR) at Trombay, which occurred as often as every six months. At the time, US intelligence expressed concerns about India's nuclear ambitions. The State Department Bureau of Intelligence and Research (INR) stated in the report, "The Indians are now in a position to begin nuclear weapons development if they chose to do so." However, they also noted that there was no evidence of an ongoing nuclear research and development program, suggesting that such a program would have been evident if it existed. The report expressed concern due to the short six-month period between fuel core changes, which was considered too short for "normal research reactor operations." Instead, it suggested that this time frame was ideal for producing weapons-grade plutonium. Although the INR report did not provide evidence of an existing nuclear weapons program for India, it was "unlikely" that India had decided to build a nuclear bomb. However, the report also noted that it was "no accident" that India's actions up to that point were consistent with the development of a future nuclear weapons program. The State Department report concluded that India had taken the "first deliberate decision in the series leading to a nuclear weapon." This implied that India had access to weapons-grade plutonium or the ability to produce it on demand. As of 2013, it was estimated that India had at least 110 nuclear weapons. Despite signing and ratifying the Biological Weapons Convention and the Chemical Weapons Convention, India has not signed the Nuclear Non-Proliferation Treaty due to its provision that allows countries like the US, Russia, China, UK, and France to maintain nuclear arsenals without obligations to disarm.
At least 42 individuals, predominantly Christians celebrating Christmas, have perished, and numerous others have fallen ill due to consumption of toxic alcohol in Pakistan, according to the Dawn newspaper. Local authorities in the eastern Punjab province have detained all alcohol vendors in Toba Tek Singh, the location of the incident, for interrogation, as stated by Muhammad Shahbaz, a regional police official, to the DPA news agency. The lethal concoction was imbibed during festivities within a Christian community, Shahbaz disclosed. Five Muslims were among the deceased. Victims had been celebrating and consuming alcohol throughout Sunday and into Monday morning, when some began to fall ill and were transported to the hospital, Shahbaz explained. Approximately 150 others were taken to clinics, with many arriving unconscious. Funerals have been conducted for 25 victims, Shahbaz added. One of the suspects, who supposedly organized the alcohol for the Christmas celebrations, is among the dead, making it challenging for police to trace the source of the tainted beverage. Incidents of fatalities from contaminated liquor, frequently homemade, periodically occur in predominantly Muslim Pakistan, often around religious events. In March, at least 40 individuals, primarily Hindus, lost their lives after consuming toxic alcohol just before the Holi festival. It is unlawful for Muslims to purchase or consume alcohol in the country, and minorities require permits to buy it in limited quantities. Christians account for approximately 1.6% of Pakistan's 190 million inhabitants, with most residing in Punjab.

Dear AleFattorini, I'd like to highlight a few aspects that set NetServer apart, but the software center stands out as the most significant difference. The absence of a command line and the elimination of frequent system reboots are welcome changes. I appreciated the documentation of SME because it often combined instructional content with practical applications, aiding my learning process. The admin manual of NetServer is concise and to the point, but for a novice user, it might be too brief, lacking enough details about how to use certain modules effectively. Perhaps providing links to relevant how-to guides within the manual would be beneficial. I've recently revisited the manual and noticed that there are several new topics covered, some of which didn't exist a few months ago. However, I found it inconvenient that there's no direct link from the community platform to the documentation and wiki, especially the how-to section. It currently requires navigating to nethserver.org to access the manual, and I couldn't find a link to the wiki. Having a direct link would make it easier to access the resources, even if bookmarks are available. For instance, when database commands are needed, the manual doesn't offer guidance, but there is a database tutorial in the wiki. Unfortunately, the wiki lacks a matrix detailing database values, which could be useful. I hope this isn't perceived as criticism. I'm merely pointing out differences I've observed. I remain a supporter of NetServer!
In anticipation of the upcoming launch of Sony and SuperBot Entertainment's crossover brawler, PlayStation All-Stars Battle Royale, we thought it would be fitting to provide you with detailed character profiles of the playable fighters. Today, we're focusing on Big Daddy, the genetically enhanced human being from the Bioshock series. Big Daddy is not a singular character; there are several types in the Bioshock games, each with their unique characteristics. However, they all share a common trait: they are formidable and extremely dangerous. Taking one down requires strategic planning, a well-stocked inventory, and carefully placed traps. In PlayStation All-Stars, the Big Daddy presented is a Bouncer type. Bouncers are so named due to their attack that causes the area around them to shake violently by slamming their massive drills into the ground. Big Daddy's primary role is to protect his Little Sister, young girls who have been kidnapped, brainwashed, and transformed into genetic material harvesters. Sisters are almost always seen with Big Daddies, searching for their next victim. Big Daddy's helmet glows yellow when he is cautious, and if anyone approaches too closely or poses a threat to his Little Sister, his helmet glows red, signifying rage, and he will attack relentlessly. Big Daddy's shining moment comes during the first battle with one of his kind. Players are often caught off guard by his onslaught. He uses his drill to disrupt your balance, causing your screen to shake uncontrollably as he charges across the screen, ready to decimate you. His enormous arms make even a punch from him devastating, sending you flying across the screen. When he finally falls, you know you have earned the upgrades that follow. Big Daddy's supers include: - Level 1: A Little Sister attacks anyone in front of Big Daddy - Level 2: Big Daddy becomes enraged. His helmet turns red, his mobility increases slightly, and all attacks become one-hit kills for a short period of time - Level 3: Big Daddy floods the stage, making it feel like Rapture, and significantly slowing down opponent movement. He is also able to lunge across the screen with his drill.
Many Harry Potter enthusiasts would generally view Draco Malfoy as a cruel bully, deserving no sympathy. However, a theory about the sixth and seventh books might cause one to reconsider their opinion of Draco and the Malfoy family. This theory posits that Draco, as a form of punishment ordered by Voldemort, was bitten and became a werewolf. Although this theory is not new, it has recently resurfaced in an Imgur post and is still discussed on the website "Draco Malfoy Is a Werewolf." According to this theory, Draco was bitten by Fenrir Greyback after Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix due to Lucius Malfoy's mistakes. Specifically, Lucius failed to retrieve the prophecy and let one of Voldemort's horcruxes get destroyed in the second book. As Remus Lupin shares in Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince, Greyback is often used by Voldemort to punish his enemies by biting children and turning them into werewolves. In the same book, Harry starts to notice how pale and different Draco behaves. While he assumes it's because Draco has become a Death Eater, with the theory in mind, it's actually because he's a werewolf. This theory also explains why Draco has a close relationship with Severus Snape, as only he could brew the Wolfsbane potion for Draco. Since Draco was no longer a true pure-blood, this theory also explains why the Malfoys eventually betray Voldemort in the last book and leave him behind. They could no longer abide by and fight for pure-bloods because of Draco, so they saw no reason to continue supporting Voldemort. Although this theory is highly persuasive, J.K. Rowling has refuted it on Twitter in 2015. When asked whether Draco was a werewolf, Rowling responded that she hadn't seen it and that it wasn't true. The newly constructed M17/M18 motorway, stretching over 57 kilometers between Gort and Tuam in County Galway, has officially opened. This toll-free highway, which cost nearly half a billion euros to complete, aims to significantly decrease travel times to and from the northwest by avoiding multiple traffic hotspots. The motorway's construction, spanning several years, followed almost fifteen years of planning. For motorists traveling to and from the northwest, the new M17/M18 motorway will eliminate the necessity of passing through the previously congested towns and villages of Tuam, Claregalway, and Clarinbridge. However, there are worries that traffic issues common in those areas may be redirected to Galway city, where gridlock on the eastern approaches is frequent. In response, Transport Infrastructure Ireland and Galway County Council view today's opening as only a part of a larger strategy to manage increased traffic volumes. The forthcoming phase will involve the planned construction of a city bypass for Galway. Yet, these proposals have already sparked controversy in the areas expected to be affected, and the development appears poised for challenges when it reaches the planning stage in the coming months.

Google appears to be effectively addressing its supply chain challenges and fulfilling promised delivery times for new Nexus 4 orders, even exceeding expectations. As reported by CNET this morning, UK customers who placed orders for the Nexus 4 when Google released its latest phone models on Wednesday have already received their devices, less than 48 hours later. Google had initially estimated that phones would take 1 to 2 weeks to reach customers' homes, but it seems that they have made some improvements, either internally or in collaboration with LG, to achieve this quicker turnaround. This rapid delivery time significantly surpasses the lengthy wait times of six, seven, and eight hours that customers experienced before the new year. The status of orders in the US is currently unknown, with no information available on whether the devices are being shipped out yet. If you have received or are expecting your new Nexus 4, please let us know. Based on the current situation in the UK, it appears that Google has learned valuable lessons about managing the supply of popular hardware and may now be capable of handling it more effectively. However, it is unlikely that they have achieved a state of supply equilibrium yet, given the rapid sell-out of the Nexus 4 and the ongoing international stock inconsistencies.

His program was celebrated not only for its victories on the field but also for the academic success of its student-athletes. Despite the ongoing El Niño weather phenomenon, California continues to experience drought conditions, albeit less severely in certain regions such as Marin County. Water restrictions remain in place in Marin County, yet the drought there appears to exist more in name than in reality. Six out of seven reservoirs in the area are at capacity, with the seventh at 95%. Despite a recent break in the rain, El Niño conditions persist, and a drought still affects the rest of the state. The water district attributes this success to residents' continued efforts to reduce water consumption. As of today, the Marin Municipal Water District reports 98% capacity in its seven reservoirs, a significant improvement compared to the rest of California. Crystal Yezman, who manages the Tamalpais watershed for the district, notes that Marin County's near-capacity status is unusual. This year, the county has an additional advantage – an increased population of Coho salmon. Gregory Andrew, the fishery program manager, reported observing one of 500 Coho that returned to Lagunitas Creek this year. This is the best showing in a decade, largely due to well-spaced storms that arrived early, enabling the Coho to swim upstream in December. While the Coho population in Lagunitas Creek is still tenuous, this year has been a positive one for the species. Andrew emphasized, "I have always said that the Coho population on Lagunitas Creek is sustainable but tenuous, and I am not changing that." It's a fragile population experiencing a good year.
The medicinal plant Rhus javanica has been demonstrated to exhibit antiviral activity against herpes simplex virus (HSV) in mice, specifically in an oral therapeutic context. We isolated two primary anti-HSV compounds, moronic acid and betulonic acid, from the herbal extract. The extraction process involved ethyl acetate at a pH of 10, followed by chromatographic separations. Moronic acid was found to be the dominant anti-HSV compound in the ethyl acetate-soluble fraction. The effective concentrations required for a 50% reduction in plaque growth for moronic acid and betulonic acid against wild-type HSV type 1 (HSV-1) were 3.9 and 2.6 micrograms per milliliter, respectively. The therapeutic index of moronic acid (10.3-16.3) was greater than that of betulonic acid (6.2). Moronic acid displayed similar sensitivity to acyclovir-phosphonoacetic acid-resistant HSV-1, thymidine kinase-deficient HSV-1, and wild-type HSV type 2 as it did with wild-type HSV-1. When administered orally to mice infected with HSV-1 three times daily, moronic acid significantly delayed the progression of skin lesions and extended the average survival times of infected mice without causing toxicity, compared to the control group. Interestingly, moronic acid was more effective at reducing virus yields in the brain than in the skin, which correlated with the prolongation of mean survival times. Thus, moronic acid was purified as the primary anti-HSV compound from the herbal extract of Rhus javanica. The mode of its antiviral activity differed from that of ACV. Moronic acid demonstrated oral therapeutic effectiveness in HSV-infected mice and displayed novel anti-HSV activity that mirrored that of the extract.
Repeat DUI offenders may face license revocation for up to a decade starting January 1, 2012, following the signing of a new law by Governor Arnold Schwarzenegger. This legislation, proposed by Assemblyman Jerry Hill of San Mateo, empowers judges to revoke driving privileges for up to ten years for individuals with three or more DUI convictions within the past decade. At present, courts can only impose a three-year license suspension for repeat offenders. Assemblyman Hill believes that this measure could remove over 10,000 repeat DUI offenders from the roads annually. In 2008 alone, approximately 188,000 DUI convictions were reported in the state, with 9,164 of these individuals having their third conviction and 3,200 having four or more DUI offenses. The National Highway Traffic Safety Administration reports that there are 1.5 million DUI arrests in California each year, with one-third of those arrested being repeat offenders. This means that more than 310,000 Californians have three or more DUI convictions, according to the agency. Governor Schwarzenegger stated, "This legislation is an essential step towards making California's roads safer. Those with multiple DUI convictions should not be on the road endangering lives." Assemblyman Hill also urged judges across the state to utilize this new authority and remove repeat DUI offenders from the roads.
Abnormal animal behavior is defined in multiple ways. Statistically, it is characterized by a significant deviation from the norm in terms of occurrence, frequency, or intensity of a behavior. This deviation can be either higher or lower than the usual. In a less technical sense, 'abnormal' refers to any activity that falls outside the typical behavior pattern for animals of a specific species or age. For instance, infanticide, which is commonly observed in some species, might be considered normal for one species but abnormal if its frequency increases or if it is rarely observed in another species. One-time behaviors that are unusual for an individual are not typically included in this definition unless they are repeated by other members of the species and are recognized as part of their behavioral repertoire, or ethogram. While many abnormal behaviors can be grouped under categories such as eliminative, ingestive, or stereotypies, there are several instances where these behaviors overlap and categorization becomes challenging. Some abnormal behaviors may be influenced by environmental factors, such as captivity, while others may be due to underlying medical conditions. The list does not include behaviors exhibited by genetically modified animals that have been engineered to display abnormal behavior, such as reeling mice. As examples, a polar bear might exhibit stereotyped pacing, and an Asiatic elephant might engage in stereotyped rocking and trunk swinging. These behaviors, when repeated excessively, can be indicative of stress, boredom, or other abnormal conditions. References: [1] M.W. Fox, Ed., Abnormal Behavior in Animals. W. B. Saunders Company, Toronto, 1968. Further Reading: [1] Behavior Consultation Media related to Animal behavior at Wikimedia Commons.
A Baltimore police officer, identified as Vincent Cosom, Jr., has been indicted today for second-degree assault, perjury, and misconduct in office. The charges stem from a violent incident caught on camera last June 15, where Cosom allegedly assaulted Kollin Truss at a bus stop located at North Avenue and Greemount. According to the accusations, Cosom punched Truss multiple times in the face while another officer restrained him against a bus shelter, with a third officer present. The footage was flagged by a surveillance camera operator the night of the incident, and both prosecutors and internal affairs detectives were aware of it. However, Cosom was not suspended until Truss's attorney made the video public in September, sparking public outrage due to repeated allegations of excessive police force against civilians and large settlements paid by the Board of Estimates for officer misconduct lawsuits. After the arrest of Truss by Cosom, the officer submitted a statement claiming that Truss had assaulted him, leading to the perjury charge. The two other officers involved in the incident were not charged. The investigation that led to today's indictment was conducted jointly by the Baltimore Police Department and the State's Attorney's Office.

A retail store is a culmination of intricate, strategic spatial arrangements: Necessities such as toilet paper or milk are strategically placed at the back of the store, forcing shoppers to pass by higher-profit items like clothing or toys first. Stores are designed with a clockwise layout, making it convenient for right-handed shoppers to easily browse and pick up items with their dominant hand. Many stores subtly perfume their interiors as research indicates that pleasing scents can stimulate impulsive buying. However, as consumers have become more focused in their shopping, retailers' persuasive tactics are losing their charm. "Consumers are now conditioned to seek specific items and this trend is impacting both online and offline shopping behavior," a retail consultant told The Wall Street Journal. Due to changes in online shopping habits, consumers are now purchasing only what they need, disregarding other items, and leaving. They have developed a resistance to traditional retail strategies. But, in practical terms, how are they resisting these tactics that have been effective for years? For one, some consumers establish self-imposed rules. The Wall Street Journal followed some Wisconsin shoppers in a grocery store and noted their shopping patterns. Some couples shop together to curb each other's impulses. Others avoid using shopping carts as they are cautious about feeling compelled to fill them up.
Over 15,000 individuals have been left homeless and seven sustained injuries due to a fire that erupted in the slum district of Tondo, Manila, according to fire officials. The fire began Tuesday evening in a shanty house within the slum area. Senior Superintendent Wilfredo Tiu, a regional head of the Bureau of Fire Protection, confirmed the origin of the fire. The blaze ravaged for 10 hours, destroying approximately 1,200 shanty houses before it was finally extinguished Wednesday morning. Seven residents were injured as they attempted to save their possessions before evacuating. Three evacuation centers have been set up, and aid, including food and water, is being distributed to the 3,000 affected families who have lost their homes, as reported by welfare officer Regina Jane Mata. Despite the evacuation centers and the fire's containment, many individuals remained on a nearby road with their belongings, including personal items such as clothes, washing machines, and electric fans. The fire caused traffic congestion, obstructing delivery trucks en route to and from the port. Investigators are still working to identify the cause of the blaze, but previous incidents have been attributed to faulty electrical wiring due to the illegal connections in many of the houses in the slum area.

Through the practice of trekchö, the body gradually dissolves, emitting rainbow light, until only the hair and nails remain. With the practice of tögal, the body metamorphoses into pure light and vanishes entirely into the expanse, a feat accomplished by Garab Dorje, Manjushrimitra, Shri Singha, Jnanasutra, and Vairotsana. This was the case with Padmasambhava, Vimalamitra, Nyang Tingdzin Zangpo, and Chetsün Senge Wangchuk. For instance, the body of Lama Achuk shrank from a height of 1.8 meters to about 1 inch, a manifestation of achieving the rainbow body. For specific use cases, MongoDB v3.4 offers the aggregation pipeline operator named $graphLookup. This operator allows for a recursive search within a collection. For further details on $graphLookup, refer to its definition. Using your document hierarchy and values as examples, you can attempt the following aggregation: ``` db.collectionName.aggregate([ { $unwind: { path: "$childrenIdList", preserveNullAndEmptyArrays: true } }, { $graphLookup: { from: "collectionName", startWith: "$_id", connectFromField: "_id", connectToField: "childrenIdList", as: "myparents", restrictSearchWithMatch: { "_id" } } }, { $match: { "_id": 7 } }, { $group: { _id: "$_id", parents: { $addToSet: "$myparents._id" } }} ]); ``` The output should resemble: ``` { "_id" : 7, "parents" : [ [1, 2, 4] ] } ``` However, it's worth noting that if you have a large collection, this query may not be efficient due to the $unwind operation on each document, which prevents the use of indexes. To improve performance, it's advisable to reevaluate your document model structure. Refer to Data Models Tree Structures for guidance. Optimize your document schema according to your application logic and querying requirements, allowing the flexible document schema to follow suit.

This unique retail space will officially open on Friday, November 17th, from 4 to 10 pm, in Akron's Northside Arts District. The marketplace is a celebration of Akron's local culture, featuring over 40 diverse vendors. Established favorites like Rubber City Clothing and Dirty River Bicycle Works have stores, while emerging local vendors fill the Made in Akron section, offering a variety of gift-worthy items such as all-natural skincare products, clothing, jewelry, and art. A spacious central lounge surrounded by food and beverage shops provides a welcoming spot for visitors to take a break and socialize with friends. The Northside Marketplace was developed by the Testa Companies, in collaboration with Downtown Akron Partnership and the Knight Foundation. Its primary purpose is to provide new or small businesses with an opportunity to operate in a physical location without the risk of opening a standalone business. During the grand opening, visitors can enter a drawing to win a gift basket filled with items from each of the Marketplace vendors. Spend more than $100 during the opening weekend, and you'll be eligible to win a weekend getaway package in the Northside District. This prize includes a stay at the Courtyard by Marriott Akron Downtown, a private movie theater screening for two, a five-course meal for two at dba Akron, hand-crafted cocktails at the Northside Speakeasy, and the grand prize winner will be announced on November 20th. The Northside Marketplace can be found at 21 Furnace St. Hours of operation are Monday through Thursday from 4 to 8 pm, Friday from 4 to 10 pm, Saturday from 10 am to 10 pm, and Sunday from 10 am to 6 pm. Parking is available on N. Main St. and Furnace St. For more information, visit the Northside Marketplace website. During the past week, I had the opportunity to visit Guantanamo Bay, thanks to the backing of the Freedom of Press Foundation, during the peak of a widespread hunger strike. Alongside four other media personnel, I toured the detention facilities, including camps 5 and 6, as well as Camp X-Ray, the hospital, library, food preparation areas, and witnessed the prisoners' morning prayers. Although the tour was meticulously planned and orchestrated, it was still an invaluable experience. The military emphasized the challenging and uncooperative nature of the detainees, and their remarkable patience in the face of frequent abuse, such as being splashed with feces and urine. The medical staff shared that not a single hunger-striking prisoner had complained about the force-feeding process, a fact I detailed in an exclusive report for Al Jazeera last week. Our visit concluded on Friday, marking the 100th day of the hunger strike. Over the course of our week, the number of Guantanamo prisoners participating in the hunger strike increased by three, bringing the total to 103. Thirty of these individuals are now being force-fed, as per the government's count. Navy Capt. Robert Durand, a Guantanamo spokesman, informed me that the military will not engage in negotiations with the prisoners to bring an end to the hunger strike. The photographs taken during our visit were scrutinized by the military, and some were edited to conceal surveillance cameras, guard towers, and other sensitive landmarks. This project, initially highlighted by TIME, utilizes a combination of eyewitness accounts and satellite imagery from DigitalGlobe to identify what appears to be piles of bodies in Kadugli and mass graves south of the town. The graves, dug by a yellow earth mover, are approximately 26 meters long and 5 meters wide. According to witnesses, before being buried in the mass grave, some of the bodies were wrapped in white plastic and temporarily stored in piles in Kadugli. As previously speculated, Facebook's video app is now official, as revealed in a blog post detailing upcoming video features. The new Facebook video app for TV offers a fresh way to view Facebook videos on a larger screen. With the app, you can watch videos shared by friends or followed Pages, top live videos from around the globe, and videos recommended based on your interests. Additionally, you can catch up on saved videos for later viewing and revisit videos you've previously watched, shared, or uploaded. However, the forthcoming Facebook app on Apple TV will provide a separate means for viewing videos on the big screen. Facebook indicates that its new video player will be rolled out soon not only on Apple TV but also on other platforms such as Amazon Fire TV and Samsung Smart TV. In addition to the new app, Facebook is introducing auto-play sound on videos, a feature that will be available to everyone shortly. Diane Francis Discusses the Far-Reaching Implications of Overpopulation - January 18, 2012 References: youtu.be, thelavinagency Canadian business author Diane Francis delves into the issue of overpopulation in this speech. She views overpopulation as a predominantly mathematical problem, despite the focus of politicians and global leaders on addressing climate change, pollution, and resource depletion. In her opinion, overpopulation is a far more pressing concern and is, in fact, the underlying cause of these problems. Francis further contends that overpopulation is a female issue, with increased education rates and reduced religious suppression playing significant roles in its management. Thanyarat Doksone, The Associated Press reports that Thai authorities apprehended four individuals, including three local officials and a Myanmar national, on Monday, accused of being part of a transnational crime network involved in the trafficking and ransom of Rohingya Muslims. The alleged network, operating for three or four years, includes individuals from Thailand, Myanmar, and Malaysia. The arrests come after the discovery of a clandestine camp in southern Thailand last week, long known as a trafficking hub for migrants seeking better lives in third countries. The unearthing of the jungle camp was a stark reminder that despite repeated promises by authorities to address the root causes, little progress has been made. The latest incident also tarnished Thailand's image, following a series of disclosures about human trafficking allegedly facilitated by corrupt Thai officials. In June last year, the United States classified Thailand as Tier 3 in its annual evaluation of global efforts to combat human trafficking. Thailand has vowed to take action to avoid being blacklisted, but its reputation has been further damaged by recent AP revelations of Thai fishing vessels holding men from Myanmar, Cambodia, and Laos as forced labor or slaves. Police are currently verifying reports of multiple hidden camps run by traffickers in the mountainous jungles of southern Thailand. They are conducting searches in Khao Kaew mountain, Songkla province, where the discovered camp was located near the Malaysian border, and plan to expand their search to other densely forested areas. "We will not stop here," said Gen. Somyot Poompanmoung, national police chief. "We will search in the widest area and continue until we are certain that there are no other camps left." A lone survivor from the camp, now hospitalized with severe malnutrition, has reportedly told authorities that the smugglers had escaped with around 100 Rohingya earlier last week. The Rohingya, a religious minority, have long faced state-sanctioned discrimination in predominantly Buddhist Myanmar. Violent mob attacks in the past three years have resulted in up to 280 deaths, triggering one of the biggest exoduses since the Vietnam War.
In 1984, a devoted elderly woman named Dorothy purchased front-row tickets at Wrigley Field for the Chicago Cubs games. Over the years, she has remained a steadfast fan, affectionately referring to her team as "my Cubbies." On Saturday night, she was present as the Cubs triumphed over the Dodgers in Game 6 of the NLCS, clinching the pennant. Following the victory, sports journalist Ken Rosenthal spoke with Dorothy, inquiring about her feelings regarding this historic moment. "I wish my brothers were alive to witness this," Dorothy shared, remembering her brothers who were killed in the war, imprisoned in Germany, and overseas during the same period. "They loved the Cubs just as much as I do. Unfortunately, they and my father have passed away. Yet, here I am, still living." When asked about her plans for celebration, Dorothy replied with a casual, "Oh, who knows — I'll probably have a Jagermeister." Indeed, Dorothy is a priceless American treasure and hero. The free movement of labor is a cornerstone of the European project and crucial for the smooth operation of a monetary union. This article presents four informative charts, reflecting current political discourse on migration within the EU. Firstly, we provide a heat map demonstrating the net migration rate (immigrants minus emigrants) per 1000 inhabitants across Europe, based on data from 2012 (latest available). High net immigration is depicted as green, while high net emigration is shown as red. Germany and Belgium have net inflows of 4.3 and 6.5 migrants per 1000 inhabitants, respectively, whereas Spain and Greece have net outflows of -3 and -4, indicating more people leaving than arriving. Secondly, we examine the relationship between unemployment rates and net migration rates. Countries that suffered more severe economic downturns during the crisis, as evidenced by higher unemployment, have experienced larger outflows of people and lower net migration. In general, countries with poorer economic health have seen larger net outflows of people, with those leaving primarily heading to countries with better economic conditions. Thirdly, we identify the main destinations for migrants within Core Europe by analyzing the distribution of population by country of citizenship in 2013 (latest available data). The member-states on the right and left are the primary sending countries, while those in the center are the main host countries in Core Europe. Lastly, it's worth noting that economic migration offers several benefits on both a macro and micro level. On a macro scale, it acts as a macro stabilizer, an essential step towards an optimal currency area. On a micro level, labor mobility improves potential firm-worker matching, addresses skills shortages, and encourages international commerce by reducing cultural barriers to trade.

Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant (ISIL) perpetrated a suicide bombing on an Iraqi army regiment in eastern Fallujah, resulting in the loss of at least 14 lives. According to military sources communicated to Al Jazeera, the attack on Sunday occurred at a base in the village of al-Harariyat. The deceased were reportedly members of the Shia unit, Popular Mobilisation Forces, who are aiding the government in their fight against ISIL. Iraq is currently experiencing its most severe security crisis since the 2011 withdrawal of U.S. troops. ISIL, a faction originating from Iraq's al-Qaeda branch, has gained control over significant portions of the country's north and west, following the capture of Iraq's second-largest city, Mosul, and the majority of the western Anbar province last year. ISIL has been responsible for numerous attacks against government forces, and currently holds approximately a third of Iraq and neighboring Syria within its self-declared "caliphate." Since its inception, Baghdad and other major cities have been plagued with near-daily attacks, including roadside bombs, suicide blasts, and assassinations. These attacks have targeted Iraqi forces, government officials, and civilians, resulting in substantial casualties among the civilian population. The ongoing violence has claimed the lives of hundreds and displaced tens of thousands of Iraqis.
Regarding the utilization of Emacs while coding C++ in Visual Studio: Emacs can be employed (after configuring numerous environmental variables) to communicate with the MSVS C++ compiler through the command line, which VS provides with batch files for setting those variables. You can create a .bat script that accepts an arbitrary number of arguments, executes the VS batch file that sets the environment variables, and then runs those arguments as a command. Here is an example of such a script: ``` rem vc2013.bat @call "c:\Program Files (x86)\Microsoft Visual Studio 12.0\VC\bin\vcvars32.bat" %* ``` From Emacs, you can execute the script using the command `M-x compile vc2013.bat`. As a novice in C++, I would welcome suggestions about this topic, such as what practices to adopt, what to avoid, and the current best practices (some of the links I've found are quite old, dating back to Emacs 19...). Are there actually C++ teams that consist of both Emacs and Visual Studio users? I can envision, for instance, in a Scala (SBT or Maven) project where some developers use Eclipse, others Emacs ENSIME, and they can collaborate harmoniously. However, would a similar collaboration be feasible in a C++ project on Windows with Emacs and Visual Studio? Indeed, such coexistence is possible. I personally only use the VS IDE for debugging (which is rarely necessary). The majority of my coding is done from Emacs. Additionally, you can employ CMake, which generates VC project files, makefiles, etc., from the same build specification.
In 2014, BACtrack, a company that integrates smartphone technology with portable breathalyzers to promote safety, released data from nearly 300,000 breathalyzer tests conducted across the United States. Unsurprisingly, St. Patrick's Day and New Year's Eve emerged as the drunkest days of the year. However, the most shocking finding was that Waltham, Massachusetts, recorded the highest average blood alcohol content (BAC) in December, with a rate of 0.133%. BACtrack's consumption report indicates that 14 out of the 15 heaviest drinking days occur during the winter months, with May 3rd, the weekend before Cinco de Mayo, being the only exception. The day after Valentine's Day also showed a high BAC of 0.092, suggesting that perhaps some lovelorn singles turned to spirits after another V-Day alone. In the city-by-city breakdown, Waltham had the highest BAC for December, narrowly beating out Jersey City, New Jersey (0.132%), Champlin, Minnesota (0.124%), and New Orleans, Louisiana (0.123%). However, a closer look at the data reveals that the sample size is relatively small. Even though 300,000 breathalyzer measurements nationwide sounds impressive, when divided among the 50 states, it amounts to just 6,000 tests per state, with larger states likely conducting more tests. Since Massachusetts has the 14th-highest population, it's reasonable to assume that BACtrack collected around 12,000 samples from the Bay State. With a population of 62,227, Waltham accounts for less than 1% of Massachusetts' total population of 6,692,824. If the same percentage holds true, Waltham is responsible for just 10 of Massachusetts' 1,000 samples in December. Even with this generous assumption, the sample size remains small. If we assume that Waltham residents are more likely to use BACtrack due to their proximity to Boston and tech-savvy lifestyle, and that each person used the breathalyzer five times during a single boozy night in December

Enabling JavaScript is necessary to watch this video. In Little Rock, an Arkansas court order now mandates the recognition of over 500 same-sex marriages conducted in the state last year. This decision allows these couples to enjoy benefits such as filing taxes jointly. Pulaski County Circuit Judge Wendell Griffen validated the marriage licenses issued to same-sex couples following a ruling that struck down Arkansas' ban on gay marriage. The Arkansas Supreme Court temporarily halted the issuance of marriage licenses to same-sex couples for a week in May 2014, and is currently considering an appeal of a voter-approved same-sex marriage ban. As a result of Griffen's ruling, couples can file taxes jointly, enroll together in state health insurance plans, be listed jointly on a child's birth certificate, and even file for divorce. Considering a modification for 75% keyboards: adding the following six keys in the first row – PG Up (R2), PG Down (R3), End (R4), FN (R4), CTRL (R4), and ALT (R4). It's likely that many of us own keyboards of this size. An alternative could be an additional extension set for 75% keyboards, including these keys, as well as the Arrows (R4) and the Win/CTRL/ALT keys on the left. The 75% keys will be part of the base set, as mentioned in the original post. Following the standard Cherry 75% layout, SKIDATA+ will arrange the keys as follows (from top to bottom): Home, PG Up, PG Down, End. I'm unsure about the reference to arrows + Win/CTRL/ALT on the left, as these keys will indeed be included in the base set, in both Winkeyless and Winkey sizes. The base set will comprise keys for 1800, HHKB, 75%, and some extras, all in Skidata colors. You should have most, if not all, keys you need from the base set. As a fellow keyboard enthusiast, my aim has always been to provide a SKIDATA keyset for the community, with a sufficient number of keys to accommodate conventional Cherry-style keyboards. Unfortunately, it's not feasible to support keyboards with unconventional sizes and layouts like the Filco Minila. The clarity will increase once the mockups are posted. Please look forward to that.
