The Catholic Church, under the guidance of the Vatican, has advised its members to exhibit politeness towards individuals exhibiting homosexual tendencies, while persisting in efforts to counteract equality. Upcoming Church documents, released ahead of the Family Synod, have dashed expectations of any loosening of anti-gay policies, despite concerns about the Church's growing disconnect from modern society. Plans for engagement with same-sex couples, which were abandoned following a public rebuke at the 2021 Synod, do not seem to be on the agenda this year. However, the document for this year's synod does advocate for "respect" in a section titled "Pastoral attention to persons with homosexual tendencies." It states: "Every person, regardless of their sexual tendencies, is to be respected for their dignity and should be approached with sensitivity and care, both within the Church and in society." It further suggests that diocesan pastoral projects should allocate special attention to families with individuals exhibiting homosexual tendencies, as well as the individuals themselves. Despite the Pope's recent attempts to improve his image as gay-friendly, he has yet to revoke any actively homophobic and transphobic policies established by his predecessors. Islamabad: A four-member team from Pakistan is expected to travel to India on Sunday, commencing a three-day official visit to inspect the Sabarmati Riverfront Development Project (SRDP), as reported by Dawn online. The Pakistani delegation consists of Lahore Commissioner Rashid Mehmood Langrial, Lahore Development Authority (LDA) Director-General Ahad Khan Cheema, LDA's strategic policy unit chief Moazzam Sipra, and Mustafa Kamal Chaudhry, a technical expert/consultant on urban infrastructure projects, as per Dawn online. The primary purpose of the delegation, according to a Punjab government official, is to analyze the SRDP and implement a similar project in Lahore, since the LDA has initiated work on the feasibility of the Ravi Riverfront Urban Development Project (RRUDP) with the technical assistance of a foreign consultancy firm. The interest in the SRDP was sparked by Prime Minister Nawaz Sharif, who has been urging officials to visit the project following his learning about it. The visit was initially scheduled for the second week of May this year but was postponed due to the officials' commitments to other tasks. The prime minister, during various briefings on the RRUDP at his residence in Jati Umrah (Raiwind), Lahore, repeatedly urged the officials to travel to India. In a recent meeting, Sharif emphasized the need for the officials to visit the SRDP in Ahmedabad and provide an update on the project in the next meeting. According to a senior LDA official, the delegation, led by the commissioner, will cross into India through the Wagah Border and travel to Amritsar to catch a flight to New Delhi. The SRDP is one of the significant developmental initiatives accomplished by Indian Prime Minister Narendra Modi during his tenure as chief minister of Gujarat, the official stated. IANS. Louisiana Legislators to Examine and Debate Marijuana Legalization BATON ROUGE, LA — Louisiana legislators are scheduled to convene later this month to evaluate the practicality and efficiency of legalizing marijuana within the state. The House Criminal Justice Committee is set to assemble on the 21st of January, in response to State Rep. Dalton Honore (D-Baton Rouge), to investigate the prospect of legalizing marijuana in Louisiana. At present, there is no pending legislation to legalize marijuana within the state. Louisiana maintains some of the most stringent penalties for marijuana possession in the nation. A first-time offender, even with a single joint, could face imprisonment for up to six months. A second offense escalates the penalty to five years and a fine of $2,500, with a third offense resulting in a felony conviction and a mandatory minimum 20-year jail sentence. Last year, an initiative aimed at mitigating these excessive penalties – reducing the maximum sentence for a second offense to two years and subsequent offenses to a maximum of eight, while abolishing the mandatory minimum sentence – was approved by the House but failed to garner sufficient support in the Senate for debate and voting. The Legislative Fiscal Office projected that the change would have saved the state $2.2 million in reduced incarceration costs in 2014 had the effort been successful. The sponsor of last year’s bill, Rep. Austin Badon (D-New Orleans), has submitted a comparable bill for 2014, House Bill 14. If enacted, the jail term for a second marijuana arrest would be limited to two years and a fine of $500, and third and subsequent offenses would be capped at a maximum five-year jail sentence and a maximum fine of $2,000. Recent surveys reveal that 53% of Louisiana voters support legalizing marijuana for adults aged 21 and above and regulating its sales. Tags: Austin Badon

Facebook is anticipated to debut its own smartphone within the next year, according to reports. The Social Networking giant, which recently went public, has reportedly been hiring a number of smartphone engineers, as suggested by unnamed sources including Facebook employees. This move comes as the company has acknowledged struggles in monetizing its growing mobile audience. In addition to this, Facebook has recently launched its own mobile app store, the App Center, which offers links to Facebook-enabled apps within Apple's iOS and Google Android stores. Developers will soon have the ability to write apps exclusively for Facebook's store. The New York Times reports that Facebook has also hired experts who have worked on the iPhone and other smartphones. A Facebook employee was quoted as saying that the company's founder, Mark Zuckerberg, is concerned that if Facebook does not create a mobile phone in the near future, it may simply become an app on other mobile platforms. It should be noted that this is not the first time Facebook has been rumored to be developing a smartphone. In 2010, Techcrunch reported that Facebook was "secretly" building a smartphone, although that particular project is said to have fallen through. The company's entry into the smartphone market could be a response to increasing pressure to improve the potential of mobile to generate revenue. In a statement to potential investors, the company admitted concerns about more users accessing Facebook through their mobile devices, a trend which could make it more challenging to sell advertising. When asked by the BBC, a spokeswoman for Facebook declined to comment on the speculation, instead referring to a written statement. The statement reads, "Our mobile strategy is simple: we think every mobile device is better if it is deeply social. We're working across the entire mobile industry; with operators, hardware manufacturers, OS providers, and application developers to bring powerful social experiences to more people around the world."
The Environmental Molecular Sciences Laboratory (EMSL), a national scientific user facility, is situated at the Pacific Northwest National Laboratory and is funded by the Department of Energy’s (DOE) Office of Science. EMSL's primary goal is to discover scientific solutions for energy and environmental issues at a molecular level. Collaborating with approximately 800 scientists from various sectors, including academia, government labs, and industry, EMSL supports both open and proprietary research. These scientists hail from nearly all 50 U.S. states and other countries. EMSL provides in-house tools and allows researchers to design and construct specialized instruments. Researchers utilize EMSL's state-of-the-art supercomputer, Cascade, for a wide range of studies, including investigations into aerosol impacts and water purification. Recently, researchers employed EMSL's unique resources, including its Chinook supercomputer, to examine the types of clouds that form over oceans, which are essential for climate predictions. Current climate models typically average various cloud types over the oceans, often simplifying them into either stratocumulus or cumulus clouds, which span tens to hundreds of kilometers. However, distinct cloud types have different impacts on the amount of sunlight reaching the sea surface, potentially introducing errors into large-scale climate models. Researchers confirmed this assumption by discovering that models that average one type of cloud underestimate actual ocean cloud cover, leading to an overestimation of the sunlight reaching the ocean. Furthermore, these models were found to underestimate temperature variations and movement within the cloud layer. This miscalculation results in models predicting a faster transition from flattened stratocumulus clouds to puffy cumulus clouds and introduces uncertainties into climate projections. These findings at EMSL could lead to more accurate climate projections.
Today, we introduce a new zero-day exploit for Internet Explorer versions 7, 8, and 9 on Windows XP, Vista, and 7. This vulnerability allows attackers to compromise systems merely by visiting a malicious website, granting them the same privileges as the current user. As Microsoft has yet to issue a patch, it is recommended that users switch to browsers such as Chrome or Firefox until a security update is available. The exploit was previously utilized by malicious actors before its publication in Metasploit. Approximately 41% of North American and 32% of global Internet users are at risk due to this vulnerability (StatCounter). We have integrated the zero-day exploit module into Metasploit to enable the security community to test their systems for vulnerabilities and develop countermeasures. The contentious General Practitioner (GP) fee, a subject of debate, could potentially be implemented without parliamentary approval, similar to the government's recent bypass of parliament to implement petrol indexation. Health Minister Peter Dutton has repeatedly declined to rule out utilizing a regulation to reduce Medicare rebates by $5, which would contribute $3.5 billion in savings from the GP fee as outlined in the budget. The government is encountering resistance in obtaining Senate approval for legislation imposing the fee, with opposition from the Australian Medical Association and other key health groups. One of the potential consequences of the GP fee is a decrease in medical research donations, which is not welcome. The Opposition, the Greens, and the Palmer United Party have all stated they will not support the fee. The AMA is concerned that the government may consider bypassing parliament to implement the fee, similar to its recent implementation of the budget measure to index petrol excise by regulation. "As the government becomes increasingly desperate to save money, we would not be surprised if they resort to such measures," said AMA president Dr Brian Owler. He added, "This would cut the rebate, take money away from patients and GPs, and that would be detrimental to healthcare." The Medicare rebate is determined by a Medicare schedule fee, which is set by regulation. The government can simply introduce a regulation to reduce the current $37.05 schedule fee for a GP visit by $5 to $32.05 to achieve the budgeted savings. This reduction would effectively lower the Medicare rebate by $5. When asked about such a move, Health Minister Peter Dutton refused to comment publicly. If the government were to take this route, many GPs might become unsustainable unless they see more patients or introduce a $5 charge to compensate for the rebate cut. According to AMA GP spokesman Dr Brian Morton, "In the end, the government will not save any money, and the fee will be detrimental to prevention and keeping people out of hospital." The parliament has the power to disallow any regulation introduced by Mr. Dutton. However, if he were to introduce it during the final sitting in June next year, the measure would come into effect on July 1 as planned and could not be disallowed until August 18. During the recent G2K16 hackathon, a significant amount of progress was made, as reported by Patrick Wildt. He notes that a key achievement was transitioning armv7 from OABI to EABI. EABI is the standard that most systems expect, and this change will improve compatibility. To facilitate this, a diff and snapshots were prepared in advance, and the change was implemented during the hackathon. Unfortunately, the Zaurus could not handle this ABI shift, so it was removed from the focus. This means that the team can now focus on ARMv7 and take advantage of its beneficial features, such as utilizing the hardware floating point unit. Additionally, armv7 was moved to Position-Independent Executable (PIE) and static-PIE by jsg@. This change will also improve C++ exceptions. Another significant accomplishment was integrating LLVM and the new C++ stack into the tree. This was achieved through coordinated efforts, with Patrick importing libc++, libc++abi, and libunwind, while pascal@ handled the LLVM import. All of this was completed before the hackathon concluded. Now, the team can focus on making it operational. Exciting times lie ahead, but there is also a substantial amount of work to be done.
During his eighth grade year in September, Adam Lanza experienced severe anxiety, as stated by his mother to medical professionals. This anxiety was so intense that his mother, Nancy Lanza, took him to the emergency room at Danbury Hospital for an evaluation. At the age of 13, Lanza was questioned by doctors about his suicidal tendencies and potential for harming others. He responded negatively to both questions. The events of September 2005, as detailed in medical records, indicate a shift in Lanza's emotional state during his middle school years, moving towards a more precarious emotional position. Lanza was diagnosed with a sensory disorder and, according to a family member, Asperger's syndrome. Seven years later, in 2012, Lanza would murder his mother and then carry out a deadly shooting spree at Sandy Hook Elementary School in Newtown. The Hartford Courant obtained exclusive information from medical and school records that had been kept confidential by agencies investigating the shootings. These documents, which span Lanza's life from birth to age 18, include a September 2005 medical summary of the Danbury Hospital emergency room visit. This information provides further insight into Lanza's childhood and adolescence, which, until the Danbury Hospital visit, appeared to be free of major documented crises, including a seemingly stable four and a half years as a student at Sandy Hook Elementary School, where he would later return as a 20-year-old and commit a massacre, killing 20 first-graders, six adults, and then taking his own life. After over a year of testing, YouTube will allow users to opt into the Material Design version on desktop without needing a URL workaround. YouTube aims to make the desktop experience more consistent with its mobile counterpart by adopting a simpler design to better showcase content on the site. The new design incorporates features such as infinite scrolling, an end-to-end user profile banner, and a larger hero video on a user’s profile page. In theater mode, the search bar at the top of the page turns black to match the rest of the screen. Dark Mode can be enabled natively by clicking under the user icon and adjusting settings. The image slider below allows you to compare YouTube on Material Design versus the classic version. The redesigned version features more white space, a lighter-colored search bar, and aligns the YouTube username under videos with current views. The preview is currently open to YouTubers worldwide, but will only be available to a limited number of users. Once a certain percentage of YouTube users have opted in, the team may close the preview to better monitor user feedback. According to Manuel Bronstein, VP of product management at YouTube, the redesign will be rolled out automatically for about 1% of users, with plans to increase rollouts every few weeks. If demand is high, the team plans to expedite the full implementation of the change. To opt into YouTube’s Material Design preview, visit YouTube.com/new. If you decide you don’t like the change, you can revert back by selecting "Restore classic YouTube" from your account menu.

Russia's Foreign Ministry Challenges Indictment Against Manafort October 31, 2017, 10:47 AM GMT / Updated October 31, 2017, 2:47 PM GMT By Alan Kaytukov and Alexander Smith MOSCOW — Russia's Foreign Ministry has contested a factual error in the indictment against Paul Manafort, claiming it proves the allegations are fabricated and not part of a genuine investigation. Manafort, a former campaign manager for President Donald Trump, and his business associate, Rick Gates, face charges such as conspiracy against the U.S., money laundering, acting as unregistered foreign agents, and seven counts of failing to report foreign bank and financial accounts. However, Maria Zakharova, the spokeswoman for Russia's Foreign Ministry, highlighted that the 31-page indictment incorrectly identifies Yulia Tymoshenko as a former president of Ukraine. In reality, Tymoshenko served as the country's prime minister on two occasions before being imprisoned in 2011 on embezzlement charges, which the U.S. and others deemed politically motivated. During an interview with the state-owned Russia 1 television station on Monday, Zakharova expressed her amusement at the error, stating, "I found it quite interesting that, according to the latest findings of American enforcers, the Ukrainian president before [Viktor] Yanukovych was Yulia Tymoshenko. We were not aware of this, but there you go." Zakharova suggested that this mistake discredits the rest of the indictment, commenting, "This is a crucial moment, revealing once more how this document was concocted. One cannot overlook such errors when talking about a serious investigation." The indictment against Manafort and Gates states that they lobbied multiple members of Congress and their staffs about Ukraine sanctions, the legitimacy of Ukraine elections, and the propriety of Yanukovych's imprisoning his presidential rival, Yulia Tymoshenko (who had served as Ukraine's prime minister, not president, prior to Yanukovych). Gmail Labs has introduced a new opt-in feature, allowing users to send text messages to mobile phones via the built-in Chat functionality. However, the team has encountered a glitch and delayed the release, which is expected within approximately two weeks. Notably, AOL's Webmail team has published an open letter to Google, which, although intended to be humorous, has been perceived as unprofessional. Activating this feature in your Gmail account settings enables you to send an SMS as soon as you start typing a phone number into the search box. New phone numbers entered will be saved in your contact list, and when contacts go offline, the chat window will offer the option to switch to SMS. The first text message sent will appear on the recipient's phone with a number from the 406 area code. Google has provided thousands of these numbers for Gmail users, and once a number is associated with your account, all subsequent text messages will come from that number. This number is bidirectional, meaning the recipient can reply to you via text message, and they can save the number in their phone as yours, even initiating new chats with you. Although we have not yet had the opportunity to test this feature ourselves, it is featured on Google's 'What's new in Gmail Labs' page, available for US phones only. This development is likely a result of Google's acquisition of GrandCentral, which took place in June 2007. No official announcement has been made on the Gmail blog, but we anticipate an announcement and general roll-out to follow soon. (Image credit: monkey_bites)
In the aftermath of the 2016 Rio Olympics, the organizing committee finds itself in a predicament reminiscent of the television game show "Let's Make a Deal." Faced with a staggering debt of 100 million reais (approximately US$32 million), the committee is attempting to settle its obligations with suppliers by offering goods such as air conditioners, portable energy units, and electrical cables instead of cash. This financial predicament stems from the economic crisis that struck Brazil as the preparations for the Olympics were underway. Mario Andrada, the head of communications for Rio 2016, has announced that the committee is negotiating to settle debts for 30 percent less than the original amount. He remains optimistic that the committee will meet its obligations by June 2016, when it is set to disband. However, if the committee fails to meet its obligations, the burden will fall on local and state governments that backed the committee's credit. Both governments are currently grappling with their own financial troubles, and it remains uncertain whether they can cover the Olympic debts. The state government, teetering on the brink of bankruptcy, is already struggling to pay public servants. Andrada expressed confidence that an agreement will be reached and that the committee will honor its commitments. He also mentioned that the committee is still awaiting payments from sponsors. Brazil's economic crisis coincided with the country's largest corruption scandal, resulting in the trial and conviction of several prominent business and political leaders. Among those implicated are heads of construction companies that built projects related to the Olympics, which cost approximately $20 billion. Sergio Cabral, Rio's governor at the time the bid was won, is also among those charged. Andrada hinted that some of the furniture from the Athletes Village, including mattresses and blankets, may have been sent to a local prison for former police officers. He jokingly suggested that Cabral, who is currently incarcerated, may be sleeping on an Olympic mattress. The severe national recession put the Olympics in financial jeopardy even before the games began. Plans for the opening ceremony, hospitality infrastructure, and other non-essential elements were scaled down, and last-minute emergency public funds were sought to stage the Paralympics.

This extension, posted on November 7, 2014, enhances the functionality of the mwomercs.com statistics pages. It introduces various features such as sortable stat columns, filtering mechs by ownership, weight class, Clan/IS, and weapon type. As of the 5/19/2015 release, the MadStats menu has been relocated to its own central icon in the top bar. When debug mode is activated, hidden features are revealed, although they are still being refined due to ongoing bugs. This mode provides control over the default experience while allowing for testing. Due to the instability of the column filters and download button, they currently require debug mode to be enabled. The profile page undergoes display modifications, replacing the scrolling box with a grid of mechs featuring a transparent background. This is an experimental change that could potentially evolve into a custom mech display with stat and smurfy integration. If you encounter any issues or have questions about the filters or functionality, feel free to use the code as you wish. However, contributions that could enhance the user experience for others are greatly appreciated. Collaboration on other possibilities is also welcome. PGI web developers are invited to incorporate these features into the official stats site. I am open to assisting in this process. This text was last edited by MadLibrarian on April 20, 2018. The extension uses the Tablesorter jQuery plugin and employs the Black Ice theme for table styles. At present, only the Chrome version is available. Icons used in this extension are credited to Sparks Murphey and Tarogato. Lastly, new data for new mechs has been updated, as indicated by "(Through hellfire)".

He emphasized that every country has individuals who commit crimes, and these individuals should be fought and prosecuted accordingly. Regarding the election, Peña Nieto expressed confidence that both candidates, Hillary Clinton and Trump, would aim to create beneficial conditions and improve the well-being of their respective citizens. He concluded by expressing his intention to establish a positive and constructive relationship between Mexico and the future U.S. president.

The high cost of healthcare in the United States is a well-known issue, but is it truly as dire as it seems? Indeed, a graphical representation by National Geographic provides an effective summary of the three key aspects of the problem: cost, outcomes, and accessibility. For those unfamiliar with such graphs, a brief explanation is necessary. On the left side, various countries are arranged along an axis indicating annual per capita healthcare spending. To the right is the average life expectancy. Consequently, the lines connecting these two axes demonstrate a country's healthcare expenditure and the health of its population. Ideally, one aims for an upward slope, indicating improved health outcomes with increased spending. However, a downward slope suggests poor results for the money spent. Regrettably, the United States does not appear on this chart due to its excessive healthcare costs. Moreover, the graphic addresses the issue of healthcare access. The line thickness represents the frequency at which residents seek medical attention. Countries such as Japan and the Czech Republic seem to offer easy access, while the United States lags behind in this regard.

While it may seem that community connection isn't crucial as long as one has relationships elsewhere, such as online, Kim and his team's study took a unique approach by controlling for individual-level social connectedness. They also accounted for factors like optimism, age, race, income, marital status, education, mental health, and health risks like diabetes, obesity, and high blood pressure. However, Kim cautioned that this is merely a correlation and causation wasn't fully isolated. I inquired about the importance of community involvement, to which Kim responded ambiguously, stating that there wasn't enough evidence to definitively say so. Yet, he suggested that the potential benefits could outweigh the harm. For instance, a neighborly conversation could lead to checking on each other's health, sharing health-related information, and providing mutual support, all of which might contribute to heart health. Kim further explained that this could be due to the "eyes on the street" principle, a term coined by sociologist Jane Jacobs, which suggests that people watching out for each other can help protect one another. As a psychologist, Kim also emphasized the role of emotional support in buffering against the harmful effects of stress. The field of psychology has traditionally focused on dysfunction. However, positive psychologists like Kim, who emerged with Martin Seligman's 2002 bestseller Authentic Happiness, focus on the benefits of positive dispositions, such as optimism and a sense of purpose in life. Kim's research specifically examines the impact of positive dispositions on health, finding that increased optimism may be associated with a reduced risk of heart failure and stroke.
Prime Minister Narendra Modi was recently criticized by Congress Vice President Rahul Gandhi, who admitted to making an error in a tweet about the rise in prices of essential commodities. In his initial tweet, Gandhi shared a table showing the increase in prices of items such as gas cylinders, lentils, tomatoes, onions, milk, and diesel. However, the figures in the table were incorrect, with percentage increases inflated by 100 points. For instance, the table indicated that the price of lentils had risen from 45 rupees per kilo to 80 rupees per kilo, implying a 77% increase. In reality, the table shared by Gandhi showed a 177% increase. The original tweet was subsequently removed and replaced with a corrected version.

Prior to the implementation of environmental protection laws and regulations, the United States witnessed rampant deforestation, depletion of wildlife populations, and the dumping of toxic waste into water sources. This section offers a glimpse into the state of the U.S. before such measures were enforced. Before the inception of the U.S. Environmental Protection Agency, the Cuyahoga River in Cleveland, Ohio, experienced numerous fires due to its contamination with oil, sewage, garbage, and industrial waste, causing harm to aquatic life and even igniting on occasion. The most severe fire occurred in 1952, yet waste continued to be disposed of in the river. A fire in 1969 ultimately led to the passage of the Clean Water Act and the establishment of the EPA. One of the objectives of the Clean Water Act is to ensure the safety of American drinking water sources from pollution. This includes provisions that mandate companies to integrate advanced technologies into their production processes, thereby reducing waste. Smog, a harmful air pollution, affects many cities worldwide. Caused by car exhaust, burning coal, and noxious substances, smog can damage lungs and trigger reactions similar to allergies. Recent U.S. regulations, such as those governing factory emissions, aim to minimize air pollution and potentially reduce smog levels. The EPA's Superfund program, initiated in 1980, aims to clean up hazardous sites contaminated with toxic substances like lead and arsenic. In many cases, these harmful chemicals permeated the air or seeped into local groundwater, posing risks to human health and the local ecosystem. One example of a Superfund site is the Berkeley Pit in Montana, where mining waste was dumped into nearby streams and wetlands since the late 1800s, contaminating soil, groundwater, and surface water with heavy metals like aluminum, arsenic, mercury, and lead. The EPA has been working on the site since the late 1980s, but the site still poses risks to human health. Before regulations were enforced, the U.S. did not have restrictions on logging, leading to widespread clear-cutting of forests. Laws such as the National Forest Management Act of 1976 helped curb excessive timber harvesting.
In Toronto, authorities apprehended a man from Brampton in relation to a TD Bank robbery on Sunday that left two individuals injured by gunfire. Toronto police staff inspector Mike Earl revealed that forensic evidence at the crime scene led them to one of the two suspects linked to the bank heist. The police are still seeking the shooter, who wounded a teller and fired at a customer. Security footage shows the suspects, one brandishing a handgun and the other jumping over the counter at a TD bank branch on St. Clair Avenue near Runnymede Road around noon on Sunday. As the second suspect jumped back over the counter, he was tackled by a customer, and the first suspect shot at the customer, striking a 22-year-old teller in her thigh. Following the altercation, the 54-year-old customer pursued the suspects into the parking lot, where he was shot in the abdomen. The teller is expected to recover, while the customer is currently hospitalized, undergoing surgery to remove his spleen, part of his pancreas, and part of a kidney. Earl advises individuals in similar situations to refrain from intervening and instead cooperate. "If someone is demanding your money or your watch, cooperate with them, because we don't want people getting hurt," he said. However, Earl cautions this advice does not apply to the suspect armed with a firearm. "He brought a loaded firearm to a bank robbery and was clearly prepared to use it." Bank employees, according to Earl, receive training to cooperate for the safety of everyone in the bank. "They're trained to cooperate with the robber because the money isn't what we're after," he said. "What we're concerned about is public safety and employee safety." Researchers at the University of Texas at Austin's Cockrell School of Engineering have made a breakthrough in battery technology, potentially leading to cheaper, lighter, and more efficient lithium-ion batteries. They have discovered a new family of anode materials, named Interdigitated Eutectic Alloy (IdEA) anodes, which could double the charge capacity of lithium-ion battery anodes. The IdEA anode production process is simplified, requiring only two steps compared to the multiple steps traditionally used for mass-producing lithium-ion battery anodes. This new process results in a foil material that is one-quarter the thickness and half the weight of the graphite and copper anodes commonly used in lithium-ion batteries today. This means that smaller, lighter rechargeable batteries could be produced in the future. Arumugam Manthiram, a professor and the director of the Texas Materials Institute, led the research team. He stated, "Our results show that the material succeeds very well on the performance metrics needed to make a commercially viable advance in lithium-ion batteries." Previous attempts to improve lithium-ion battery electrodes have focused on building new nanomaterials atom by atom. However, Manthiram's team developed a new class of anode materials by mechanically rolling eutectic metal alloys into nanostructured metal foils. The traditional anode for mass-produced rechargeable lithium-ion batteries is a graphite powder coated on a copper foil. The copper adds bulk without improving the battery's power, and the anode manufacturing process is laborious and fastidious. The IdEA anode manufacturing process omits the complicated slurry coating process, significantly simplifying production. Karl Kreder, the lead author on the study and a postdoctoral fellow, realized that a micrometer-scale alloy anode could be transformed into a nanomaterial using traditional metallurgical alloying processes. He explained, "The eutectic microstructure forms naturally because of thermodynamics, then you can reduce the microstructure by rolling it, which is an extraordinarily cheap step to convert a microstructure into a nanostructure." The resulting anodes occupy significantly less space, addressing a critical barrier to commercial
In photographs, one cannot directly manipulate the lighting and backdrop, but one can influence other aspects to a degree. It's widely believed that the color blue tends to flatter people in photos or on screen, making it a suitable choice for significant events. This principle may also extend to hues similar to blue, such as green or purple. However, this doesn't imply that colors like yellow or red are inherently unattractive; rather, they can be more challenging to pull off effectively. The success of these colors largely depends on an individual's skin tone, and wearing overly similar shades can potentially diminish one's appearance in a photo. The angle of one's face is another crucial factor. Whether to slightly turn the head, tilt the chin, or maintain a direct gaze at the camera is a matter of personal preference and the photographer's advice. Ultimately, the person behind the camera is best equipped to guide you on the most flattering angles for each specific photo, assuming they possess an aesthetic sense. In the case of social media photos, such as those on Facebook, one need not overthink this too much. Instead, analyze your appearance in various photos to determine the angles that work best for you, and apply these insights to future shots. With these tips in mind, men and women alike should find themselves better prepared to appear photogenic in photographs.

Henkel, a German consumer products company, announced on Friday that it will acquire U.S. laundry and home care company, The Sun Products Corp, from Vestar Capital Partners for $3.6 billion, including debt. This deal will add brands such as All, Sun, and Snuggle to Henkel's portfolio, making it the second-largest laundry care maker in North America, behind Procter & Gamble and ahead of Church & Dwight. Berenberg analysts believe that Henkel can significantly boost the margins of the Sun brands with its innovation expertise, providing additional profit beyond synergies. Shares in Henkel were 0.6% lower at 1045 GMT, despite being the top performers on the DAX index, which fell 7.1% due to Britain's decision to leave the European Union. The acquisition of Sun Products, with annual sales of approximately 1.4 billion euros in the U.S. and Canada, will increase the proportion of sales generated by Henkel's laundry and home care division in North America to about a third, up from 13%. Berenberg expects the acquisition to add about 6% to Henkel’s operating profit in 2017, rising to 17% by 2019 due to revenue synergies. Christian Weiz, an analyst at Baader Bank, values Sun Products at about 2.3 times sales, which he finds very attractive, reaffirming his "buy" recommendation on Henkel’s stock. Sun Products employs around 2,000 people at two production sites and one research and development center in the U.S. Perella Weinberg Partners and Credit Suisse served as financial advisors to Henkel, while Cleary Gottlieb Steen & Hamilton LLP acted as legal advisor. The acquisition will be fully debt-financed and is underwritten by Deutsche Bank, JP Morgan, and BNP Paribas.
NVIDIA has announced native support for 2 and 3-way SLI on Intel X58-based motherboards, without the need for any nForce 200 chips. This isn't a simple process, as NVIDIA has implemented a certification program to ensure compatibility and generate additional revenue. Any motherboard manufacturer can submit their X58 board for certification, which will be conducted by NVIDIA. If the board passes and the manufacturer agrees to pay a certification fee (the amount remains undisclosed), the board will be certified, and NVIDIA will provide the manufacturer with a key to place in the BIOS. When installing NVIDIA drivers, they check for the presence of this key in the BIOS. If found, SLI support is enabled natively on X58. This support is exclusive to X58 for Nehalem owners this fall and won't work with any other Intel chipsets. This development is significant as it allows for both CrossFire and SLI support on the right motherboard, without resorting to an OEM system or more exotic solutions like Skulltrail. The following are the supported configurations: - Two or three graphics cards can be used with X58/SLI (a pair of GX2s is possible, but four individual cards in SLI is not). - 3-way SLI + 1 card PhysX acceleration is also supported. - For the highest bandwidth possible, three PCIe x16 slots are only supported using nForce 200 chips; otherwise, you're limited to two x16 slots or one x16 and two x8 slots. The nForce 200 route seems unnecessary due to added cost and power consumption, but it remains an option.
In Formula 1, a common query revolves around the distribution of earnings among teams. The total amount is based on the EBITDA (Earnings Before Interest, Taxes, Depreciation, and Amortization) of the Formula 1 group, but the exact inclusions and exclusions are not always clear. However, the general distribution of funds can be understood. Ferrari receives 5% of the total earnings directly, while 2.5% goes to the teams and another 2.5% to the commercial rights holder (CRH). This distribution is justified due to Ferrari's status as the longest-standing team. The prize fund, which makes up the remaining portion, is divided into two smaller funds, known as Columns. Column 1 is evenly distributed among all qualifying teams, which must have been in the top 10 for at least two of the three previous seasons. Column 2 is distributed based on performance, with the World Champions receiving 19% of the fund. The remaining teams receive the following percentages: 16%, 13%, 11%, 10%, 9%, 7%, 6%, 5%, and 4%. Additional bonus schemes are in place, with the most significant being the Constructor Champions’ Bonus (CCB) scheme. This scheme rewards the three teams with the most race wins in the previous four seasons. As of 2013, 2014, 2015, and 2016, this translates to $37 million for Mercedes, $33 million for Red Bull, and $30 million for Ferrari. This means Mercedes receives $685,000 per win, Red Bull $1,830,000 per win, and Ferrari a staggering $6 million per win. If a team wins two consecutive Constructors’ Championships, they receive a one-off annual payment of $30 million, a benefit that has aided Mercedes in recent seasons, having won three championships to date. When all payments are considered, it is evident that Ferrari receives a substantial portion of the sport's earnings. Adding in sponsorship, merchandising, licensing, and other related expenses, it becomes clear that Ferrari's investment in Formula 1 is minimal, if any. Therefore, the notion

Kang stated that as the conflict entered its fifth year, extreme violence and brutality persisted, with both sides attacking populated areas with explosives. She highlighted that the Syrian government continues to employ barrel bombs in airstrikes, resulting in the death of nearly 100 people and wounding dozens in Damascus between January 21 and 26. However, she also noted that armed opposition groups and terrorist organizations continue to use explosive weapons in populated areas in Damascus, launching 50 rockets and mortar shells on January 25, killing seven people and injuring at least 50 others. Kang emphasized that hospitals, schools, and infrastructure facilities are still under deliberate and indiscriminate attack, with eight attacks against medical facilities documented in December 2014 by governmental forces. She also pointed out that the Al-Nusra Front has cut off the water supply to the city of Idlib, affecting more than 60,000 people, while the Syrian regime has prevented the arrival of humanitarian aid to opposition-controlled areas. Kang called attention to the atrocities committed by ISIS elements against civilians in Syria, stating that the ongoing violence and destruction have led to one of the worst displacements of people the world has seen in decades. Colorado's Rapids president, Tim Hinchey, aims to reduce the number of MLS teams without a shirt sponsor from three to at least two by the commencement of the next season. He considers securing a shirt sponsor a top priority, viewing it as a significant milestone in the franchise's overall development. Hinchey expressed that he initially believed the process would be easier than it has proven to be, but remains optimistic about finding a suitable partner. He mentioned that the challenge lies in the substantial investment required, typically amounting to at least $2.6 million annually for a minimum of three years. To secure such a deal, the involvement of top-tier executives from large Colorado-based companies is necessary. Despite the absence of a shirt sponsor, the Rapids experienced considerable progress both on and off the field in 2013. Attendances increased for the fourth consecutive year, season ticket renewals have reached an all-time high, and they signed their first Designated Player, Gabriel Torres, in August. Hinchey emphasized that securing a shirt sponsor is the club's next logical step forward, and its absence is a persistent issue he is eager to resolve. He revealed that the club is currently in discussions with multiple potential sponsors and has recently presented their proposals. It's worth noting that the San Jose Earthquakes and Houston Dynamo also played without a jersey sponsor in 2013, but unlike the Rapids, both teams have secured deals in past seasons. The Australian National Symbols Officer has recently penned a letter to Juice Media, creators of Rap News and Honest Government Adverts, alleging that their use of Australia's coat of arms contravenes several Australian laws. This accusation is puzzling given that Juice Media's content is undeniably satire, and no reasonable viewer would mistake it for official material. In fact, the coat of arms displayed in the Honest Government Adverts series is incorrectly spelled, reading "Australien" instead of "Australian." It is regrettable that the Australian government struggles to differentiate between parody and impersonation. This is particularly concerning as the government has proposed legislation imposing jail terms for the impersonation of a government agency. While some anti-impersonation laws can be justified (such as those combating telephone scams involving fraudulent tax officials), the proposed Australian legislation lacks necessary safeguards. For instance, a 2-year sentence for impersonating a government agency does not necessitate intent to deceive or prove any resulting harm. Consequently, the law could potentially encompass actions beyond the fraudulent intent underlying the bill. The proposed legislation does contain an exemption for conduct undertaken solely for satirical, academic, or artistic purposes. However, critics argue that this provision grants the government the power to censor satire it deems unacceptable. Additionally, the requirement that conduct be "solely" for satirical purposes could stifle free speech. For example, would a video produced for satirical purposes lose its protection if it was also created to generate advertising revenue? Misunderstanding satire is not exclusive to Australia. In 2005, a lawyer representing President Bush sent a letter to The Onion, claiming that the satirical website violated the law through its use of the presidential seal. The Onion retorted that it was "inconceivable" that anyone would perceive its use of the seal as anything but parody. Thankfully, the White House chose not to pursue the matter further, likely avoiding a First Amendment lawsuit. Australia, however, lacks a First Amendment (or even a written bill of rights), prompting civil libertarians to express concern that the proposed anti-impersonation law could be used to suppress political commentary. We urge the Australian government to either abandon the bill or amend it to incorporate both a requirement of intent

The following day, he accused the woman, whose real name is Lisa Cadeau, of theft. The report states that Zickuhr then physically attacked Cadeau, punching her in the face and threatening to kill her if she didn't return the money. He proceeded to bind Cadeau using backpack straps, pour cold water on her, and lock her in a closet. Zickuhr demanded that she provide him with the telephone number of someone who could bring the money. Cadeau provided the number of a Las Vegas police officer, at which point she reportedly pleaded, "He's going to kill me," before the call disconnected due to her screaming. Fearing that neighbors alerted by the commotion would contact the police, Zickuhr allegedly forced Cadeau to jump out the window. The police report further states that he took Cadeau to the Eureka Casino near the Las Vegas strip, believing he would receive the money. However, he instead encountered two police officers and was arrested. Cadeau could not be reached for comment, and the History Channel declined to comment on the incident. Zickuhr's attorney did not respond to requests for comment. Zickuhr was released on bond late last year and is currently out of police custody, awaiting a preliminary hearing in early May.

"A K Shukla, the chief conservator of forests and chief wildlife warden, announced plans to enhance existing forest areas and expand green cover in new areas. The Delhi government aims to boost the city's forest coverage from 20.08% to 25% over the next five years, requiring approximately six to seven hectares of additional green cover in the polluted city. In April, a meeting will be held among greening agencies from various government departments, municipal bodies, and the Centre, such as the Airports Authority of India, the three municipal corporations of Delhi, New Delhi Municipal Council, Public Works Department, and the Delhi Development Authority, to discuss an action plan. The Department of Forests and Wildlife is considering earmarking about six to eight meters on both sides of upcoming elevated road projects for a green belt. When the right of way is granted for signal-free elevated road projects, the horticulture department will be responsible for ensuring dense planting on both sides of these roads. The government is also considering planting trees over drains like those in Najafgarh and Shahdara, as well as in empty plots under the DDA. Shukla stated that the 42 forests in the city will be developed by constructing pathways and installing solar lights. A model will be created, and third parties, such as mohalla sabhas or eco-task forces comprising school students, will be invited to evaluate it. Upon searching for her pets, she encountered an Albuquerque Police Officer who informed her that someone had reported shooting at her dogs. Federal Judge Affirms Navajo Nation's Right to Pursue Lawsuit Against Urban Outfitters FARMINGTON – A federal court judge has affirmed that the Navajo Nation can proceed with its lawsuit against Urban Outfitters Inc., as outlined under the Indian Arts and Crafts Act. The tribe initiated this legal action in the U.S. District Court of New Mexico against the retail company in February 2012, alleging trademark infringements, unfair competition, and violations of the arts and crafts act. The lawsuit followed Urban Outfitters' sale of items such as clothing, jewelry, and accessories labeled as "Navajo" on their website and in stores. The company removed these products in October 2011 after receiving a cease-and-desist letter from the tribe. On December 21, U.S. District Judge Bruce D. Black determined that the Navajo Nation has the necessary standing to continue its claims under the Indian Arts and Crafts Act, as it has suffered an "injury in fact," according to court documents. Urban Outfitters had contested the tribe's standing, arguing that it could not prove an "injury in fact." Black's decision followed a series of summary judgments filed by both parties in late 2014. He denied both summary judgments in his 10-page opinion and order. Enacted by Congress in 1935, the Indian Arts and Crafts Act aims to safeguard the cultural property of Native Americans. The original legislation established the Indian Arts and Crafts Board within the U.S. Department of the Interior, mandating it to promote and protect Indian arts and crafts, and to create trademarks to shield such items. A 1990 amendment granted tribes the authority to bring lawsuits against any person or entity selling a product that falsely suggests it is Indian-produced, an Indian product, or the product of a specific Indian or Indian tribe or arts and crafts organization. In the Navajo Nation's 2012 complaint, it was stated that the tribe registered "Navajo" as a trademark in connection with the sale of goods and services as early as 1943. At the time of the complaint's filing, the tribe had registered 86 trademarks that included

The significance of facilitating the operation of personal Bitcoin full nodes is paramount. This ease of self-verification could potentially lead to a vast number of nodes worldwide in the future. This self-reliance, in turn, mirrors the sentiments of Thomas Jefferson and Woodrow Wilson, who emphasized that liberty and freedom originate from the collective will of the people, rather than institutions or corporate actions. I find it implausible that a few dozen companies auditing the blockchain would ensure its integrity to the same extent as individual audits. Bitcoin's primary purpose is to empower individuals financially, a control that is most crucial when it conflicts with state or corporate interests. The question arises as to why web companies support internet censorship in China, or why the banking system restricts certain legal transactions. These actions are not defensible, as no limited number of companies can withstand state pressure effectively, let alone it being in their best interest. Running an individual node may currently be challenging, with tasks taking hours or days, and this difficulty is likely to increase as Bitcoin grows. However, fostering a culture of individual responsibility is essential for Bitcoin's success. While not everyone needs to run a full node, there should be a substantial number of individuals who do, and the barriers to doing so should be minimal. The blockchain's and Bitcoin's freedom cannot be safeguarded merely by promises from a few companies. Rather, it is the collective action of countless individuals that ensures this freedom. This does not mean the block size can never be increased; rather, it suggests that we should prioritize caution and the preservation of this fundamental property, which is Bitcoin's unique contribution to the world, over the potential success of a Bitcoin startup competing with PayPal.
The Ledger Wallet, led by CEO Eric Larchevêque, is renowned as one of the most secure Bitcoin wallets available. This is evidenced by Larchevêque's personal storage of approximately 1,000 bitcoins, equivalent to around $450,000 as of today, within his wallet. This demonstrates the wallet's robust security. I had the opportunity to interview him on our stage at CES. The initial product from Ledger Wallet was a USB-like key, which could be unlocked using a PIN code. In the event of loss, your bitcoins remain safe, as a private key is required to send these bitcoins. Even if you lose the device, you can recover your wallet and transfer your bitcoins to a new one. In essence, Ledger Wallet enhances the number of factors required to access your bitcoins, including a physical element. Even if your computer is compromised, hackers cannot access your bitcoins, as the most critical part of the code is executed directly from the wallet. At the event, Ledger Wallet unveiled a new wallet, the Ledger Blue. This wallet boasts a touch screen, supports USB, Bluetooth, and NFC, and employs the same mechanisms as the company's previous wallet. During the interview, I asked Larchevêque about the current climate surrounding Bitcoin. He remains optimistic, although he believes it may not achieve the level of ubiquity that was previously anticipated. Given his substantial personal ownership of bitcoins, his sentiments likely reflect his genuine convictions.
The 100 Days Campaign of 1815, marking the finale of the Napoleonic Wars, saw Napoleon Bonaparte's last-ditch effort to retain his title as Emperor of France. His return from exile on Elba, to a disillusioned France under King Louis XVIII, was met with a force of 600 guardsmen, whom he confronted in Grenoble. Facing the 5th Regiment, Napoleon declared, "Soldiers of the 5th. You can shoot your emperor if you dare." Unmoved, they did not. As he marched towards Paris, his troops swelled with veterans and regular soldiers, prompting a notice in the Place Vendome: "From Napoleon to Louis XVIII. My good brother - there is no need to send any more troops - I have enough." On March 19, the Bourbons fled to Belgium, and the following day, Napoleon took control of the government and prepared for the impending Allied military onslaught. Two months after his return, he commanded an army of 280,000 men, with another 140,000 on the way. Despite this formidable force, it was outnumbered by the Allied armies, totaling nearly a million men. Initially, only England's Duke of Wellington (110,000 men) and Prussia's Field Marshal Blucher (120,000) were close enough to threaten France. In an attempt to divide and conquer, Napoleon launched an invasion of Belgium with 125,000 men, aiming to separate Wellington and Blucher's armies and defeat them individually. This strategic move proved successful, and he assigned Marshal Ney to delay the Anglo-Allied force.

Trustworthy news at your fingertips? Subscribe to our complimentary newsletters. This morning, as I perused my Los Angeles Times, the business section's headline caught my eye: "Steep decline in unemployment rate sparks controversy among Obama critics." The assertion, initially tweeted by Jack Welch, ignited a fervor among certain factions, escalating to the front page of the Times. The influence these entities hold in shaping the news agenda is truly remarkable. However, there may be an unacknowledged irony at play. Although the Bureau of Labor Statistics (BLS) did not manipulate the unemployment data, it's indisputable that the headline figure, derived from a telephone survey of households, can be somewhat volatile from month to month. The employment figure for September showed a significant increase, which could be genuine or it could be a statistical outlier. Another possibility exists: In a scarcely noted part of yesterday's report, BLS revealed that it had underestimated job figures by 386,000 from April 2011 to March 2012. It's conceivable that this undercounting has persisted since then, as Karl Smith speculates. If so, then not only is the September number accurate, but it may be compensating for an undercount over the past six months. The shaded area under the red line in the chart below, which is a simple trend line extending from the revised March 2012 figure to September, supports this theory. It indicates that the September employment number aligns with what one would expect if the economy were continuing a gradual but steady recovery, a plausible assumption. Here's the irony: If BLS has indeed been underestimating job figures, it means that the employment situation appeared more dismal during the first half of the year, a period that inflicted the most damage on President Obama. This implies that the critics might not only be mistaken, but they could be completely wrong-footed. It's possible that instead of being biased in Obama's favor, the BLS numbers have been disadvantageous to him. The September spike rectified this, but perhaps too late to offer significant benefit.

A French court has recently upheld a previous ruling, finding Monsanto guilty of chemical poisoning. The judgment, delivered by an appeal court in Lyon, confirms a 2012 decision where Monsanto was held accountable for the chemical poisoning of a French farmer, Paul Francois. Francois claims he developed neurological problems after inhaling Monsanto's Lasso weedkiller in 2004, and argues that the company failed to provide adequate warnings on the product label. The court has ordered Monsanto to offer full compensation to Francois. However, a lawyer for the U.S. bio-tech company has stated that they will continue to appeal the decision. Monsanto has released a statement, claiming that experts have not found a causal link between the alleged exposure to Lasso and the damages for which Francois is seeking compensation. In other news, Monsanto is facing pressure to exit the markets in Greece and Latvia, following similar moves from Germany and Scotland. The two countries have opted out of growing Monsanto's MON810 GM Maize, the only genetically modified crop currently allowed within the EU. This trend raises concerns about the potential impact of the controversial TPP arrangement, which, if passed, could allow corporations like Monsanto to force their products into the market, despite legislation designed to prevent such moves. A proposed bill in Congress aimed at aiding homeowners impacted by the mortgage crisis has garnered substantial bipartisan support, despite a potential veto from the White House. However, the free-market advocacy group FreedomWorks has brought attention to an unrelated provision included in the Senate version of the bill: a requirement for credit card companies and electronic payment processors, such as PayPal, to submit annual aggregate transaction reports to the IRS detailing payments to individual merchants who exceed $10,000 and conduct more than 200 transactions per year. This provision, introduced without debate as a means to offset the costs of the housing bailout, is projected to generate approximately $9.8 billion in revenue over a decade by enhancing tax compliance and encouraging accurate income reporting by merchants. During a hearing before the House Small Business Committee earlier this year, Committee Chair Nydia Velásquez expressed concerns that such reporting requirements pose significant technical and financial challenges for banks and entrepreneurs alike. She argued that the projections of tax compliance gains were based on the misconception that electronic payments equate to profits, when in reality, electronic transactions bear little correlation to actual income for most small businesses, especially when chargebacks, merchant discounts, and other fees are taken into account. As a result, compliant entrepreneurs could face costly IRS audits. Small business associations opposed to the requirements have pointed out instances where businesses received deposits via credit card that did not represent true income. They also worry that the IRS may use the data to target businesses with an unusual number of electronic or credit card transfers for their specific industry. Privacy groups, such as the Center for Democracy and Technology, have their own reservations. David Sohn, a representative from the center, testified that the reporting requirements would compel transaction middlemen to retain information like tax ID numbers, which for many small businesses would be the owner's Social Security Number, that these firms would otherwise discard. He also expressed concern that an aggregate reporting requirement could easily evolve into a demand for more detailed data. The bill is anticipated to return to the House for a simple up-or-down vote next week. According to Ari Schwartz from the Center for Democracy and Technology, this is poor legislative process, as it means the reporting measure is unlikely to receive much careful consideration. Hackers are targeting vulnerabilities in the PHP web application development platform, according to the latest hacker intelligence report from security firm Imperva. This practice aligns with the established trend of hackers focusing on commonly used third-party components to maximize their return on investment. PHP, an alternative to Microsoft's Active Server Page (ASP) technology, is primarily used on Linux web servers. Amichai Shulman, CTO at Imperva, stated, "Since compromised hosts can be used as botnet slaves to attack other servers, exploits against PHP applications can impact the overall security and well-being of the entire web. The consequences of these attacks can be significant, as the PHP platform powers over 80% of all websites, including Facebook and Wikipedia. It is evident that the security community needs to address this issue more thoroughly."

These individuals, who found themselves incarcerated at some point in their lives, are housed in a specific pod with the goal of transforming their lives. The workouts are led by James Lancaster and Joc Crawford, who believe that this program offers more than just physical fitness. Lancaster explains, "Many of these men have never been held accountable. They've never been shown that they can take a different path. Our aim is to establish a method to teach them to guide others as well." Both Lancaster and Crawford, who are Memphis natives and high school acquaintances, have found success in their lives. They recently reunited and decided to use their shared passion for fitness to make a positive impact in their city. They visit the jail once a week to conduct CrossFit workouts. For Crawford, who had his own brush with trouble during his youth, this opportunity to work with the young men is deeply personal. He notes, "Inside these walls, you have individuals involved in gangs and familiar with gang leaders. Once they leave here, they can tell their former associates, 'I'm no longer part of that lifestyle.'" The inmates appreciate the effort made by Crawford and Lancaster. One inmate shared with WREG's Shay Arthur, "Their presence here gives us hope. We realize we can change our lives too." Crawford and Lancaster aspire for the positive change they are instigating within 201 Poplar to extend beyond its walls. They hope their story will inspire others in the community to use their talents to assist others in need within the city as well.

Economist Ben Stein criticized the opposition to the Keystone XL pipeline on Fox News on Saturday, labeling it a psychological issue rather than a policy concern. Speaking with Neil Cavuto, Stein claimed, "These protests aren't about policy at all. They're about seeking attention, providing purpose, and feeling morally superior. A University of British Columbia undergraduate geography student, Iain Marjoribanks, asserts that Airbnb significantly influences Vancouver's rental housing market. His research, conducted with guidance from the B.C. Non-Profit Housing Association, reveals that approximately 77% of Airbnb's revenues originate from hosts who do not appear to reside in the properties they list on Airbnb, which Marjoribanks terms as commercial hosts. The top 10% of hosts, or "mega hosts," generate about 27% of Airbnb's revenue and manage three or more listings. These hosts either operate a single house as a hotel or rent multiple properties across the city. However, Airbnb disagrees with Marjoribanks' conclusions. Aaron Zifkin, the country manager of Airbnb in Canada, stated in April that the majority of Airbnb listings worldwide are in hosts' primary residences, and these are individuals who occasionally rent out their homes or a room. Marjoribanks' research suggests that only 47% of Airbnb hosts reside in their listed properties. If Airbnb were to cease operations in Vancouver, the rental vacancy rate could potentially double from 0.8% to as high as 2%. Regulating Airbnb poses challenges, according to Marjoribanks. Cities like San Francisco and Portland have attempted to regulate the number of days a property can be rented for short-term stays and require Airbnb hosts to register their rental properties. However, both cities have low compliance rates, with San Francisco at 9.5% and Portland at 11%. This is due to Airbnb's policy of protecting hosts' identities, making it difficult to identify and penalize non-compliant hosts. Marjoribanks proposes that cities or the province should impose fines on Airbnb for violations, and the company would presumably pass these fines on to non-compliant hosts. He suggests that if a host removes a full house from the market for an entire year, they should be held accountable for the societal costs that result. Australia and China will finalize a free trade agreement in Canberra today, marking the culmination of over a decade of negotiations. Trade Minister Andrew Robb and Chinese Commerce Minister Gao Hucheng will officially sign the deal, which aims to eliminate tariff barriers for Australian businesses. Peter Arkell, chairman of the Australian Chamber of Commerce in Shanghai, expressed his enthusiasm, stating, "This is a momentous event that's happened. The negotiations have been landmark. I hope this agreement will encourage many Australian businesses that may have been hesitant about entering China, due to perceived barriers, to now feel confident in doing business here." Currently, Australian businesses face tariffs of up to 40% on goods exported to China. The free trade agreement is expected to boost Australian agriculture, manufacturing, and tourism, among other sectors, according to the Australia China Business Council (ACBC). The ACBC also highlighted that the agreement comes at a strategic time, as China's economy shifts towards consumption-driven growth. John Brumby, ACBC president and former Victorian premier, noted, "China's economic rebalancing is generating greater demand for consumer goods, premium products, and professional services. Australian goods and services are recognized for their high quality, and the China-Australia Free Trade Agreement (ChAFTA) will help reduce barriers for Australian companies as they compete in an increasingly competitive market." Mr. Brumby added that the agreement would provide Australian businesses with a competitive edge over key competitors such as the US, European Union, and Canada. The ACBC also reported that the benefit to Australian households from trade with China had increased fivefold from $3,400 in 2009 to nearly $17,000 in 2013. Recently, Australia has completed free trade agreements with Japan and South Korea. Topics: international aid and trade, trade, business, economics, and finance, Australia, China, Asia.

In Towcester, England, on March 24, 2014, jockey Jamie Moore was seen jogging around Towcester racecourse. Numerous research studies have linked regular running to numerous health benefits, but a recent study suggests that excessive running may be associated with a shorter lifespan. HealthDay reported the findings on Sunday by Dr. Martin Matsumura, co-director of the Cardiovascular Research Institute at the Lehigh Valley Health Network. The study revealed that both individuals who do not exercise and high-mileage runners have shorter lifespans compared to those who run an average amount. However, the reasons for this discrepancy remain unclear. Dr. Matsumura and his team analyzed data from over 3,800 male and female runners who participated in the Masters Running Study, a web-based study of health and training for runners aged 35 and over. Approximately 70% of the runners reported running more than 20 miles each week, with the average age of high-mileage runners being 42 years. Factors such as heart risk factors, diabetes, high blood pressure, family history of chronic illness, and the use of painkillers and prescription medicines were taken into account, but none of these factors could explain the shorter lifespans associated with high-mileage runners compared to moderate runners. Interestingly, the use of painkillers was more common among average runners. Dr. James O’Keefe, director of preventive cardiology at the Mid-American Heart Institute in Kansas City, suggested that excessive running could still potentially be related to life-shortening effects. He proposed that the "sweet spot" for running might be a slow to moderate pace for a total of about 2.5 hours each week, approximately two to three times per week. Dr. Matsumura noted that the study did not provide definitive answers, and he emphasized that he does not advise against running. However, Dr. O’Keefe suggested that running a marathon should be considered a one-time accomplishment to be crossed off one's bucket list, as the link between lifespan and running mileage is still under investigation.
In the serene English countryside, amidst the festivities of a friend's wedding, an unexpected question was posed to Peter by a priest. "Do you have faith?" The query, seemingly innocuous, caught him off guard. Peter, a former Methodist Christian turned atheist, hesitated before replying, "Yes," and retreated without elaboration. The question, out of place in the festive setting, revealed a religious undercurrent that neither Peter nor I had anticipated. Our religious backgrounds have been complex. Peter, having been raised as a Christian, later renounced his faith and embraced atheism. As for me, I was born a Muslim, a faith that, for a globetrotting, unmarried woman like myself, posed challenges. When a Samoan family invited us to their Catholic church, we hesitated, unsure if our presence would be appropriate. However, Lena, our gracious host, reassured us, stating, "We welcome all people in our church." The prospect of experiencing Samoan culture, coupled with the promise of a free meal, overcame our British reserve, and we accepted the invitation. As the service commenced, I noticed Peter shifting beside me. For me, it was a fascinating cultural experience; for him, it stirred memories of his childhood and the confusion surrounding his faith. Despite the different language, the sentiments echoed those he had encountered in his youth. Later, when he recognized the rhythm of the Lord's Prayer, he silently mouthed along in English and joined in the concluding 'Amen.' I observed the congregation kneel, cross themselves, pray, and sing. At one point, our normally vibrant and self-assured host was seen with tears streaming down her face. This moment served as a reminder that, despite religion's flaws, it offers comfort and solace to a significant portion of the global population. In a world dominated by media, it's easy to believe that religion is the source of the world's troubles, inspiring division and hate. But in that welcoming church, I felt no division and no hate. As I listened to the hymns, my thoughts wandered. If, in a small village in deeply religious Samoa, I could stand alongside people with beliefs different from my own, perhaps one day the rest of the world would follow suit. And then

Microsoft is set to initiate a substantial Patch Tuesday in January 2012, encompassing seven security bulletins that collectively address eight distinct vulnerabilities. Typically, January releases feature only one or two bulletins. The critical bulletin within this batch resolves a remote code execution issue in Media Player. The remaining six bulletins, scheduled for release next Tuesday, address the BEAST SSL issue and various information disclosure bugs, privilege escalation issues, and an update to Microsoft's SEHOP (Structured Exception Handler Overwrite Protection) technology to bolster its defense-in-depth capabilities for legacy applications. The "important" rather than critical status for the BEAST SSL issue is debatable. The BEAST attack targets web servers that support SSLv3/TLSv1 encryption. Microsoft has already provided a workaround, which involves utilizing the non-affected RC4 cipher in SSL installations. Initially, a patch was promised in December, but it was delayed until this month due to testing issues. According to Paul Henry, a security and forensic analyst at Lumension, "Despite all the hype over 'The Beast', attacks have never materialized, and the issue has retained its 'important' classification from Microsoft." Adobe and Oracle have scheduled updates for January 10th and 17th, respectively, promising a busy month for patching. Microsoft's pre-alert can be found here. ®

Elon Musk, CEO of Tesla, announced during an earnings call on Wednesday that the upcoming Model Y electric crossover vehicle will be constructed on a similar architecture to the Model 3, in a bid to accelerate its market release. This decision is a shift from earlier statements where Musk indicated that the all-electric compact SUV would be distinct from any vehicle Tesla has previously produced. Musk explained that his executive team advised him to reconsider this approach to ensure a faster market launch. Originally, Musk had intended to abandon the 12-volt battery architecture used in Tesla's existing vehicles, a move that could significantly reduce electric wiring and simplify production processes. This change would have allowed for increased automation and the introduction of more robots into Tesla's production line. Musk confirmed during the call that this plan remains in place, but the decision to use a shared platform for the Model Y to streamline production was made due to the high costs associated with creating a new vehicle platform, especially for a company like Tesla that operates on narrow profit margins. Like many automakers, Tesla will utilize a single vehicle architecture to assemble the Model Y, sharing components with the Model 3, which is now in production. However, the Model Y will also incorporate some features from other Tesla models, such as the Model X's falcon-wing doors. The Model Y is expected to enter production towards the end of 2019 or early 2020. The Model Y is crucial to Tesla's goal of delivering 1 million cars by 2020. The company recently announced that it shipped 47,000 cars in the first half of 2017.
I'm consistently impressed by the extensive release notes that Unreal Engine provides with each update, as they manage to pack a multitude of features into every release. One feature that caught my attention in the latest release (4.17) is the addition of a spectator camera for VR. This functionality allows for the rendering of a distinct image to the VR headset and a separate image to the screen. However, the documentation for this feature appears to be somewhat scant, with the link provided in the release notes leading to a dead end at the time of writing this post. Despite this, I found it relatively straightforward to implement, so I thought I'd share my findings with you. Here's a simple three-step process for setting up a spectator camera: 1. Create a 2D Scene Capture Component - Consider this as the camera for the spectator. Attach it to the character actor you're already using. 2. Create a Render Target - This will serve as the storage space for the image captured by the 2D Scene Capture Component. 3. Set your spectator screen mode and texture - The 4.17 update introduced improvements for displaying content on the main view-port through the "Set Spectator Screen Mode Node," including options for displaying just one eye and with or without distortion. For our purposes, we simply want to set it to a texture and to retrieve the texture from the render target we created. With these steps, you should now be able to move the 2D Scene Capture Component around and obtain a non-head-mounted view of the gameplay. Please keep in mind that this will have an impact on your frame rate, as you'll now be rendering an additional image each frame. Use this feature with caution. A report, discreetly published on Christmas Eve, reveals that Australia's greenhouse gas emissions rose by approximately 1% in the 2014-2015 fiscal year, compared to the previous one. The Australian government, responsible for the report's release, chose an unconventional timing for its disclosure. This increase in emissions is a concern as the Paris Climate Agreement calls for Australia to reduce emissions by 26% to 28% by 2030. The report highlights increases in electricity generation, stationary energy (excluding electricity), transport, fugitive emissions, and industrial processes and product use. However, there was a significant decrease of 3.8% in emissions from agriculture. Emissions from electricity generation rose 3% in 2014-2015, despite consumer demand remaining stable. Power generation from black coal increased by 1.4%, and brown coal generation rose by 9.7%. Electricity from wind and other renewable sources (excluding small-scale solar) increased by 12.2%, but hydroelectric generation dropped by 30.3%. Electricity generation was the largest source of emissions, accounting for 34% in 2014-2015. Professor Will Steffen from the Climate Council expressed concern about the December figures, stating, "If we're putting more into the atmosphere than the year before, than we're heading in the wrong direction. We've got to drop emissions fast. We've got to get out of fossil fuels very quickly, coal first – there can be no new coalmines anywhere in the world."
