The Puya raimondii, colloquially known as the Queen of the Andes, titanka (Quechua), or Puya de Raimondi (Spanish), is the largest known species of bromeliad, capable of reaching heights of up to 15 meters. Native to the high Andes of Bolivia and Peru, this remarkable plant was first scientifically described by French naturalist Alcide d'Orbigny in 1830, following his encounter with immature, non-flowering plants in the Vacas region of Bolivia at an altitude of 3960 meters. The species was later named Puya raimondii in 1928 by German botanist Hermann Harms, in honor of 19th-century Italian scientist Antonio Raimondi, who had encountered the plant in Peru and initially classified it as Pourretia gigantea. The Queen of the Andes boasts a trunk that can reach 5 meters in height, with a rosette of leaves up to 1.25 meters long, and leaf spines extending up to 1 centimeter. The inflorescence can measure between 4-8 meters tall, with the entire plant potentially reaching 15 meters. A single plant can produce between 8,000 and 20,000 flowers over a 3-month period. Remarkably, this plant's reproductive cycle typically lasts approximately 80 years, though one individual at the University of California Botanical Garden bloomed in August 1986 after just 28 years. P. raimondii is native to the Andes of Bolivia and Peru, typically found between 3000-4800 meters of elevation on shrubby and rocky slopes. Despite its preference for specific site conditions, it has shown resilience, thriving at near sea level in a temperate climate. Puya raimondii is currently classified as an endangered species by the IUCN, with threats to its survival including human-caused fires, climate change, and a decline in genetic diversity.
During a recent interview, German soprano Diana Damrau and Italian tenor Vittorio Grigolo attempted to articulate the onstage chemistry they share. Upon reading their comments, I found myself questioning whether they might be overanalyzing their connection. After all, they only collaborated for the first time last year, portraying the lovers in Massenet's "Manon" at the Metropolitan Opera. Their performances left audiences and critics spellbound by the palpable intensity they exuded. Therefore, their connection is still relatively new. In discussing their instinctive bond, there is a risk of making it self-conscious. However, any fears were unfounded. On New Year's Eve during the Metropolitan Opera's gala, the duo starred in a new production of Gounod's "Roméo et Juliette," where they played Shakespeare's young, tragic lovers. Scene after scene, these captivating and charismatic artists immersed themselves in their characters, inspiring each other to deliver performances brimming with white-hot sensuality and impassioned lyricism. Directed by Bartlett Sher, this was his seventh production for the Met. The staging was essentially traditional, with some surreal elements that appeared somewhat forced. Nonetheless, to whatever extent Mr. Sher influenced the bold performances of his stars and the overall strong cast, he deserves recognition for his contribution.

Every year, the Mountain View Arts Society organizes the Days of Yore festival in Rosebud Park, Didsbury, Alberta. Over two days, this event features numerous historical reenactors engaging in sword fights, cannon firings, and live combat. Visitors can "Travel Through Time" in the reenactment village, where they'll encounter groups like the Sons of Fenrir Vikings, Dragons Own Medieval Combat Group, and many others. The day is filled with battles, music from pipers and fifers, sing-a-longs, and storytelling. The Artisan Alley offers a shopping experience with heritage arts and traditional crafts that align with the festival's theme. This unique event allows you to interact with soldiers from various historical periods, creating a one-of-a-kind immersive experience. You could role-play as a Viking, one of King Arthur's knights, a fur trader with the Hudson's Bay Company, or a commander from one of the World Wars. Alternatively, you could dress up and participate in a game of croquet with Queen Victoria's friends. Guests are welcome to dress up in their favorite period costumes and contribute to the festivities. The event offers free parking, is wheelchair and stroller accessible, and food trucks will be on site. Only service dogs are permitted.
Verizon has been vocal about its pursuit of Voice over LTE (VoLTE) as a modern replacement for conventional circuit-switched voice. As early as 2011, test calls were conducted using the LG Revolution. At that time, the company had announced that the service would become commercially available in 2012, a promise that may still hold true. An analyst from Northland Capital Markets suggests that Verizon has already activated two trial VoLTE markets, with a nationwide rollout planned for 2013. Light Reading notes that this doesn't rule out an initial commercial launch in the current year, as Verizon might opt to deploy the service market by market, aligning with a 2013 nationwide availability that coincides with the carrier's plans to overlay its entire 3G network with LTE the following year. The significance of this technology lies in the fact that LTE is an IP-based technology, meaning that legacy calling services can't be deployed on LTE without reverting to CDMA or GSM. Consequently, carriers can only eliminate 2G and 3G networks and refarm spectrum by adopting VoLTE. Although this transition won't occur immediately, it is inevitable in the long run.

Blind gamers often experience a sense of invisibility, in addition to their visual impairment. For example, when Brandon Cole, a blind gamer, wrote to THQ suggesting modifications to enhance accessibility in their Smackdown series of WWE wrestling games, he received a form letter expressing gratitude for his appreciation of the game's graphics. The invisibility of some characters in EverQuest II further complicates matters for visually impaired gamers. However, one visually impaired gamer, Alexander Stern, has taken a more assertive approach. Last month, Stern filed a lawsuit against Sony, Sony Online Entertainment, and Sony Computer Entertainment America in the United States District Court for the Central District of California. The lawsuit alleges that Sony is violating the Americans with Disabilities Act by neglecting to implement features that would make their games accessible to visually impaired gamers. The Americans with Disabilities Act states that no individual should be discriminated against on the basis of disability in the enjoyment of public accommodations. According to the lawsuit, Sony has disregarded numerous requests for reasonable modifications to make their games more accessible. The lawsuit, which seems to focus on massively multiplayer online titles, requests the inclusion of visual cues to guide gamers with visual processing impairments to their destinations. The lawsuit also highlights how other companies have made their games accessible. For instance, Blizzard Entertainment's World of Warcraft allows the use of third-party mods, leading to the creation of several programs to incorporate accessibility aids in the game. The lawsuit also mentions Pin Interactive's action adventure PC game Terraformers, citing high-contrast 3D graphics modes, an audio compass, and voice-over detailing collected items as features that enhance accessibility. Beyond the denial of entertainment, the lawsuit also claims that Sony's actions have caused financial loss to visually impaired gamers. As Sony operates an official auction site where gamers can sell their in-game items for real money, the lawsuit asserts that Stern's inability to participate in this marketplace is costing him money. "Sony has constructed the products in a way that is inaccessible to plaintiff; maintains the products in this inaccessible form; and has failed to take any action whatsoever to correct these barriers even after being
Microsoft's choice to adopt new AMD chips for its upcoming Xbox console indicates that it may not be compatible with Xbox 360 games, according to a recent report. This unnamed console, tentatively referred to as "Xbox," will reportedly utilize a variant of AMD Jaguar technology and an x86 PC-style architecture, which should make game development more affordable and accessible for developers already acquainted with the standard. However, this shift effectively eliminates backward compatibility with current-generation games, as reported by Bloomberg. With your old Xbox 360 system, you might want to hold on. Sony faces a similar predicament with the PlayStation 4 but has already found a workaround - it can stream older games using its Gaikai technology. For quite some time, we've understood that backward compatibility was not a certainty. Last week, veteran analyst Paul Thurrott disclosed that Microsoft plans to release a budget-friendly $99 (£65) Xbox 360 model concurrently with the new console, suggesting that the new console may not support current-gen games. However, there remains a slim possibility that Microsoft could somehow reintroduce backward compatibility in some form. "Different hardware configurations don't necessarily make backward compatibility simple," Rich Leadbetter, Digital Foundry's visionary of the future, shared with us. "That said, one could argue the same about the transition from Xbox to Xbox 360, where Microsoft made efforts to ensure that a substantial library of older Xbox titles worked reasonably well on the Xbox 360's PowerPC/AMD combination. In fact, some of them even showed improvement, with added anti-aliasing." "Given sufficient time and resources, a similar form of backward compatibility could potentially be introduced on the new console, but the sheer amount of time and effort required to provide flawless compatibility with a multitude of titles, let alone an entire library, makes this rather unlikely." Microsoft is expected to unveil the new Xbox on May 21st, according to multiple sources. The console is rumored to launch in November and carry a price tag of $500, or $300 with some form of subscription.

Today, Slovenia held a referendum on the issue of same-sex marriage and related matters. The purpose of this vote was to determine whether or not to repeal a law passed by parliament, aiming to bring Slovenia in line with more progressive member states of the European Union. The referendum's success was uncertain due to the strict conditions set for it. However, defying expectations, a substantial number of Slovenians participated and managed to repeal the law. Our Slovenian correspondent, Andrej Turjaški, provides this update: The Slovenian people have just experienced a miracle. In the referendum held today (December 20, 2015), they rejected the proposed law that would have granted marriage equality to same-sex couples, allowed them to adopt children, and introduced gender theory in schools, among other things. The voter turnout was slightly over 36%, and 63% of those who voted were against the proposed law. This exceeded the number of votes required for the law to be repealed (20% of all registered voters). Augusto Pinochet - Chile The U.S.-led ousting of President Salvador Allende aimed to curb human rights abuses; however, the result was a 17-year reign of state-sponsored torture and oppression under the dictatorship of Augusto Pinochet, making this foreign policy decision a resounding triumph in failure. 2. El Salvador's Right-Wing Junta In an attempt to counter communist insurgency, U.S. funding supported right-wing paramilitary death squads that perpetrated rapes, massacres, and widespread atrocities, furthering the ideological agenda while also achieving a remarkable feat of failure. 3. The Shiite-Led Government - Iraq The U.S.-established government in Iraq, replacing Saddam Hussein, is struggling to avoid the world record for failure, persistently ceding power and strategic interests to extremist militants despite a substantial $14 billion U.S. investment in post-troop withdrawal stabilization. The U.S. truly knows how to make a significant impact through failure. 4. Manuel Noriega - Panama Once a CIA operative, Noriega became the military dictator of Panama, a role that failed to serve U.S. interests as his regime was marked by extrajudicial killings and drug trafficking on a massive scale. The U.S. eventually withdrew its support and detained Noriega as a prisoner of war, setting a high bar for future failures. 5. The Mujahideen - Afghanistan With the objective of defending American economic interests against Soviet aggression, the Carter and Reagan administrations supported Afghan insurgents throughout the late '70s and early '80s. The result was a devastating decade-long conflict that left over a million Afghans dead and 6 million displaced. The chaos created by this failure ultimately paved the way for the Taliban to rise to power, creating a new set of problems for the U.S. On a scale of 1 to 10, this failure would easily rate a 20. An EPIC failure indeed!

ABC's chief investigative correspondent, Brian Ross, delves into his relentless pursuit to bring down an American airliner. Although these devices failed to detonate, their ability to bypass what was believed to be advanced airport security alarmed authorities. The news of al-wuhayshi's death is significant. This is a setback for the Al Qaeda movement as a whole. Title: The Art of Shin Godzilla: A Comprehensive Exploration of Hideaki Anno's Reimagining of Godzilla The Art of Shin Godzilla serves as a comprehensive art and production book for Hideaki Anno's (of Evangelion acclaim) reinterpretation of the iconic monster, Godzilla. This film, distinct from previous Japanese and American Godzilla films, ranks as my favorite Japanese adaptation thus far. Given the extensive length of the book (560 pages), this review is divided into two parts, with this installment focusing on the book's contents and concept art. Weighing a substantial 3.5 kg, the two-volume book set arrives in a white cardboard exterior box, with the books protected within a robust black cardboard slipcase. Accompanying the books are two promotional flyers, one for the forthcoming Blu-ray release of the film and another for the exceptionally detailed Godzilla figure replica. The cardboard slipcase bears the Japanese title of the film. The two volumes themselves feature the main tome showcasing a striking, towering image of Godzilla, while the second book contains the film's screenplay, primarily of interest to readers fluent in Japanese. Included within the main volume are two foldout posters, one illustrated by Uruta Kenji (see his art book, Future) and the other by Mahiro Maeda, the creature designer for this film. The initial section of the book delves into the concept art and Godzilla creature designs by Mahiro Maeda. The sketches and image boards are meticulously detailed and of exceptional quality, providing a fascinating glimpse into the various iterations of Godzilla's appearance before the final design was chosen. Maeda even experimented with the concept of a self-replicating Godzilla featuring two heads, an idea ultimately rejected by Toho studios. Some of the most intriguing concept art pieces in the book depict humanoid creatures that emerge from Godzilla's tail, a detail that was somewhat obscured in the film's conclusion. It's possible that we may see their appearance in future films. Thus far, I find Mahiro Maeda's concept art pieces to be extraordinary. Stay tuned for part 2 of the review

Scientists have provided evidence that exonerates the black rat, long accused of spreading the bubonic plague, and instead implicate gerbils as the new suspect. In a study published in the Proceedings of the National Academy of Sciences, researchers found that climate data dating back to the 14th century contradicts the widely accepted notion that European plague outbreaks were caused by a reservoir of disease-carrying fleas hosted by the continent's rat population. Nils Christian Stenseth, one of the study's authors, told the BBC that the "Black Death," as the epidemic was known, seemed to be tied to the climate in Asia. Analysis of 15 tree-ring records, which document yearly weather conditions, shows that Europe always experienced plague outbreaks after central Asia had a wet spring followed by a warm summer - conditions unfavorable for black rats but ideal for Asia's gerbil population. It is believed that these rodents, carrying bacteria-ridden fleas, then traveled to Europe via the Silk Road and arrived on the continent a few years later to cause epidemiological havoc. The findings clear European black rats of responsibility for the deaths of more than 100 million people during the "second plague pandemic," which began with the Black Death in the mid-14th century and recurred until the 1800s. The disease's intermittent appearance throughout the centuries can now be explained, as it was not lingering on the continent due to rats carrying it, but rather due to successive waves of the disease arriving from Asia. This is not the first time scientists have challenged a popular understanding of the disease. Last year, researchers examining plague DNA found in 25 14th-century skeletons suggested that the disease may have been airborne rather than distributed via flea bites. Stenseth's team plans to verify their findings by analyzing DNA from a variety of ancient European skeletons. If the samples show significant genetic variation across time, it would indicate that successive outbreaks were caused by newly arrived waves of the disease rather than a resurgence from the continent's rat reservoir. "If we're right, we'll have to rewrite that part of history," Stenseth said. This revelation may also prompt a reconsideration of the

Which cities in Canada struggle most with sleep? Surprisingly, the city with the most sleep-deprived residents may not be what you expect. According to a study published by Sleep-Centre.ca and IPG Mediabrands, an uncomfortable room temperature is the second most common reason Canadians have trouble sleeping at night, as summer's heat and humidity approach. The study found that 62% of Canadians experience some form of sleep problem, with pain being the leading cause (50%) and temperature being the second (31%). Loraine Cordery, insights and marketing manager for the study, commented, "The room-temperature reason is quite eye-opening because it feels like the most easy thing to control, aside from the temperature outdoors." She added, "We definitely hope to repeat the survey, especially if we time them around seasons, as this would provide a better insight." Other causes of sleeplessness included work stress, illness, snoring, and too much caffeine. Common solutions for sleep problems included changing sleeping positions, using the bathroom, turning to screens, and taking medication. The study also ranked the Top 20 most sleepless cities in Canada. Kitchener, Ontario, was identified as the most sleep-deprived city. Saskatoon and Vancouver tied for second worst. Interestingly, Toronto residents were found to be getting the best sleep out of the top 20 sleepless cities. Chris Herlihey, vice-president research at IPG Mediabrands, explained that this could be due to Toronto having a higher number of singles. Cordery noted, "At the top of the list, Kitchener is a tech-savvy community, made up of young families. There are more babies and toddlers." The study also highlighted that sleep deprivation costs companies nearly $75-million each year due to sick days. Cordery emphasized, "This is an issue that can't be ignored. People too easily push aside the fact that they had a bad night's sleep, when really it's so important to get a good night's sleep." The study was conducted by surveying more than 3,000 people across the country in April. Researchers aimed to match the Census of Canada by surveying 1,00
Williams Advanced Engineering, the technological wing of the Williams Formula 1 team, has been intensifying its focus on electric vehicles recently. They have now introduced a lightweight electric vehicle platform. The company is primarily recognized for its contributions to Formula One racing and engineering work for various automobile companies, but in recent years, it has also been associated with the all-electric Formula E. They were responsible for creating the battery packs and held the supply contract for Formula E until McLaren secured the new contract last year. Despite this, Williams Advanced Engineering has continued to develop electric vehicles and raised $125 million to establish an EV battery factory in the UK, where they will manufacture battery packs for Aston Martin's new all-electric RapidE. However, their ambitions extend beyond this. They aim to provide their expertise in building electric vehicles and today, they unveiled a new concept for a lightweight EV platform, named the FW-EVX, to demonstrate their capabilities. The platform showcases several innovations in battery pack design, cooling systems, and lightweight structures. These innovations have been integrated into a single, scalable platform. For example, Williams' engineers have devised a highly automated, nearly waste-free process for creating fiber-reinforced suspension components on the EV platform, resulting in a 40% weight reduction compared to conventional aluminum wishbones. Another innovation showcased is the process of forming high-strength 3D structures from 2D materials, which in this case, has created an exoskeleton for a battery module that also enhances the structural performance of the battery. Paul McNamara, Technical Director of Williams Advanced Engineering, stated, "Efficiency has always been a key focus for Williams, whether in Formula One or our customer projects. These technologies, and our approach to creating a tightly integrated, lightweight chassis and powertrain package, have the potential to significantly boost the competitiveness of the next generation of electric vehicles. By making EVs more appealing to consumers, we can help expedite their adoption and the air quality benefits they bring." Craig Wilson, Managing Director of Williams Advanced Engineering, went so far as to say that this new concept "marks a new direction for Williams’ advanced engineering business." The company understands that there is a transition from internal combustion engines to a fully electric future and aims to facilitate this transition as a supplier.

I haven't encountered a Certificate Authority (CA) that doesn't demand personal information for Domain Validation (DV) certificates. Is this policy enforced by all major browsers and operating systems, which reject CAs that don't require such information? Or is there another reason for the scarcity of privacy-focused CAs? I aim to replace my personal web server's self-signed SSL certificate with one issued by a reputable CA. I comprehend that certain use cases necessitate extensive identity checks, but for my purposes, a basic DV certificate suffices. I am reluctant to disclose personal details, such as my home address and phone number, that are unnecessary for the purpose of end-to-end encryption for personal use. I'm not seeking a CA that unquestioningly accepts a claim of domain ownership. Instead, I require one with stringent domain validation procedures. I simply desire a CA that asks for information only to the extent of proving domain ownership. Why should they need my name or location as long as I can demonstrate ownership of the domain? Are they amassing this information in anticipation of legal action if I misuse the issued certificate? Or is the information collected to comply with government demands for law enforcement or foreign intelligence purposes?

Initially, delving into the intricate workings of the Internet, I was struck by the text-based nature of many of its protocols, such as HTTP and SMTP. At first, this seemed unusual; text is inefficient for machines to interpret, and protocols are meant for them, not humans. A binary system would be more compact and easier for software to handle. However, I soon recognized the brilliance behind this design. When everything is text-based, interaction with a server can be achieved using simple telnet, allowing for easy exploration. This is particularly valuable given that much of the Internet's infrastructure is built on the Robustness Principle. The ability to examine things in this way is crucial for understanding how they function, a vital step towards using them effectively. When we don't comprehend the tools we employ, we are forced to rely on other tools to mask the underlying complexity and simplify things to manageable levels. In doing so, we forfeit the ability to create solutions tailored to the actual problem, rather than the apparent problem concealed by all the abstraction layers. This reflection is prompted by the HTTP 2.0 draft, which needlessly complicates the HTTP protocol to cater to the demands of a select group of influential parties. Instead of attempting to foresee the future through a crystal ball, consider how this principle impacts Web development by looking in a mirror at the present. For instance, take Web-based APIs, my current focus. On one hand, you have REST, a straightforward set of principles that form the backbone of the Web. Used correctly, it possesses the unique ability to be both powerful and incredibly simple to grasp. Compare this to SOAP, which is technically text-based but is exponentially more complex than REST due to its assumption that humans will never need to read or understand it. After two decades in this field, I can only hand-debug a SOAP transaction with a hammer and a straitjacket. I'd even prefer an old-school EDI transaction over SOAP. The unfortunate truth is that many people seem oblivious to this importance. Obscurity and excessive abstraction are two of the most damaging issues plaguing software development; they combine into a form of willful ignorance that leads to the creation of subpar code. Enough is enough.

Throughout your lifetime, people will repeatedly offer advice and guidance, urging you to follow a certain path... a predictable one. They'll encourage you to stay within the boundaries, shun risks, and adhere to traditional norms. Some of this advice is well-meaning, believing that you'll succeed better if you avoid controversy. Others, however, are merely seeking comfort in the familiar, finding solace in knowing they're not the only ones choosing the safe route. The typical plan seems straightforward: excel academically, earn good grades, attend a prestigious university, secure a respectable job, climb the corporate ladder, have children (twice), and upgrade your home every five to ten years. While this path is viable, it's merely one of many possibilities. What if there's another route? What if you decided to drop out of school and embark on a journey across the country? What if you dismissed the importance of grades and instead pursued knowledge in areas that piqued your interest? What if you spent time volunteering in developing countries, encountering individuals untouched by popular culture? What if you experienced every sensation, witnessed every spectacle, confronted your fears, and endured a few bumps along the way? You have one life. Live it as you see fit, but do take a moment to ponder an alternative path. There's a vast difference between the lives you could lead and the mediocre ones most people settle for. Plus, if you should stumble, at least you'll have some compelling tales to share. Ultimately, the choice is yours. I'm not here to dictate life decisions. However, it's worth remembering that within a century, you, along with everyone you cherish, will be nothing more than a memory. The stresses you're enduring now will be long gone. The tide of convention is a formidable force, swallowing all in its path. You may feel powerless against it. But remember, power lies in your decision to resist or embrace it.
Is the Canadian Economy Truly Secure under Finance Minister Joe Oliver's Leadership? Amidst the escalating economic instability and market turbulence in Europe and other regions, Canadian Finance Minister Joe Oliver has cautioned that our nation's economy might be susceptible to these external factors. Despite his confidence in European authorities' ability to address the crisis, Oliver acknowledges the potential negative impact on Canada due to the ongoing instability abroad. He emphasizes the significance of maintaining international trade relationships and admits that Canada's economy would likely suffer when trading partners experience economic crises, such as the one unfolding in Greece. Oliver asserted that Canada will persist in implementing policies aimed at bolstering the Canadian economy. However, the current fiat currency system, as admitted by the Bank of Canada, is detrimental to the citizens and the economy itself, with the Canadian Loonie projected to lose significant purchasing power over time due to this unsustainable policy. If Oliver genuinely aimed to strengthen the Canadian economy, one might expect him to address this reality and work towards reforming the system for its enhancement. When questioned about whether Canada was in a recession, Oliver evaded the question, stating that the second-quarter data had not been released yet. He reiterated the importance of fiscal responsibility, but surprisingly, he did not prioritize addressing the self-destructive nature of Canada's fiat currency policy. This lack of attention to the dangers surrounding our current monetary system, which is debt-based, is the reason behind the ongoing lawsuit between the Bank of Canada and the Committee on Monetary and Economic Reform (COMER). If we are serious about fostering economic strength, introducing currency competition could be a promising starting point, offering more benefits to the citizens and the country. Currency competition would be a more effective method than the current centralized currency, which only perpetuates an inescapable debt environment for the citizens and the nation as a whole. In the year 2010, the Union of Belgian Cities and Provinces (Unia) documented 338 cases of incitement to hatred, discrimination, or violence. This figure increased to 404 in the previous year. Moreover, Unia has seen an escalation in the number of hate crimes, with 84 dossiers in 2015 contrasted with 48 in 2010. However, Unia maintains that this rise in hate dossiers is not attributable to the refugee crisis or the Paris attacks. Els Keytsman of Unia asserts, "It is plausible that people feel more alarmed due to the influx of refugees, but independently, we have observed a concerning trend among Belgians: racist behavior is increasingly perceived as normal or acceptable." The reports also encompass more severe incidents, such as verbal abuse in public, the forcible removal of headscarves worn by women, and increased difficulties faced by the LGBTQ+ community. Despite this, Unia noted a decrease in complaints about discrimination last year, with 1,596 cases compared to 1,670 the year before.

The Malta Electronic Sports Association (MESA) was unveiled this week, the culmination of numerous months of planning and preparation. This new entity provides a regulatory body for Maltese and Gozitan competitive gamers, aiming to elevate the local esports industry within Malta. The launch took place at Montekristo Estates in Luqa, MESA's primary sponsor, and attracted over 80 attendees, ranging from gamers and students to business executives and sports enthusiasts. The event commenced with a sequence of presentations and speeches, among them, the Chairman of SportMalta, Dr Luciano Busuttil, who expressed his intention to collaborate with the Association. The presentations underscored a significant point: esports is larger than many perceive, and it offers a legitimate career path. MESA's president, Mr Nicolai Gauci, announced plans to establish a National League that would motivate local talent to take competitive gaming more seriously and foster a superior quality environment for players and organizers. Additionally, MESA will represent local talent on an international stage and promote Malta as a destination for esports events and major tournaments. Gauci remarked, "MESA came into existence due to the support of Maltese video-gamers who sought a positive change in the local esports scene." This sentiment was echoed as gratitude was extended to the families of these gamers, who are beginning to recognize the potential of this industry. Esports Insider commented, "This week marks the formal announcement from the British Esports Association, and now the emergence of an entirely new association in Malta. As more countries' scenes gain access to such bodies, it should aid in the growth of esports as a professional industry."
Militants launched an attack on a CRPF camp of the 45 battalion, located in Sumbal, Bandipora district, Jammu and Kashmir. Four terrorists were killed in the ensuing encounter with the Central Reserve Police Force (CRPF) and the Jammu and Kashmir Police. The attack occurred around 4:10 am, as the heavily armed militants attempted to enter the camp. They hurled grenades and opened fire, prompting a response from the alert sentries. The encounter concluded within 45 minutes. The first terrorist was killed within the initial minutes of the attack. The remaining terrorists retreated after a heavy exchange of fire, only to be gunned down by the Sumbal Police. A substantial arsenal of weapons and ammunition was recovered, including four AK-47 rifles (one fitted with UBGL), and over a dozen grenades. The identities of the slain militants have yet to be ascertained. According to sources, the four terrorists may have recently infiltrated from an undisclosed location, planning an attack similar to the one at Uri. They were also found to be carrying incendiary material, including three petrol bombs. The terrorists intended to seize control of the camp and set it ablaze, with the goal of causing widespread damage. CRPF IG Zulfikar Hassan praised his forces for successfully thwarting the terror attack. "Our alert jawans, along with the Jammu and Kashmir police, neutralized the terrorists," he said. Chetan Cheeta, a brave CRPF officer who sustained nine bullet wounds in an encounter in Bandipora earlier this year, commanded the battalion that was attacked. Confirming the incident, Jammu and Kashmir DGP SP Vaid stated, "Four terrorists have been killed after they attempted to attack the 45 Battalion CRPF at Sumbal." Recent infiltration attempts have been observed in North Kashmir, following a terror attack on an army convoy in Quazigund. Extra forces have been deployed along the LoC and borders, anticipating potential trouble from Pakistan and an increased threat from Border Action Teams (BATs). In San Diego, the long-awaited full-scale replica of the San Salvador, the ship that Juan Rodriguez Cabrillo navigated into San Diego Bay in 1542, was transported to Marine Group Boat Works in Chula Vista yesterday, in preparation for its launch next month. This maritime marvel, constructed by around 500 volunteers affiliated with the Maritime Museum of San Diego over a span of four years at Spanish Landing Park, adjacent to Lindbergh Field, was originally scheduled to be transferred onto a barge on Sunday afternoon, but the move was postponed due to unfavorable weather conditions. With improved weather today, the move was successfully carried out. "Today marks a significant milestone for the Maritime Museum of San Diego, our dedicated volunteers, generous donors, the San Diego region, and the state of California," stated Dr. Ray Ashley, the CEO of the Maritime Museum of San Diego. "The creation of the San Salvador has been a multi-year project." The San Salvador, which will serve as a floating classroom along the California coastline, mirrors the original vessel in size, weighing 150 tons and measuring 92 feet in length by 24 feet in width. The materials used to construct the San Salvador were sourced from various parts of the world, including Angelique wood from Suriname, Sapele wood from Nigeria, Southern live oak from the U.S. state of Georgia, and Douglas fir from the Pacific Northwest. "Every element of the San Salvador showcases the dedication, from the keel to the deck," commented San Diego Mayor Kevin Faulconer. "We are grateful to the Maritime Museum for their determination in building such a magnificent ship and offering it to the region as an educational opportunity not only for our children, but for every San Diegan and visitor interested in unraveling our origin story." The San Salvador is set to make its public debut over Labor Day weekend, during the museum's Festival of Sail.
Inmates in Georgia are being hailed as heroes after they swiftly intervened when a guard collapsed during a work detail. According to Polk County Sheriff Johnny Moats, the incident occurred on Monday at a job site where the inmates were working under security supervision. The guard, whose identity was not disclosed, suddenly fell unconscious. In response, all six inmates present immediately sprang into action. They promptly dialed 911 using the guard's work phone, removed his gun holster and bulletproof vest to facilitate breathing, and turned him over to ensure his well-being. Inmate Landon Ware described the situation, stating, "He had his face down and was breathing a little hard, so we turned him over to make sure he was okay." The guard is expected to recover, and Sheriff Moats expressed his admiration for the inmates' actions, stating, "They really stepped up in a time of crisis and they showed it. They really care about my officers." As a gesture of gratitude, the guard's family treated the inmates to a free lunch at a local park.

She addressed two common misconceptions: first, that no Indian institution ranks highly on a global scale, and second, that substantial amounts of money are essential for high-quality research. Irani argued that large sums of money do not guarantee better science, using the example of a fusion experiment being conducted in both Orange County with millions of dollars and Bengaluru with just Rs 2 lakh. She encouraged young researchers to focus on quality research with limited resources. CNR Rao, among others, had previously criticized the government for allegedly reducing funding for fundamental research. Irani countered the global ranking of Indian institutions by stating that the ranking system only considers research published in English and not in Indian languages. She announced the development of an Indian ranking system to address this bias, with over 3500 higher education institutions already participating in the Indian ranking framework. Irani also launched a common website for all six IISERs in the country, intended to provide comprehensive information about the institutions, including the subjects offered, faculty, and ongoing research projects. During her speech, Irani remembered Kaustubh Deshpande, an alumnus of IISER-Pune, who had started remedial teaching for underprivileged children in the surrounding areas. She urged students to help one underprivileged child learn English to overcome the language barrier often faced by those from disadvantaged backgrounds. Lastly, Irani mentioned the Global Initiative of Academic Networks (GIAN) launched by the Union ministry of human resource development, which now includes 22 state universities and 400 foreign teachers. She predicted that this year, 1,000 foreign academics would teach in government institutions.
Wholesale marijuana prices have been gradually increasing following a significant drop over the past year. Since 2015, Cannabis Benchmarks has been monitoring the prices of wholesale cannabis and has observed a decrease in the average price per pound from $1,953 to $1,487 in 2016. However, the first quarter average for 2017 has risen to $1,613. According to Jonathan Rubin of Cannabis Benchmarks, the price of wholesale marijuana exhibits a pattern similar to that of a typical commodity, with prices being influenced by supply, which is linked to harvest schedules. The wholesale marijuana market sources its products from three distinct origins with varying harvest times. Indoor growers harvest year-round and can produce four to six harvests, while greenhouse grows typically yield four harvests annually. Outdoor grows, on the other hand, harvest only once a year, usually in the fall, which floods the market with a large supply and pushes prices down. Rubin explains that the spike in prices observed in August is due to the depletion of the outdoor harvest. Outdoor growers tend to sell their entire harvest in the fall to recoup expenses, but then reduce sales and allow prices to rise as they gradually introduce more product to the market. Each year and each state encounter unique challenges, and marijuana prices experienced their most significant decline starting at the beginning of 2016, only to recover by the holiday season. This decline was attributed to increased supplies from new and expanded capacity, improved cultivation techniques, and better supply chain management, which resulted in a decrease of $365 per pound or 19.7%. Prices typically rise during holiday sales and 420 celebrations. The average price in the fourth quarter of 2016 was $1,487, but it increased to $1,613 in the first quarter of 2017, representing a 17.4% decline year-over-year, but a sequential increase. Oregon's market, however, faced its own set of issues, such as a testing bottleneck at the end of 2016 and a spike ahead of the full adult use markets that began in January. Currently, there is no option for marijuana farmers to trade like other commodities to

Vice-Admiral Clive Johnstone revealed this to the U.K. Telegraph, stating that the group's expansion in lawless Libya serves as a grim indication of their sinister intentions. As they gain territory in Libya, they acquire access to the sea and the potential for maritime weaponry, Johnstone explained. The Wall Street Journal Now Offers Subscriptions Through Apple's Newsstand Service. After a period of hesitation, The Wall Street Journal has decided to sell digital subscriptions through Apple's Newsstand service. This move makes the Dow Jones-owned business newspaper one of thousands of magazines and newspapers available for purchase through Apple's iTunes store, albeit with Apple receiving a portion of the sales revenue and controlling the relationship with customers. Notably, the Journal was one of the prominent print publishers yet to offer app access via Apple. Earlier this year, Time Inc., another holdout, also joined the ranks. As a result, Apple will retain 30% of all subscription revenue generated from in-app sales and manage customer billing information, such as credit card numbers and billing addresses. However, the Journal will still be able to sell digital subscriptions, including access to its Apple apps, through its own website. This approach will allow the Journal to retain all revenue and customer data from these sales. Additionally, Apple customers can now easily subscribe to the Wall Street Journal using their existing iTunes account, and they can effortlessly read the paper thanks to Newsstand's automatic background downloads feature for developers. Representatives from both Apple and Dow Jones have remained silent on the matter. Sources have suggested that former Dow Jones president Todd Larsen, who left the company last summer, had opposed this move to sell subscriptions via Newsstand.
In the realm of art and literature, John Vinycomb's work, "Fictitious and Symbolic Creatures," published in 1909, available at sacred-texts.com, discusses the crocodile as a precursor to mythical dragons on page 91. The crocodile, a colossal amphibious reptile, bears a striking resemblance to a giant lizard, adorned with impenetrable, large scales, except for its vulnerable underbelly. These creatures, native to the Nile and Indian rivers, can grow up to 25-30 feet in length. While agile in water, pursuing fish as their primary diet, they pose a threat to dogs, other animals, and humans who venture into the water or linger carelessly on the banks. The crocodile is the Lacerta crocodilus, as classified by Linnæus, derived from the Greek word κροκοδειλος (krokodeilos), of uncertain origin. The alligator, its American counterpart, takes its name from the Spanish El Legarto, meaning 'lizard.' Its Latin form is either Lacertus or Lacerta. According to Miss Millington in "Heraldry in History, Poetry and Romance," the crocodile and dragon were often confused in ancient times, with Philip de Thaun stating in his "Bestiarus" that "crocodille signifie diable en ceste vie." Guillim, an old heraldic writer, adds that dragons are so fiery that they cannot be quenched by water but still seek air for refreshment, as suggested in Jeremiah 14:6. Young, author of "Night Thoughts," in a footnote to his description of the leviathan (crocodile), in his paraphrase of part of the book of Job, notes that "the crocodile, say the naturalists, lying under water, and being there forced to hold its breath, when it emerges, the breath long repressed is hot, and bursts out so violently that it resembles fire and smoke." Despite this, even the most eloquent of poets have employed the same metaphor in their works.
The City of Calgary has successfully overturned a previous acquittal in its appeal against street preacher Artur Pawlowski. The dispute originated from a ticket issued to Pawlowski in April 2007 for using an amplifier to preach in a public park without a permit. Initially, Pawlowski challenged the tickets and was acquitted, with the judge determining that his rights to freedom of religion and expression had been unjustly infringed upon. However, the city contested the ruling, and the earlier acquittal has now been reversed. In his decision, Justice R.J. Hall of the Calgary Court of Queen's Bench stated, "I do not believe the city has misused its authority. It was compelled to reconcile the public's concerns with Mr. Pawlowski's desires." He further added, "The residents of Calgary are entitled to a serene environment, including noise control in city parks." Pawlowski has announced his intention to appeal the ruling, stating, "We believe our freedom of expression is being stripped away, and this infringes upon our liberties, so we will be appealing it." As of yet, a date for Pawlowski's next appeal has not been set.

The solution to speech you find objectionable is more free speech. It's not improper, dishonest, or underhanded to exercise your own right to free speech to contest the speech of others. This is the system functioning as intended. In my state, Oregon, the Mayor of Portland sought to prohibit a group from assembling due to disagreement with their intended speech (which I share). This type of action undermines the constitutional safeguards that are meant to prevent the excessive influence of the government over us all. The government should never be able to mute a citizen for beliefs it dislikes. Citizens, however, possess the power of speech as a response to others' speech. This encompasses civil debates when appropriate and necessary, as well as protest speech. In Idaho, a decade ago, Fred Phelps and his "God Hates [Group]" followers planned to protest a Catholic funeral in Boise. While I can't recall the specific reasons for their interest, their usual tactic involves spewing abusive, hurtful, and hateful language, causing further distress to mourners on one of their most difficult days. The community in Idaho united. Both secular groups and an interfaith coalition of local Christian, Muslim, Jewish, and Buddhist communities organized and created a human barrier around the entire city block surrounding the church. We stood shoulder to shoulder, with our backs turned to the protesters, and protected those attempting to enter for the funeral. On the inside, facing the people entering the church behind our barrier, we displayed signs of love, hope, and messages of support. This is how the First Amendment should be used. It is acceptable for a community to collectively decide, "we do not share your values." It is acceptable to organize in opposition to these views. As for emboldening the protesters, well, the Phelps family abandoned their plans and returned home early.
Ensuring the safety of Canadians and securing our borders are essential duties of the federal government. Any policy that weakens our security checks for asylum seekers is unacceptable. Last Friday, Sun Media columnist Candice Malcolm, citing high-ranking officials in the federal immigration department, revealed that the Trudeau government plans to expedite asylum applications from countries with a high success rate of refugee claims. According to Malcolm's report, this could mean that some claims may be approved without a hearing, through a quicker process, or by a paper-based review. While many asylum seekers from Middle Eastern and African countries, where Canada has historically accepted a large number of refugee claimants, are genuine, some are terrorists, war criminals, and criminals. In response to Malcolm's column, federal officials stated that there will be no changes to "security and criminality screening practices" but some claims will be approved without hearings. These concerns about the screening process are not new. As the Senate Standing Committee on National Security and Defence stated in its June 2015 report, "Vigilance, Accountability and Security at Canada's borders," there are concerns about how immigrants are screened, with few face-to-face interviews being conducted and the application process being seen as a "paper-based exercise." While Conservative leadership candidate Kellie Leitch has been criticized for suggesting face-to-face interviews to screen immigrant and refugee applicants for values incompatible with Canada, former ambassador Martin Collacott told the Senate committee that such interviews are important as they help a Canadian visa officer determine whether an applicant poses a security threat or holds extremist views conflicting with Canadian values. Canada is a compassionate nation, but we cannot afford to be complacent about who we let in. Our decision-making process must be thorough, not careless.
Over the past two decades, globalization, digitalization, and the expansion of the Internet have elevated intellectual property law to a significant role in international policy discussions. Debates about the management, licensing, utilization, and reutilization of intellectual property have become a prevalent part of a broader public discourse that transcends a select group of legal experts. Given the profound impact of intellectual property law on economic, cultural, health, commercial, creative, and intellectual freedom matters, it is unsurprising that there is an increasing body of literature on intellectual property issues. This literature is not limited to legal scholars or practitioners, but extends to individuals from various academic backgrounds. In the spring of 2012, the Centre for Law, Technology, and Society at the University of Ottawa organized a workshop aimed at assembling scholars from diverse disciplines with an interest in intellectual property law. The objective was to foster cross-disciplinary dialogue, encourage collaborative projects, and generate research that examines intellectual property law issues from multiple perspectives. This book compiles the papers produced from that workshop. Paperback and ebook versions of this book can be purchased from IRWIN LAW.

Siegel established a website, BabiesForBernie2016.com, to sell merchandise, with all profits intended for the Sanders campaign. There is also an official Facebook group where Sanders supporters have gathered to share articles and news about their preferred candidate. A C-27A Spartan, the military adaptation of the Aeritalia G222 aircraft, was observed in flight over Howard Air Force Base in Panama. These planes were destroyed by officials from the Defense Logistics Agency, as Afghan military personnel were unable to maintain them. Katherine Peters reported that the Defense Department spent nearly $500 million on 20 planes to equip the Afghan Air Force, only to scrap 16 of them for a mere $32,000. The Defense Logistics Agency destroyed the planes at Kabul International Airport while the Special Inspector General for Afghanistan Reconstruction (SIGAR) was investigating the Defense Department's failed program to provide the Afghans with a fleet of twin-propeller military transport aircraft. The G222 aircraft, manufactured in Italy, proved too challenging for the Afghan military to maintain, leading the Pentagon to terminate the program in March 2013, three months after SIGAR initiated its investigation. By this point, the department had already spent at least $486 million on the aircraft. According to SIGAR, the aircraft flew only 234 hours out of the required 4,500 from January through September 2012. In a letter to Air Force Secretary Deborah James, John Sopko requested all documents related to the decision to scrap the planes, as well as an explanation. Specifically, he inquired about why the planes weren't exported for sale elsewhere and the steps taken to secure a refund. Sopko also sought information about the end use of the scrap metal sold to an Afghan company and the ultimate fate of parts that weren't destroyed, such as engines and brass components. Given the potential for these materials to be used in weapons against U.S. troops in Afghanistan, the answers to these questions could be of great concern to both U.S. and Afghan officials. The remaining four aircraft of the original 20 are currently at Ramstein Air Force Base in Germany. In a separate letter to Defense Secretary Chuck Hagel, Sopko requested advance notice before the remaining planes are moved or destroyed.
A man, David Ball, 32, from Tyseley, Birmingham, has been sentenced to four years in prison for a bizarre incident that occurred in April. Clad only in a bedsheet and Ugg boots, Ball carried out a ram-raiding of a local supermarket, under the influence of alcohol. He stole cigarettes during the incident and led police on a high-speed chase through Warwickshire before his arrest. Ball was found to be more than twice the legal alcohol limit when arrested on April 16th, and initially claimed to have no recollection of the crime, stating he had been asleep in the car. However, upon viewing CCTV footage, he admitted to remembering the incident and pleaded guilty. The court heard that Ball has over 50 convictions for theft dating back to 1990, resulting in several brief stints in jail. The crime occurred after Ball stole his girlfriend Tricia Dowling's Ugg boots and Renault Clio in the middle of the night. The prosecution argued that Ball had "very little recollection" of the night's events. CCTV footage was shown in court, depicting Ball repeatedly ramming a Co-op in Balsall Common in the West Midlands. The sentencing took into account Ball's guilty plea, as well as the fact that his girlfriend was expecting their child. Three years of the sentence were for burglary, and he received an additional 12-month sentence for aggravated vehicle taking. Ball was also disqualified from driving for three years, as he had been driving at 80mph on a road with a 40mph speed limit during the police chase. As he was led from the dock, Ball gave a thumbs-up sign to family and friends who had come to support him.
In the closing week of 2011, several business stories managed to evade the year-end limelight, with Verizon's controversial $2 bill-pay fee being the most notorious flop. However, the issue that may have the most profound impact in 2012 is the heated dispute over the Stop Online Piracy Act (SOPA). Introduced in October by Texas Republican Lamar Smith, this proposed anti-piracy legislation, often referred to by its acronym, aims to tighten web-based restrictions on the duplication and sharing of copyrighted materials. Yet, opinions on SOPA are proving to be more complex than initially perceived. No entity has felt the brunt of SOPA more than Internet domain registrar, Go Daddy. Unlike tech giants like Google and Facebook, who publicly denounced SOPA due to its restrictive nature, Go Daddy supported the bill, sparking a widespread grassroots campaign against the company. A comment thread on Reddit in late December proposed, "GoDaddy supports SOPA, I’m transferring 51 domains & suggesting a move your domain day," a sentiment that swiftly gained traction and spread an anti-Go Daddy message across the Internet. The crux of the controversy lies in the bill's enforcement powers, particularly those granted to the U.S. Department of Justice, which can penalize those who fall under SOPA's definition of copyright infringement. The proposed boycott and anti-Go Daddy sentiment were intense enough to prompt CEO Warren Adelman to retract the company's pro-SOPA stance. In a statement issued on December 23, Adelman declared, "Fighting online piracy is of paramount importance, which is why Go Daddy has been working to revise this legislation—but we can do better. It's essential that all Internet stakeholders collaborate on this. Go Daddy will support it when and if the Internet community supports it." The statement further emphasized: "We are committed to the fight against online piracy. We have been working to help craft revisions to this legislation, but it's clear that we can improve. It's crucial that all Internet stakeholders work together on this issue. Go Daddy will support the legislation when and if the Internet community supports it."

Cleveland, Ohio – NFL coach Hue Jackson is establishing a foundation under his name to combat human trafficking in Cleveland and its vicinity. The formal announcement will take place on July 20 at the Browns' facility in Berea. This is the first time Jackson, who has recently affiliated with Jay Z's Roc Nation, has had a foundation of his own. According to a press release, "The Hue Jackson Foundation aims to empower children, teenagers, and adult victims of Human Trafficking by funding organizations that advocate for and serve as a voice for those who are exploited." Jackson and his wife Michelle, parents of three daughters, created the foundation "for causes close to their hearts" and are "dedicated to supporting non-profit organizations that embolden and offer hope to victims of sexual exploitation and coercion." Ohio has some of the highest reported cases of human trafficking in the country, as per statistics from the National Human Trafficking Resource Center in Washington, D.C. The foundation will concentrate its efforts on increasing awareness, prevention, and healing for victims of this crime. Victims of Human Trafficking are deprived of their autonomy and self-respect by traffickers who employ violence, physical and emotional coercion, fraud, debt bondage, and other means to subjugate their victims and exploit them for sex and labor commerce. These victims can be children, teens, or adults, of any gender, race, or ethnic group. Human Trafficking occurs in cities and suburbs, in rural and urban areas, in low-income and high-income neighborhoods, on the streets and in the suburbs. In addition to Jackson, speakers at the event will include Ohio Attorney General Mike DeWine, Renee Jones of the Renee Jones Empowerment Center, and Major Lurlene-Kay M. Johnson from The Salvation Army.

Making Decisions Regarding Purchases If you watched our latest Volca Vibes episode, you might have been impressed, as we were, by the Retrokits RK002 active MIDI cable and the Volca Sample. The ingenious microprocessor within the Retrokits MIDI cable enables chromatic playback of Volca Sample samples, and even allows for playing all 10 samples via a standard keyboard. This is achieved by processing an incoming MIDI signal from a standard MIDI keyboard in real-time through some clever firmware within the MIDI cable's processor. In our review, we were disheartened to find that the Volca FM did not respond to velocity over MIDI, a significant aspect of the DX FM sound due to its sensitivity to velocity. While you can adjust velocity using the velocity fader and incorporate it into a Motion Sequence, Retrokits has now introduced a new firmware for their cable that addresses this issue by mapping velocity in real-time using their cable. The firmware update is carried out by dumping a .MID file into the cable, followed by editing via Chrome's Web MIDI within the browser. All you need is a MIDI interface connected to the cable. And it works! For further information, please visit RETROKITS. Note: JavaScript is required to view the comments powered by Disqus.
The 'High Five Friday' initiative, which saw police officers greeting students with high-fives as they entered school each Friday, has been suspended in Northampton, Massachusetts. This program, aimed at fostering positive relationships between students and officers, was initiated by the Northampton Police Department in December, following consultation with the school district's superintendent. However, the program has faced criticism from some community members, who expressed concerns about the comfort levels of students, particularly minority students, undocumented children, or those with negative experiences with the police. Following a community meeting, Northampton Police Chief Jody Kasper and School Superintendent Dr. John Provost decided to discontinue the program. In a Facebook post, the department acknowledged the concerns and stated that while they enjoyed interacting with the students, they understood that the program might not be received positively by all members of the community. They emphasized their commitment to ensuring students arrive at school excited and ready to learn. Reactions to the program's cancellation have been mixed. Anisa Schardl, a local resident, expressed concern about students feeling scared of the police officers, suggesting an alternative approach like educational presentations about police work. On the other hand, some Facebook users have expressed pride in the police department's community engagement efforts. It remains uncertain when a replacement program will be introduced, but reports suggest that the police are looking forward to collaborating with the school district on a new initiative.

On Monday, the Center for American Progress held a discussion titled "In Search of Secure Borders," addressing the federal government's efforts to manage illegal immigration. One of the panelists, Arizona State Representative Kyrsten Sinema (D-AZ), a critic of Arizona's new immigration law, spoke with Wonk Room about Governor Jan Brewer's (R-AZ) assertion that most undocumented immigrants crossing into the U.S. are involved in drug trafficking and related criminal activities. Sinema, along with Senator John McCain (R-AZ) and T.J. Bonner of the National Border Patrol Council, has contested Brewer's statements, declaring them false. Sinema explained, "It's just not true." While some may find it advantageous to distort facts or make unsubstantiated accusations in the short term, Sinema believes this practice is unfortunate. In political discourse, she thinks it's beneficial to have diverse opinions and vigorous debates about ideas. However, she emphasized, "We’re not entitled to our own facts." The facts Brewer has presented, both recently and in the past, are, according to Sinema, untrue. When asked why she feels empowered to challenge Brewer's statements while Brewer does not, Sinema responded, "I believe in facts." Furthermore, Sinema asserted that it's not accurate to claim that the majority of undocumented immigrants function as drug mules, nor is it true that most people in jails are undocumented persons. "That doesn't mean that border crime and interior crime isn't a serious problem," Sinema stated. "But I believe that problem is serious enough without making up facts." Brewer has defended her decision to sign SB-1070 by arguing that Arizona is under attack by Mexican drug cartels and undocumented immigrants, and she has frequently criticized the federal government for failing to secure the border. However, SB-1070 only pertains to individuals who have already crossed the border into Arizona and does not address the prevention of undocumented immigrants and drug cartels from entering the state. Focus Features has obtained the rights to 'Won’t You Be My Neighbor?', a documentary directed by Morgan Neville ('20 Feet From Stardom'). This film will bring the beloved character Mister Rogers back to the big screen. Focus Features has secured global distribution rights for 'Won’t You Be My Neighbor?', a film detailing the life and work of Fred Rogers, the creator of Mister Rogers' Neighborhood. The movie, produced by Tremolo Productions, Impact Partners, and PBS's Independent Lens, is set for release on June 8, 2018. 'Won’t You Be My Neighbor?' provides an intimate look into Rogers, a visionary who captivated generations of children with his kindness and boundless creativity. His show, Mister Rogers' Neighborhood, was one of PBS's longest-running series, wrapping up production in 2000 after 31 seasons. Reruns of the series continued on PBS until August 2008. Rogers passed away in 2003 at the age of 74 due to stomach cancer. In a statement, Neville said, "The Fred Rogers I uncovered during the making of this film is both comfortingly familiar and completely surprising. I believe Mister Rogers is the kind of voice we need to hear right now." Neville added, "I am delighted to collaborate with Focus Features in distributing this film, along with my associates at Impact Partners and Independent Lens." Peter Kujawski, Focus chairman, commented, "Morgan manages to steer clear of traditional biographical filmmaking and instead offers a glimpse behind the scenes to show how Fred Rogers tackled the cultural and social issues of the latter half of the 20th century with his unique, forward-thinking, and compassionate wisdom that remains timeless." Kujawski continued, "Mister Rogers inspires us all to strive to be better people, and we are honored to be a part of telling his story today." Produced by Neville, Caryn Capotosto, and Nicholas Ma, 'Won’t You Be My Neighbor?' is a production of Tremolo Productions in association with Impact Partners and Independent Lens/PBS. On June 2nd, 2015, the live webcast of a hearing will be available on the House Judiciary Committee's website. The hearing, scheduled for tomorrow at 2 p.m. ET in room 2141 of the Rayburn House Office Building, will address the state of free speech on America's public college campuses. Greg Lukianoff, President and CEO of the Foundation for Individual Rights in Education (FIRE), will lead the discussion, joined by Wendy Kaminer, attorney and author; Kim Colby, Director of the Christian Legal Society’s Center for Law and Religious Freedom; and Professor Jamie Raskin of American University Washington College of Law. Lukianoff will delve into the concerning practice of public colleges and universities enforcing speech codes that blatantly violate the Constitution. He will also discuss the chilling effect these codes have on students who are increasingly inclined to suppress speech they find objectionable. The testimony will further examine the threats to faculty speech and the ambiguous protections for faculty expression following the Supreme Court's 2006 decision in Garcetti v. Ceballos. This hearing is not the first time Lukianoff has spoken about free speech on campus. Last year, he testified before the United States Commission on Civil Rights regarding the federal government's interpretation of Title IX and its impact on student and faculty expression. In 2003, Lukianoff testified before the U.S. Senate’s Health, Education, Labor, and Pensions Committee about university speech codes and free speech zones and their influence on campus discourse. Lukianoff emphasizes the importance of maintaining free speech on campus, stating, "Free speech on campus is an issue that needs to stay on Congress’s radar. I’m hoping Congress will take meaningful action to protect the First Amendment rights of students and faculty at our nation’s public institutions. FIRE stands ready and willing to work with legislators to ensure campuses remain true marketplaces of ideas." FIRE is a nonprofit educational foundation that unites civil rights and civil liberties leaders, scholars, journalists, and public intellectuals from across the political and ideological spectrum to defend individual rights, freedom of expression, academic freedom, due process, and freedom of conscience at our nation’s colleges and universities. For more information on FIRE's efforts

The Saudi Arabian government has warned that it may liquidate over $750 billion (AUD 975 billion) of American assets, including Treasury securities, should the U.S. Congress pass a bill that could potentially implicate the kingdom in the September 11, 2001 attacks. According to The New York Times, Saudi Foreign Minister Adel al-Jubeir made this statement to U.S. politicians last month, suggesting that these assets could be at risk of being seized by American courts if the bill is enacted. The bill, which was previously approved by the Senate Judiciary Committee, would revoke immunity for foreign governments in lawsuits related to terrorist attacks resulting in the death of an American on U.S. soil. The newspaper, citing administration officials and congressional aides, has reported that these threats have been a topic of significant discussion among politicians and officials from the State Department and the Pentagon in recent weeks. The Obama administration has reportedly been actively lobbying Congress to prevent the passage of this bill. The State Department has maintained its support for the victims of these attacks and their families, stating that it remains committed to bringing those responsible for such acts of terrorism to justice. John Kirby, the State Department spokesman, reiterated this stance, saying, "We stand firmly with the victims of these acts of violence and their loved ones." In a separate development, a U.S. judge dismissed claims against Saudi Arabia by families of the September 11 victims earlier in September, citing the kingdom's sovereign immunity from damage claims by the families and from insurers covering losses sustained by building owners and businesses.
The Trump administration is considering using funds from the United Nations' Green Climate Fund, intended for climate change adaptation in developing nations, to finance the construction of coal-fired power plants instead. According to Bloomberg News, the White House intends to use this fund, to which the U.S. has contributed $1 billion, to support the development of "clean coal" power plants globally. The Green Climate Fund is a collaborative United Nations initiative aimed at channeling funds from wealthier countries to developing nations bracing for the worst effects of climate change. Previously funded projects by the GCF include hydropower projects in the Solomon Islands and Tajikistan, as well as a renewable energy initiative in Egypt. A Trump official informed Bloomberg that future funding would be directed towards "clean coal" and other power plants designed to emit fewer carbon emissions than current facilities. President Trump has often criticized the Paris climate agreement, including the $3 billion commitment the U.S. made to the GCF. Former President Barack Obama was able to contribute $1 billion before leaving office this year, and Trump has stated that the U.S. will no longer make future contributions to the fund. However, the U.S. still retains a seat on the GCF's board due to its previous contributions. The GCF operates on a consensus basis, making it challenging for the U.S. to advance a coal project without support from other nations.

Apart from a few fasteners and carpet, the car is said to be fully intact. It is listed on Craigslist in Rocky Top, Tennessee for $3,500, or in trade for specified vehicles. Many thanks to BaT reader Spike M. for this submission. The car's exterior, although limited in angle, shows no visible cracks in the fiberglass or paint, which might improve with a wash. All trim, wheels, and windows appear to be present. The seats, steering wheel, and some other interior accessories are not visible in the provided images but are claimed to be included. The dashboard, however, seems damaged and may require replacement, along with new carpet. While these compact Lotus vans seem to be plentiful as low-cost projects, the completed work on this one is a significant advantage. At a refined event such as the U.S. Open, one would typically hear supportive comments from mature women with tasteful haircuts and modest attire, not exclamations like "SHUT THE FUCK UP." This woman, whom we'll refer to as Milly, was simply expressing enthusiasm, much like anyone would at a high-stakes sports event. However, she was not watching American football, nor was she donning a team jersey or sipping from a plastic bottle of beer. Instead, she was watching tennis, and her persistent cheers and khaki-clad dance moves were starting to irritate the sophisticated spectators around her. "Leave me alone," Milly complained, feeling agitated. But the hecklers showed no signs of relenting, finding amusement in their teasing. Milly was not one to be silenced, and after repeatedly telling her detractors to "shut the fuck up," a woman finally responded. "We can't see!" Milly turned to face the camera, her expression defiant. "I don't care—you can go over there," she hissed. Unfortunately, Milly's luck seemed to have run out. The final video showed her being escorted from the match by security, two burly men from whom she struggled to free herself. "Taser her," one voice suggested, sparking laughter—though it was unclear whether the comment was intended to be witty or not. "Did you just say 'taser me?' Milly asked. "That's not funny." There was a hint of sadness in Milly's voice as she pulled away from security, reminiscent of a dog trying to avoid a bath. Eventually, she was dragged out of sight. The crowd erupted in cheers, but the irony was not lost on them. With Milly gone, the match would likely feel dull and lifeless. They would come to regret their harsh treatment of her, realizing that despite her annoyances, she had breathed life into a stagnant game. Farewell, Milly. We will miss your spirited presence.
French DJ and producer Tchami is frequently linked to the term "future house," a moniker he casually coined and subsequently found himself consistently labeled with. (Refer to Los Angeles' Wax Motif and "G-house.") Furthermore, certain tracks from his upcoming EP, The After Life, set for release on December 22 via his own label, Confession, exhibit a more forward-thinking approach compared to a retro-influenced one. For instance, the heavy basslines in "Missing You" and "Superlativ" are swung with the precision of kettlebells, while the only vocals are a deeply pitched-down instruction to "Drop that!" However, elsewhere on The After Life, Tchami transcends such genre boundaries, as demonstrated on "Alone," a near piano ballad bolstered by the subdued basslines provided by frequent collaborator of The Weeknd, Illangelo.
