Glide version 0.11.0 introduces several enhancements to facilitate easier management of dependencies and versions. Let's explore some of these new features and their applications. As usual, all modifications are documented in the release notes. Test Imports: Now, Glide resolves test imports for your project. Any test imports not already imported in the 'import' section of the 'glide.yaml' file are added to a 'testImport' section. You can manually manage this section or use a flag during 'glide get' to include the new dependency in the 'testImport' section. Config Wizard: Determining if a dependency has semantic versions or what a version range should look like in a 'glide.yaml' file was a manual process, but not anymore. The configuration wizard, which can be run independently or after 'glide init', assists in figuring out versions and ranges. Everything is optional, allowing you to choose only the parts and steps you require. For a demonstration, refer to the video above, where you'll also notice the 'testImport' section in action. Easier Release Installs: Previously, there were two primary methods to install Glide, in addition to using 'go get' for the latest development version. The options were to download and place the binary where desired or to use Homebrew on Mac. Two new installation options have been added. On the Glide website, there is now a shell script that installs Glide in the directory where your Go binaries are stored (either '$GOPATH/bin' or '$GOBIN'). The script is available on GitHub for reading or creating a pull request. Additionally, a Glide PPA has been established, maintained by Francisco Guimarães. With the PPA, you can now install Glide using the following commands: ``` $ sudo add-apt-repository ppa:masterminds/glide $ sudo apt-get update $ sudo apt-get install glide ``` This is just the beginning of improving the ways you can easily obtain a stable release. Look forward to future versions for further improvements in the release options. Further Additions: Glide 0.11.0 includes 10 additions and 12 changes. Due to space constraints
Prolonged internet usage contributes to the emergence of school burnout, which in turn may result in excessive internet use or digital addiction. The link between digital addiction and school burnout has been established in both comprehensive school and upper secondary school students, as per a longitudinal study funded by the Academy of Finland, titled "The Dark Side of Internet Use." This study, published in the Journal of Youth and Adolescence in May 2016, reveals that excessive internet use can ultimately lead to depression through school burnout. Adolescents are most likely to develop digital addiction when they lose interest in school and become cynical towards it. Promoting enthusiasm for learning is crucial in preventing this issue. The research suggests that the most critical stage for addressing digital addiction and school burnout is around ages 13-15. To support adolescents' mental health and curb excessive internet use, it's essential to boost school engagement, foster students' motivation to learn, and prevent school burnout. Depressive symptoms and school burnout in late adolescence are more common among girls than boys, while boys are more prone to excessive Internet use compared to girls. The study was conducted among Helsinki adolescents aged 12-14 and 16-18. The early adolescents consisted of lower-school 6th graders born in 2000, while the late adolescents were first-year upper secondary school students born in 1997. Over 3,000 Helsinki adolescents from 33 lower schools and 18 upper secondary schools participated in the study. The Academy-funded project is the first longitudinal study exploring the reciprocal associations between excessive internet use, school engagement, school burnout, and depression among adolescents. Today's young people, often referred to as 'digital natives,' are the first generation to grow up with mobile devices and social media. The digital transformation has two aspects. On one hand, the internet offers valuable social experiences that are beneficial for future studies and careers. The pedagogical use of digital technology can also stimulate young people's interest in science and technology. On the other hand, digital addiction can lead to burnout and even depression in adolescents. For more information, please contact: - Professor Katariina Salmela-A
Despite Nevada not anticipated to commence recreational marijuana sales until around mid-2018, State Senator Tick Segerblom aims to introduce legislation in the upcoming session to speed up the process. As reported by CBS affiliate KLAS-TV, Segerblom is drafting a bill to submit at the start of the year, which would grant Nevada's medical-marijuana dispensaries temporary authorization to sell cannabis products to the recreational sector. Although Question 2's passage makes cultivation, possession, and use of marijuana legal across Nevada from January 3, consumers will still need to purchase marijuana from the black market until state officials finalize the regulatory framework for the recreational sector, a process expected to take another year. Segerblom, who recently returned from a fact-finding mission in Portland, proposes that Nevada emulate Oregon's approach by passing legislation that would allow pot consumers early access to legal marijuana through the state's medical-marijuana market. Segerblom believes this would weaken the black market and ensure that Nevada fully reaps the financial benefits of its recently passed ballot initiative. "I think, given our tourist economy, we're looking at close to $100 million in just taxes," Segerblom stated. While several states have legalized marijuana for recreational use, only Oregon has implemented a plan to allow people to purchase legal marijuana before retail sales are ready. This is due to Oregon lawmakers prioritizing policies that discourage consumers from turning to black-market sources for marijuana. If all goes as planned, Nevada's medical-marijuana dispensaries could be authorized to sell marijuana to adult consumers by fall of 2017.

President Donald Trump is set to issue a wide-ranging executive order aimed at rescinding climate-related regulations established by the previous administration, as reported by The Washington Post on Tuesday. The order will direct cabinet members to revise regulations limiting carbon emissions from power plants, lift the ban on federal coal leasing, and alter how climate change is considered in federal decision-making – all key components of the Obama administration's strategy to combat climate change. The administration is under mounting pressure to disclose the order promptly, given that a lawsuit contesting Environmental Protection Agency (EPA) carbon emissions standards is currently in progress. This lawsuit was initiated by conservative attorney generals, among whom is now EPA administrator Scott Pruitt, although he is no longer a plaintiff. The EPA regulation aimed to reduce emissions by one-third by 2030. In a letter to EPA head Scott Pruitt, climate scientists asserted, "Just as there is no escaping gravity when one steps off a cliff, there is no escaping the warming that follows when we add extra carbon dioxide and other greenhouse gases to the atmosphere." Urgent action against climate change is increasingly necessary, as data from the National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration (NOAA) indicates that carbon dioxide levels in the atmosphere are rising at an unprecedented rate. Current carbon dioxide levels stand at 405 parts per million (ppm). The latest readings confirm scientists' prediction from last year that atmospheric CO2 levels would soon surpass the symbolic threshold of 400ppm. The accelerating increase in carbon levels is already causing significant changes to the planet. Recent studies published this week reveal that the Amazon rainforest is experiencing a "downward spiral of drought and deforestation;" the Great Barrier Reef is undergoing its second major bleaching event in two years; extensive sections of Australia's mangrove forests are dying due to lack of water; and dwindling water resources suggest that the Middle East may become uninhabitable for humans within a few decades. Meanwhile, a climate-related late-season blizzard is advancing up the East Coast of the U.S., while global sea ice is melting to record-low levels due to heat waves in the polar regions. President Duterte has given approval for the construction of temporary military facilities, as per the mutual agreement between the United States and the Philippines under the Enhanced Defense Cooperation Agreement (EDCA), Defense Secretary Delfin Lorenzana stated on Tuesday. The EDCA, whose constitutionality was affirmed by the Supreme Court last year, has bolstered the military accord between the two countries, which dates back to the 1951 Mutual Defense Treaty. During a press conference at Malacañang, Lorenzana clarified that President Duterte was misinformed when he alleged that American soldiers were transporting war weapons to Palawan, Pampanga, and Cagayan de Oro City. Lorenzana explained, "I'm not sure where the President obtained his information, but I corrected it. I spoke with him to inform him that, 'Mr. President, there has been no construction yet of EDCA camps.' 'Construction will take place later this year or next year.' Secondly, it's not permitted in our agreement. There will be no ammunition storage or anything that could be utilized for military exercises.'" Lorenzana further stated that the equipment the US military will be bringing in will primarily be used for humanitarian aid and disaster response, such as rubber boats. He added that these resources would be "positioned strategically across the country" to enable US forces to promptly provide assistance in the event of disasters. Lorenzana also disclosed that he had inquired about the President's decision regarding the continuation of the EDCA construction. The President responded, "OK. Let's proceed, but ensure there will be no ammunition stockpiling there."
At the beginning of the year, concerns about a potential trade war between the U.S. and China arose due to President Trump's firm stance on reducing the U.S.'s trade deficit with China. However, these concerns have largely subsided as trade between the two nations has remained stable. Yet, recent developments suggest that a trade dispute may be imminent. According to the Financial Times, the Trump administration has suspended its primary initiative aimed at strengthening economic ties with China, citing the growing trade imbalance and China's reversal of efforts to liberalize its economy. This was disclosed in an interview with David Malpass, a high-ranking economic diplomat within the administration, who serves as the undersecretary for international affairs at the U.S. Treasury Department. Malpass stated that the Comprehensive Economic Dialogue (CED) with China is currently at a standstill and there are no plans to resume negotiations. This decision follows the July dialogue between the two countries, which ended without any significant advancements, as reported by the Financial Times. The strained relationship between the two nations comes at an unusual time, with Trump seeking China's cooperation in pressuring North Korea over its nuclear missile program. Meanwhile, the White House is adopting a more confrontational stance in its economic dealings, including opposing China's bid for recognition as a "market economy" in the World Trade Organization, as reported this morning. Malpass spoke of the CED in the past tense, stating that it was intended to make progress on market liberalization and economic dialogue between the two countries. "China is not moving in a market-oriented direction, so for now, the CED is also stalled," he said during a visit to New York. "There is not a dialogue on restarting the CED. The critical step is for China to change its economic practices to align with global rules and market liberalization techniques." For the time being, without any concrete actions following the latest escalation of the verbal trade war, we do not anticipate a formal response from China beyond the occasional editorial in Global Times. However, should Trump impose tariffs on Chinese imports, that could change, although the extent to which a full-blown trade war between the U.S. and China would impact these surging markets is increasingly questionable.
The largest medical cannabis dispensary in the U.S., previously known as the "marijuana superstore," has successfully concluded a four-year legal battle with federal prosecutors who aimed to close its Oakland and San Jose outlets. Known as Harborside Health Center, this dispensary, which serves over 1,000 individuals daily, was the target of a federal crackdown in 2012. However, the government has now withdrawn its forfeiture action, freeing Harborside from the ongoing conflict between local and federal authorities over medical marijuana. Steve DeAngelo, the executive director of Harborside, celebrated the move as a potential sign of the end of federal marijuana prohibition. California's marijuana initiative has qualified for the ballot, though federal law, enacted in 1970, still classifies marijuana in the same category as heroin, denying it any medicinal value, and prohibiting its prescription under any circumstances. Despite this, Harborside has been praised for its compassionate distribution of medical marijuana to sick patients and its significant contribution to municipal coffers through tax revenue. Opened in 2006, the dispensary, which was featured in the reality series Weed Wars, employs 150 people and, according to DeAngelo, generated $28 million last year, making it the second-largest retail taxpayer in Oakland. Initially, the city of Oakland sued the federal government to keep Harborside open, arguing that it was preferable to regulate and tax the cannabis industry rather than drive it onto the streets. The U.S. Attorney's Office in San Francisco has confirmed the dismissal of the legal action aimed at closing Harborside, but emphasized that it would continue to use its discretion in enforcing the Controlled Substances Act.
Israel, poised to become the world's first cashless society, has proposed a three-phase plan to significantly reduce cash transactions. The plan, overseen by Prime Minister Benjamin Netanyahu's chief of staff, Harel Locker, aims to recoup a significant portion of the 20% of the national budget lost annually due to tax evasion and money laundering. Reuters reported that Locker led a government panel which, on Monday, issued interim recommendations for turning Israel into a cashless society. These recommendations include initially limiting businesses to cash or cash-equivalent transactions of 7,500 shekels (approximately $2,150), down from the current 20,000 shekels, and no more than 5,000 shekels after a year. Private citizens will be permitted cash deals of up to 15,000 shekels. The new rules will also curtail the use of checks. As part of the effort to minimize cash usage, the panel suggested that banks issue debit cards. Currently, banks only issue credit cards, and Locker believes costs will decrease with debit cards as there is no credit involved. Locker expressed optimism that most citizens will adhere to the new rules, as violating them would be a punishable offense and most transactions by ordinary people are less than 5,000 shekels. The committee outlined the following short-term guidelines: - Immediately limit business transactions done in cash or by check to 7,500 shekels. This limit will be reduced to 5,000 shekels one year after legislation. - Limit private transactions done in cash or by check to 15,000 shekels. - Any violation of these limits will be a criminal offense, punishable by a substantial fine. The new law is expected to take effect by the end of 2014.
A long-standing tradition in the White House involves a division of responsibilities between the chief of staff, who oversees administrative matters, and a political adviser, who offers guidance on the political implications of policies. In this regard, Donald Trump's decision to establish two lines of authority under him, with Reince Priebus as chief of staff and Stephen K. Bannon as "chief strategist and senior counselor," is not unprecedented. However, the nature of Bannon's appointment is cause for concern. Bannon is a prominent figure in the alt-right, a far-right fringe group that has been emboldened and mainstreamed by Trump's campaign. Breitbart News, a website Bannon dominates, promotes the alt-right as a middle-class uprising against a corrupt global elite. In reality, the movement is deeply reactionary, rooted in white chauvinism, and has been associated with anti-Semitic sentiments, as evidenced by Breitbart headlines such as "Bill Kristol: Republican Spoiler, Renegade Jew" and articles attacking Anne Applebaum as a "Polish, Jewish, American elitist." Bannon's appointment sends a negative message to those who did not support Trump but have been willing to give him the benefit of the doubt post-election. By elevating a figure perceived as threatening, Trump's response to the call for unity among the disappointed half of the nation has been to antagonize them further. Bannon's extreme ideology and past attempts to instigate rebellions within the Republican Party may even make him unwelcome in establishment circles. The appointment of Priebus is seen as a positive move, as he is expected to steer Trump towards mainstream policies and restrain Bannon. However, Priebus's ability to check Trump's worst impulses remains questionable, given his enabling and apologetic role during the campaign. The strength needed to resist the forces of intolerance is now moving into the White House.
In the upcoming game, Scrolls, developed by Minecraft creator Mojang, players will initially make a payment to access the game. Post this initial purchase, further play will be free, with the option to buy additional scrolls. As per Markus "Notch" Persson, this initial payment grants a lifetime subscription to regular scroll updates, and players can also acquire free scrolls through ranked tournaments and other activities. Notch has referred to Scrolls as having elements of a free-to-play model, but not labeling it as such, stating it's not a "free" game. Scrolls, embroiled in a high-profile trademark dispute with Elder Scrolls maker Bethesda, is a fantasy-based interactive collectible card game. Notch, in a blog post titled "I hate 'free to play'," expressed his skepticism towards the free-to-play trend. He believes the shift towards free-to-play is primarily driven by profit motives, aiming to monetize players and encouraging them to spend more. Notch compared such games to slot machines, expressing concerns about the exploitation of psychological traps and the prioritization of monetization over game quality. Little was known about Scrolls until a making-of documentary was released last week, following a Swedish judge's decision in favor of Mojang in an interim injunction claim by Bethesda. Notch expressed his preference for purchasing games post-purchase, citing customization, extra levels, or subscription costs as acceptable expenditures. However, he emphasized that the enthusiasm for free-to-play is primarily among game developers, not players. Notch concluded by expressing his excitement to play Team Fortress 2 until the release of Dota 2.

South Carolina has recently decided to make it more challenging for towns to establish their own city-owned Internet Service Providers (ISPs) offering speeds of 190Kbps or higher. A bill passed last week aims to hinder such initiatives, sparking criticism that it is an attempt by carriers like AT&T to stifle competition. A similar scenario unfolded in North Carolina, where Time Warner Cable waged a year-long legal battle to shut down a municipal network offering faster speeds than its Road Runner service. Some claim the bill was crafted and lobbied for by ALEC, a conservative think tank, with AT&T being one of its board members. ALEC and others argue that private companies may struggle to compete with locally-funded municipal broadband, which can leverage taxes, and that such solutions may negatively impact free markets and limited government. However, with recent stimulus programs focusing on broadening broadband access, the US still lags behind in total speed and availability. Thus, blocking a potential source of faster internet may not aid in improvement.

The House Republican leadership postponed a vote on Representative Dennis Kucinich's resolution to withdraw U.S. forces from the Libyan bombing campaign due to concerns it might pass. Speaker John Boehner believes that enacting this legislation, which would take effect 15 days after its adoption, could potentially harm the NATO mission to oust Muammar Qaddafi, according to Politico's John Bresnahan and Jonathan Allen. Republican Dan Burton, a co-sponsor of the resolution, is advocating for a direct vote on the measure, much like the vote on raising the debt limit that Republican leaders initiated because they were confident it would fail. Last week, Senate Democrats compelled moderate Republican senators to vote on Representative Paul Ryan's Medicare overhaul proposal for the same purpose. That proposal, too, ultimately failed. The official reason given by GOP leaders for delaying the measure is the need for additional information and consultation from the Obama administration. However, with the Libyan bombing campaign now entering its fourth month and recently extended for another three, a growing bipartisan group of legislators is expressing frustration with the intervention. The House Republican leadership is reportedly considering alternatives to voting on the legislation, such as having the armed services committee draft backup proposals. However, they find themselves in a difficult position, as the Kucinich proposal is considered privileged under House rules, allowing Kucinich to force a floor vote even if both Democratic and Republican leaders are opposed. The resolution matures next week, giving Kucinich the opportunity to call for a vote when Congress reconvenes following the recess. The House Republican leadership will hold a special meeting on Thursday to discuss their next steps, according to the Associated Press. One possible course of action is rescheduling the vote for a later date, presumably when it appears more likely to fail.
House Speaker Paul Ryan, as reported by Politico on Thursday, has communicated to his inner circle his intention to retire from Congress following the 2018 midterm elections. Having served Wisconsin's 1st Congressional District since 1999, Ryan, at 48 years old, is a seasoned Republican representative. In interviews with over 40 lawmakers, congressional and administration aides, conservative thinkers, and Republican lobbyists familiar with Ryan, none expressed the belief that he would continue in his role beyond 2018. When asked about his plans to step down during a press conference on Thursday, Ryan laughed and denied any immediate plans, saying, "I'm not, no." Politico noted that Ryan had grown weary of Washington even before he reluctantly assumed the speakership in 2015. In 2012, Ryan was Mitt Romney's running mate during the Republican presidential campaign. According to the publication, Ryan has discussed his retirement plans with his advisors and has made it clear that he intends to serve until the 2018 midterms and then retire before the new Congress convenes in January 2019. Despite his impending departure, Ryan is expected to focus on entitlement reform in his final legislative push, with tax reform, which appears poised to become law, being his current major focus.

A four-year-old child tragically lost his life following an attack by a group of three pit bulls outside a residence in Felton, Delaware. According to Delaware State Police, the child was playing in the yard while his mother visited with a female friend in the 900 block of Edwardsville Road. The boy's mother, who is several months pregnant, looked out the window and witnessed the dogs attacking her son. As her friend dialed 911, the mother rushed outside to save her child. She sustained multiple bites on her arms during the rescue attempt. Two repairmen, who were working at the home, also attempted to save the child by warding off the dogs with PVC piping. Emergency services tried to revive the child, but he was pronounced dead at the scene. The mother was transported to Kent General Hospital for treatment of her injuries. Authorities have yet to release the child's name, pending notification of family members. "I've never seen anything so horrific," said Capt. Sherri Warburton, head of Delaware Animal Care and Control. The two female dogs and one male, all related and unneutered, were involved in the attack. Warburton speculated that one of the females was pregnant, while the other may have been in heat, which could have incited a pack mentality among the dogs. "It's not advisable to leave a child unattended with such dogs," Warburton warned. The animals were taken away and euthanized by the First State Animal Center and SPCA. As the dogs were not vaccinated, their remains will be tested for rabies. Warburton suspects that the oldest female is the mother of the younger female and the male dog involved in the attack. "Although I can't confirm it, it's likely that interbreeding occurred there," she said. Warburton does not believe the dogs were used for fighting. Animal control officers initially visited the property where the attack occurred on Wednesday morning at approximately 8:30 a.m., following reports of two pit bulls on the loose. Upon arrival, the officers were unable to locate the dogs and no one seemed to be home. After the afternoon attack, officers contacted the individual who had reported the loose dogs and confirmed that they were indeed the same dogs that had escaped earlier in the day.

On a frigid Friday afternoon, approximately a month prior to the White House's inauguration of the 45th president, I found myself at President Lincoln's Cottage, nestled in Washington, D.C. Originally known as the Soldiers' Home, this stucco villa now bears the name of its most prestigious resident, Abraham Lincoln. Perched atop a 250-acre tract that has served as a retirement haven for war veterans since the 1850s, the cottage offers a tranquil and poignant respite from the city's daily politics. Opened to the public since 2008, the cottage stands as a somber yet inspiring testament to Lincoln's leadership, where he penned the initial drafts of the Emancipation Proclamation amidst the ominous crackle of cannon fire. Each morning, the president would depart for his office at the White House, a three-mile journey that offered a stark reminder of the nation's wartime struggle, with wounded soldiers, grave-diggers, and the haunting voices of escaped slaves filling the cityscape. Despite its proximity to my residence, I had only recently become aware of the cottage's existence. Having spent the majority of my life in Texas, I relocated to Washington in 2005 to pen a book about George W. Bush, America's 43rd president. Upon my first visit to the more renowned presidential residence at 1600 Pennsylvania Avenue, I was struck by the West Wing's seemingly historical void.

A tanker belonging to Libya's eastern government, which had been attempting to export oil in defiance of the Western-supported administration in Tripoli, returned to the country on Saturday. The United Nations had blacklisted the tanker, making it impossible for it to be sold or enter any port. The tanker, carrying 650,000 barrels of oil, had hoped to be sold by the eastern government's parallel oil company. However, the UN measure prohibited it from entering any port. Libya has been plagued by two competing governments since 2014, one based in Tripoli and another in the east, both backed by armed factions. The eastern administration established its own National Oil Corporation (NOC) in parallel to the Tripoli-based NOC. A U.N.-backed unity government arrived in Tripoli last month, aiming to replace the rival administrations and assert authority over the entire country. Western powers are concerned that any independent crude oil exports by the eastern NOC could undermine the Tripoli government and further divide the country along regional lines. The NOC Chairman, Mustafa Sanalla, issued a statement warning ship owners and trading companies that oil exports from Libya by any entity other than the National Oil Corporation of Libya are illegal and will be stopped. He also expressed concern that the actions of the individuals behind this attempt could split the country. The Distya Ameya tanker departed from Marsa el-Hariga port late on Monday and was blacklisted by the UN on Wednesday. It then headed to Zawiya port in western Libya. Sanalla stated that the tanker would unload its cargo within a few days, but a source from Zawiya reported that bad weather was preventing the vessel from discharging its crude. The eastern NOC claims legitimacy from the government and parliament based in eastern Libya, which received international recognition after armed opponents took control of Tripoli in 2014 and installed rival institutions there. The new U.N.-backed unity government, which aims to end the conflict, faces resistance from hardliners in both factions, whose rivalries have persisted since the 2011 uprising against Muammar Gaddafi. This accident resulted in an SUV falling approximately 30 feet onto North Nimitz Highway, resulting in the tragic death of the SUV's driver, as reported by the police. Investigators suggested that speed was a contributing factor in the 9:10 p.m. incident, but there was no indication of drug or alcohol involvement. The two men responsible for the crash, aged 65 and 30, both from Waipahu, were allegedly driving at a high speed when they rear-ended a vehicle driven by a 26-year-old Honolulu woman. The driver of the SUV, a 48-year-old man from Aiea, was pronounced dead at the scene. This accident marked Honolulu's 54th traffic fatality of the year, compared to 47 at the same time last year.

The Spirit Lake Tunnel, constructed after Mount St. Helens' 1980 eruption to drain a lake whose natural outlet was blocked, is experiencing an issue. Expert analysis suggests that if the tunnel collapses, Interstate 5 in Washington state could be submerged, as it serves as the lake's primary drainage. The tunnel was bored through bedrock in 1985 to provide a new outlet for Spirit Lake, which had its natural outlet blocked by ash and debris. Recent inspections have revealed that the tunnel floor is rising, with geologists attributing this to shifting rock formations beneath the surface. The tunnel's opening has decreased over the years, from eight feet, six inches in October 2013, to seven feet, one inch by the following year, and further to six feet, eight inches in April 2015. This significant uplift has raised concerns about the tunnel's stability. If the tunnel were to collapse, the lake could overflow, potentially leading to a disaster. A recent report by the U.S. Army Corps of Engineers states that such an event could destroy all transportation routes west of the lake, including Interstate-5 and major North-South rail lines. Despite the concerns, the Army Corps of Engineers believes the tunnel still has some time before it becomes ineffective. However, they are currently working on designs to address the issue and hope to carry out emergency repairs later this year. The cost of the fix has not yet been determined. Three Washington politicians have expressed serious concerns about the issue, stating that a complete failure of the tunnel could have catastrophic effects on Washington state.

A Georgia couple, Kristina Brown and her husband, are constructing a $3.5 million indoor shooting range in Powder Springs. This establishment, known as the Governor's Gun Club, will offer top-notch technology for marksmen and serve alcohol, including Maker's Mark, thanks to a city council-approved alcohol permit. Hart voices her concern about the potential presence of intoxicated individuals in the neighborhood. Georgia law generally allows residents who can legally own firearms to carry them in their homes, vehicles, and places of business, with some exceptions, such as government buildings. In the case of bars and restaurants, gun owners can carry their weapons if the establishment's owner permits it. In response to concerns, Brown clarified that once a customer orders a drink in the lounge, they will not be allowed to enter the firing range. They must present their identification card, and once it is accepted, they cannot re-enter the range that day. Despite this, Brown acknowledges the unique nature of their business model, stating, "Georgia Law allows persons with gun permits to bring their weapon into a restaurant that serves alcohol, we are taking it even a step further."

Comprising nine individuals with expertise in rail systems like the Hong Kong MTR and London Underground, the panel was established in 2013 to bolster SMRT's engineering capabilities. Discussions centered around training more rail professionals and enhancing the rail engineering profession within SMRT. NTU physics professor Alfred Huan, who has chaired the panel since its inception, mentioned this as a key topic. Professor Kristin Wood, co-director of the SUTD-MIT International Design Centre, emphasized the importance of SMRT's ongoing growth in in-house engineering expertise. SMRT Trains currently employs over 400 engineers, representing a 96% increase since 2014. SMRT's chief technology officer, Ng Bor Kiat, stated that nurturing employees to reach their full potential is crucial for SMRT to expand its capacity and ability to manage an extended train network. Professor Wood stressed the need for SMRT to solve problems internally rather than relying on external vendors. National University of Singapore engineering dean Chua Kee Chaing highlighted the necessity of engineers with "deep engineering expertise" in various areas, such as trains, signaling, and power systems, as well as those with "system-wide knowledge" of all aspects of rail engineering. Engineering students from local universities should be encouraged to join rail operators SMRT and SBS Transit, as well as the Land Transport Authority, to ensure knowledge translation has a direct impact on the rail network, suggested SMRT-NTU Smart Urban Rail Corporate Laboratory director See Kye Yak. A previous Hale County administrator, Tricia Galbreath, who alleged she was dismissed in 2013 as part of a purge of white employees, was granted $136,600 by a federal jury this week in a ruling that supported her breach of contract, wrongful termination, and due process claims. Initially, Judge Callie V. S. Granade had dismissed Galbreath's other claims, such as those based on racial and age discrimination. The jury's verdict on Monday awarded Galbreath $8,000 for emotional distress and $128,600 in compensatory damages. Attempts to contact Galbreath's lawyers, the Hale County Commission, and Probate Judge Arthur Crawford were unsuccessful before the publication of this article. Galbreath filed a lawsuit in 2015 against Crawford and the commission, with Crawford also serving as the commission chairman. Crawford, who is African American, was elected Hale County Probate Judge in November 2012 following a write-in campaign, after initially winning the Democratic primary but being removed from the ballot by an Alabama court due to non-compliance with campaign disclosure laws. Following Crawford's election, the county allegedly initiated a systematic purging of white employees, terminating Galbreath, the then-Chief Clerk of the Probate Court, and the then-County Attorney. Each of these employees was replaced by an African-American, with Galbreath's and the then-County Attorney's replacements being younger than them. Galbreath and the then-county attorney were terminated during a commission executive session meeting on June 18, 2013, according to the magistrate judge's ruling. Galbreath was not given any prior notice of her termination or any form of discipline, but was instead called into the meeting under the pretense of discussing performance issues and an 'improvement plan.' The reasons given for her firing included absenteeism, failure to perform duties, and use of foul language, but none of the commissioners had ever raised these issues with Galbreath, nor had anyone acting on their behalf ever indicated that she was not meeting their expectations or failing to perform her duties. Ottawa – Nearly a century after Montreal and Ottawa faced off on the National Hockey League's (NHL) inaugural day, the Canadiens and Senators will commemorate the league's centennial with an outdoor game. The league announced on Friday that the Habs and Senators will take to the ice outdoors on December 16 at TD Place Stadium, the home of the Canadian Football League (CFL) champion Ottawa Redblacks. The Canadiens emerged victorious over the Senators 7-4, on December 19, 1917, when the NHL first began play. Eugene Melnyk, the Senators' owner, stated, "One hundred years ago, our Senators played their first NHL game, helping to establish the greatest professional hockey league in the world. Hockey holds a deep and respected place in the heart of our nation's capital. Our team and our fans are incredibly privileged to host an NHL outdoor game this December, marking the culmination of the league's year-long centennial celebrations." The December 16 game will take place three weeks after the CFL's Grey Cup game is played at TD Place Stadium, with the stadium set to increase its seating capacity – currently at 24,000 – for both events. This will be the Senators' first time hosting an outdoor game, having previously played outdoors in Vancouver in 2014. The Canadiens, on the other hand, will be participating in their fourth regular-season outdoor game. Pierre LeBrun contributed to this report.
Seeking reliable news updates? Sign up for our complimentary newsletters. A significant challenge in prosecuting rapists and sexual assailants across many states lies within the legal system itself. In the United States, 34 states, including Washington D.C., impose statutes of limitations on filing rape or sexual assault charges, with durations ranging from 3 to 30 years. For instance, charges in New Hampshire must be filed within six years of the crime, while Connecticut allows five years. In Minnesota, the limit is three years. Some states link the statute of limitations to reporting deadlines. For example, in Illinois, if a survivor reports within three years, the state has a decade to file charges. If reporting is delayed beyond this period, the case is effectively closed. Twenty-seven states make exceptions or extensions to statutes of limitations when DNA evidence can identify a suspect, but the specifics of these exceptions differ. For instance, Georgia has no time limit for rape cases with a DNA match, while Indiana requires prosecutors to charge a suspect within a year of the DNA match. In Connecticut, the initial crime must be reported within five years for any subsequent DNA match to be considered valid.
In the face of a fourth consecutive decline in American farm income, McMartin Farms (McM Inc), a significant high-value crop farm based 30 miles south of the Canada-U.S border in St. Thomas, has filed for Chapter 7 bankruptcy in the U.S. Bankruptcy Court in Fargo on February 10. McM Inc. was a major player in the sugar beet, potato, and dry bean cultivation industry, employing over 50 full-time staff and 100 seasonal workers. As reported by Mikkel Pates in Agweek magazine, McMartin Farmed approximately 39,000 acres in 2016, with 2,000 acres dedicated to sugar beets and over 4,000 acres to potatoes. This acreage was a decrease from the 59,000 acres farmed in 2012. Speculation about McM's financial health arose last year, prompting Agweek to feature Ron McMartin Jr., the farm's president, in a cover story, where he acknowledged the struggles faced by farmers in the Red River Valley, stating they were "trying to make sense with a very challenging time." The creditors' first meeting is scheduled for March 16 in Grand Forks. While the assumption persists that larger farms equate to greater profitability, the financial viability of a farm seems to extend beyond the number of acres. To my delight, this endeavor has resulted in more than just one movie per week. I recently terminated my Netflix subscription to either borrow films or rediscover those I already own, with the primary intention of supporting my local independent video store, Video Wave, which I have visited more frequently this month than in all of last year. It's a place I adore! Today, I wish to share some thoughts on a somewhat quirky film that I watched during the holidays, courtesy of Roku (I believe it was streaming for free on Amazon with my sister's Amazon Prime membership) — The Long, Long Trailer (1953). My mother is a fan of everything Lucille Ball, so she persuaded me to watch this amusing comedy about Tacy and Nicky (essentially, Lucy and Ricky), who opt to purchase a fashionable trailer instead of a traditional home to save money. The humor is abundant. My takeaways from this film are as follows: 1.) I had forgotten how much I appreciate the comedic chemistry between Lucille Ball and Desi Arnaz. Their partnership is undeniable, and the movie is genuinely funny. 2.) I am eager to acquire every outfit worn by Tacy, thanks to the exceptional costume design by Helen Rose. Rose, who also dressed memorable films like On the Town (1949), Annie Get Your Gun (1950), and Silk Stockings (1957), and won two Oscars for her costumes, is the mastermind behind these stylish ensembles. The Department of Justice (DOJ) has submitted court documents in support of former Maricopa County, Arizona Sheriff Joe Arpaio's petition to overturn his criminal contempt conviction, following his pardon by President Trump. In the filing, DOJ lawyers assert that the case is "moot" due to the presidential pardon, which removes any punitive consequences associated with Arpaio's non-final conviction. The DOJ argues that it would be "just and appropriate" for the conviction to be vacated, given that it was rendered "moot" by the unforeseeable act of a presidential pardon. Trump announced his pardon for Arpaio in a statement in late August, citing Arpaio's dedication to public safety and his long-standing service to the nation. Arpaio, an early backer of Trump's presidential campaign, was found guilty of criminal contempt in July for willfully disregarding a federal judge's order to cease racial profiling. Shortly after his pardon, Arpaio called on U.S. District Judge Susan Bolton to reverse his conviction and launched a campaign to raise funds for his legal defense.
In 2018, China intends to make history by landing the first probe on the moon's dark side, a significant step forward in its space exploration program, as reported by the official Xinhua news agency. This ambitious endeavor comes approximately two years after China's successful "soft landing" on the moon with the Chang'e-3 craft and its Jade Rabbit rover in 2013. While previous spacecraft have observed the far side of the moon, none has landed on it. The upcoming Chang'e-4 probe, similar to its predecessor but capable of carrying a larger payload, will be used to investigate the geological conditions on the moon's far side. According to Liu Jizhong, head of the science, technology, and defense industry administration's lunar exploration center, the craft will also potentially host a radio telescope for astronomers' use. Due to Earth's radio transmissions being unable to reach the moon's far side, this location offers an ideal setting for sensitive instruments. China first announced its intention to land on the moon's dark side in September 2015, aiming to launch a mission before 2020. Setting a launch date as early as 2018 signifies the priority that China's leaders place on advancing their space program, with President Xi Jinping advocating for China to become a space power. China maintains that its space program is for peaceful purposes, but the US Defence Department has expressed concerns about China's increasing space capabilities, citing activities aimed at preventing adversaries from utilizing space-based assets during a crisis. In 2007, China raised concerns about a potential arms race in space when it used a ballistic missile to destroy an orbiting satellite. In a shift from relying solely on state-owned enterprises, China announced in March 2015 that it would open up its lunar exploration program to private companies, with the aim of fostering technological breakthroughs. Xinhua reported that China sent "letters of intent of cooperation" on its latest mission to foreign countries in early 2015, but it remains unclear if any countries have agreed to collaborate.
Three weeks prior to his BBC radio interview, Environment Minister Greg Hunt received detailed information about the impact of climate change on Australia's weather patterns, as revealed by confidential Bureau of Meteorology briefings obtained by Fairfax Media via freedom-of-information laws. These briefings indicate that senior officials had warned Mr. Hunt that the extraordinary heat experienced in Australia during 2013 was "unprecedented." This warning was given before Mr. Hunt downplayed any connection between fires and climate change in his interview with the BBC's Newshour in October of the previous year. The initial briefings provided to Mr. Hunt suggested that recent extreme heat was in line with "a pattern of global warming," while subsequent advice in November stated that climate change had heightened the likelihood of "severe weather conditions favorable for severe bushfires." These documents contradict statements made by Prime Minister Tony Abbott, who last year denied any link between global warming and bushfires. They also underscore the extent to which the government has been informed about climate change's role in Australia's recent extreme weather conditions.
The board of directors of Carlisle United Football Club convened a series of discussions on Sunday, culminating in a late-night meeting with team manager Graham Kavanagh. Regrettably, after a challenging and disheartening start to the season, the decision has been made to part ways with Mr. Kavanagh. Over the past year, under Mr. Kavanagh's leadership, the club underwent significant changes, such as restructuring the youth management, achieving Category 3 in the EPPP process, implementing strength and fitness coaching, and overhauling the first team squad during the summer. However, these efforts and hard work have not translated into improved results on the field. Since Greg Abbott's departure last season, the team has averaged one point per game from 45 league matches, leading to relegation to League 2 in May 2014. The board felt that the team was on a similar downward trajectory this season. Saturday's result at Cambridge served as a turning point for those responsible for the club's administration and management. The board wishes Mr. Kavanagh and his family success in their future endeavors, acknowledging his dedication, perseverance, and coaching abilities. They are confident that his skills will bear fruit in another setting. The search for a new team manager commences immediately. In the interim, club captain Paul Thirlwell and goalkeeping coach Tony Caig have agreed to oversee training sessions and make decisions regarding team selection in the coming days.

The incident took place at the intersection with Victoria Road, causing the closure of Albro Lake Road between Victoria Road and Chapman Street. A call center in Thane, a suburb of Mumbai, is under investigation for defrauding over 6,000 Americans, with the Federal Bureau of Investigation (FBI) involved in the case. FBI officer Suhel Daud, a cybercrime expert of Indian origin, met with Thane's police chief, Param Bir Singh, to collaborate on the investigation. Daud reportedly stated that their work has made a significant impact on a global scam. The call center workers allegedly posed as Internal Revenue Service (IRS) officials and threatened Americans with tax investigations if they didn't pay up. More than 2,000 people worked at the nine Thane call centers, with the alleged mastermind, a 24-year-old named Sagar Thakkar, feared to have fled the country. Thakkar, along with his sister Reema, are wanted for their role in the scam, which may have funded their luxurious lifestyles through car purchases and real estate investments. The scam involved call center workers contacting Americans, claiming that police would soon raid their homes if they didn't pay. Many Americans complied, transferring amounts between $500 and $60,000. The police have arrested 72 workers, and the FBI's assistance is expected to help trace the money trail from the US to Indian accounts. Additional call centers in Noida and Gurgaon may also be investigated as the crackdown continues. The police have already seized hardware during raids in Ahmedabad.

The Obama administration's handling of the Russian hacking incident was lackluster, according to a senior official. In late December, President Obama approved a limited response, which included expelling 35 diplomats, closing two Russian compounds, and imposing narrowly targeted economic sanctions. A covert measure authorizing the planting of cyber weapons in Russia's infrastructure was also approved, but it was still in its planning stages when Obama left office, leaving it for President Trump to decide whether to use. The Obama administration's response was criticized for its lack of urgency, based on the belief that Hillary Clinton would win the election. This failure to act more aggressively is seen as a significant oversight, especially in hindsight. Critics argue that the administration's smug confidence in Clinton's victory led to a lack of proactivity in the investigation, which ultimately resulted in the current situation.

In Springfield, Massachusetts, the Roman Catholic Bishop of Springfield commemorated Gunnery Sgt. Thomas Sullivan, a native of the city who was among the five service members tragically killed by a gunman in Chattanooga, Tennessee on July 16th. Sullivan, aged 40, was remembered as "exemplary" and "a leader with genuine courage" during a private funeral Mass at Holy Cross Church, where he was a childhood parishioner. The Mass was attended by family, friends, active duty Marines, and dignitaries including Governor Charlie Baker, U.S. Senator Elizabeth Warren, and U.S. Representative Richard Neal. As the procession made its way from the funeral home to the church, hundreds of Springfield residents lined the streets, many waving U.S. flags and a bagpiper played the Marine Corps hymn outside the church. Bishop Mitchell Rozanski spoke of Sullivan's deep love for his family, his selfless dedication to his service as a Marine, and his unwavering faith in God. Rozanski highlighted Sullivan's faith, noting that he attended Catholic schools, including Cathedral High School, and received his confirmation at Boston College. The bishop stated, "As a follower of Jesus, Tommy knew the strength of faith that made him an exemplary Marine, a leader, and a man of true courage." Sullivan will be laid to rest in the Massachusetts Veterans Memorial Cemetery in Agawam. Thousands of people paid their respects at a public wake held the previous day.

The incident occurred at their apartment in the 17100 block of East Ohio Place on Thursday. According to an arrest affidavit, Lebron-Rivera stated that he was demonstrating to his wife, Genesis Rodriguez, how to disarm someone when the gun went off, fatally wounding her. Upon the arrival of the police, Lebron-Rivera reportedly admitted to the shooting, saying, "Sir, I killed my wife, it was my fault." Lebron-Rivera explained that his wife was playing with his gun when he got out of the shower and he didn't remember loading the magazine before they began playing with it. After taking the gun from his wife, he claimed that he chambered a round and fired one shot, striking and killing her. The police responded to the apartment complex near East Mississippi Avenue and South Buckley Road around 6 p.m. on Thursday. Upon arrival, they found Rodriguez deceased. Auburn Davis, a spokeswoman for the Air Force at Buckley, confirmed that Lebron-Rivera is an Airman First Class in the 460th Security Forces Squadron. The Air Force is cooperating with the Aurora Police Department and local authorities to gather updates on the investigation. Lebron-Rivera appeared in court on Friday for an advisement on the charges. He was booked on a felony manslaughter charge and is currently being held in the Arapahoe County jail on a $50,000 bail.

Samsung is leveraging the imminent launch of BBM for Android, yet to be officially released, to advertise its Galaxy devices, Samsung App Store, and Messaging Hub in a marketing campaign aimed at the African market. BlackBerry is collaborating with this initiative, as the two companies have agreed to jointly promote the service to African mobile customers. This collaboration hints at BlackBerry's plans for BBM, now that it is expanding access to its proprietary messaging platform. BBM has historically been a significant player in one-to-one mobile communication and has recently introduced BBM Groups, enabling one-to-many broadcasts using familiar messaging tools. In key developing markets such as Indonesia and Africa, BBM has not only facilitated communication but also local commerce and business, serving as a universally reliable, affordable, and potentially trustworthy alternative to SMS. The joint promotional efforts suggest that BlackBerry is not only making its messenger available for iOS and Android users but is also actively promoting this availability, even if it seems to undermine its own interests. Samsung profits from this by offering new users a familiar and trusted means of communication, further incentivizing them to switch from dedicated BlackBerry devices. The benefits for BlackBerry are not immediately clear. Facing a shrinking user base for both devices and services, BlackBerry stands to gain access to a growing market through this deal. While relinquishing the BBM platform advantage may raise questions, it is no longer a significant advantage, as evidenced by the dwindling BlackBerry market share. At this point, expanding availability to iOS and Android devices is of little consequence to the company's dwindling user base. The potential benefits for BlackBerry include securing more users for a platform that could become valuable in terms of data, advertising, and other initiatives like BBM Money. If partnering with competitors helps reach more users and encourages a few platform-jumpers, it is a small price to pay at this stage in the game.

In London, it has been revealed that the true likeness of Mr. Darcy, the enigmatic protagonist from Jane Austen's acclaimed novel "Pride and Prejudice," would bear little resemblance to Colin Firth's portrayal. Instead, the authentic Mr. Darcy would be characterized by a pale complexion, a sharp, pointed chin, a long nose, an oval, beardless face, and powdered white hair. His physique would be somewhat lean, with sloping shoulders, earning him the description of being more akin to a ballet dancer than a traditional heartthrob. As we approach the 200th anniversary of Austen's passing, a new study published on Thursday has provided a less-than-flattering depiction of Fitzwilliam Darcy, the beloved hero of "Pride and Prejudice." This study, authored by John Sutherland, a professor of modern English literature at University College London, and Amanda Vickery, a professor of early modern history at Queen Mary University of London, claims to present the first historically accurate portrait of the fictional character. This revelation may come as a surprise to fans, potentially reshaping their affections for English literature's most sought-after bachelor.
Netflix has introduced the long-awaited feature of offline playback for a selection of films and TV shows. Starting from November 30, 2016, users can download content from Netflix for viewing when they are not connected to the internet. This feature is ideal for airplane journeys, long car rides, or even when stuck in a subway for an extended period. Netflix has initiated the launch of this feature with some of its original content, such as Orange is The New Black, Narcos, and The Crown, available for offline viewing. The updated app shows a vast array of content, both original and first-party, that can be viewed offline, although availability may vary by region. Users can choose from two different quality options when downloading content, depending on whether they prioritize video quality or device storage space. This feature is currently available on Android and iOS smartphones and tablets running iOS 8.0 or Android 4.4.2 or later.

In the recent week, a team member from Substratum, named Nicholas Chum, shared a series of screenshots hinting at a forthcoming feature for the widely-used theme engine. These screenshots displayed the theme engine installed on a custom ROM, complete with a dedicated Customization option within the main Settings menu. The images demonstrated a theme being applied and a fresh theme being successfully compiled without any errors. The significant revelation came from the fourth screenshot, which showed the device, a Nexus 6P running Android 7.1.1 Nougat, was not rooted at all. Given that Substratum typically requires root access to function effectively, this suggests a shift in the application's functionality in an upcoming update. Mr. Chum expressed gratitude towards Ivan Iskandar and Randall Rushing for the commits that enabled this new feature. He clarified that this functionality will not work on stock versions of Android, but it should be compatible with all custom ROMs that have integrated the special masquerade job engine and the new version of Substratum. While some enthusiasts at XDA may not mind rooting their device for theme support, others have refrained from using the application due to the root requirement. Mr. Chum admits they are unsure about the smoothness of the transition from rooted to rootless operation. He mentioned that a statement will be released soon to custom ROM developers who wish to incorporate this new version into their builds. The statement will include instructions on integrating this feature into their custom ROMs, followed by testing, after which they can start releasing their new custom ROMs. If all goes well, the process should be as straightforward as a dirty flash on top of the current custom ROM.
A malfunctioning water pump system in Cibecue, Arizona, has led to a severe water shortage, prompting the White Mountain Apache Tribe to declare an emergency for the town. As per Navajo County, the pumps supplying water to the community have failed, leaving the town with only 5% of its usual water supply. The county is soliciting donations of hand sanitizers and bottled water, which can be dropped off at the Navajo County Board of Supervisors Offices in Holbrook or the Reception Desk in Show Low at 550 N. 9th Place. Similarly, Yavapai County has declared an emergency in Cordes Lake due to the inability of the water system to meet demand despite equipment and wells operating efficiently. The release advises residents to voluntarily cut their water consumption by half to help conserve resources. Water is being transported from Prescott Valley to fill tanks in Cordes Lake, and the town has implemented a system-wide shutdown from 11 p.m. to 3 a.m. each night until the system recovers. A limited supply of bottled water is available at the Mayer Fire Station in Cordes Lakes. This report was published in 2017 by KPNX.

Honeywell Retiree Medical Coverage Under Threat: Lawyers File for Injunction In a recent development, attorneys representing Honeywell retirees have petitioned the U.S. District Court for the Eastern District of Michigan for an injunction to halt the company's decision to terminate medical coverage. This action comes in response to Honeywell's announcement that it will discontinue health coverage for retirees as of June 30, 2017. Previously, David Lymangrover, a retiree from Honeywell, looked forward to his golden years with a pension, supplemental insurance, and prescription coverage. However, his expectations were shattered when he received a letter from Honeywell on April 3, informing him that the company was ending health coverage for retirees due to a reevaluation of its healthcare offerings. The letter from Honeywell states that the Medigap market has matured, enabling Medicare-eligible retirees to find affordable and comprehensive health insurance and prescription drug coverage. Retirees are asked to contact the Honeywell Retirement Service Center for any questions, although a representative confirmed that the company has outsourced question-answering to a call center. Charlotte Lymangrover, David's wife, expressed concern about the impact of this decision on their health coverage, which currently pays for blood pressure medicine and David's inhalers. She noted that they are permanently retired and cannot easily find alternative employment to secure new insurance. The Lymangrovers' health coverage also previously covered the remainder of David's operation costs. Charlotte expressed concern about the potential financial burden, stating, "Cutting (medical and prescription coverage) out now is just detrimental to people’s lives." In 1978, the Supreme Court, in the Bakke case, invalidated racial quotas in higher education. Highlighting a superior method, Justice Lewis Powell referred to the undergraduate admissions policy at Harvard as an "enlightening example." Unlike other elite institutions, Harvard did not set aside specific spots for underprivileged minority candidates. Instead, it took race into account as one of several positive factors in a student's application. Thirty-six years later, Harvard's admissions process is under scrutiny in a federal district court in Boston. The accusers assert that Harvard's admissions policy is a disguised quota system that disadvantages Asian-Americans. This is the most recent legal challenge to affirmative action, and the first to target a private university, masterminded by Edward Blum, an activist determined to overturn Bakke. Among his initiatives, Blum's organization, the Project on Fair Representation, attracts students who believe they have been unfairly denied admission to universities that prioritize racial preferences. The lawsuit against Harvard originates from Students for Fair Admissions (SFFA), a new platform for Blum's crusade. The SFFA boasts a compelling symbol: an unnamed child of Chinese immigrants with top scores on three college entrance exams, who graduated first in their class at a competitive high school, captained the tennis team, and volunteered for National Public Radio. The student was reportedly rejected by Harvard, according to the complaint, because the university aims to cap the number of Asian-Americans on campus. Blum, however, alleges that Harvard's admissions policy is a "facade to conceal, deceive, and confuse racial balancing and quotas." Although Asian-Americans accounted for over 27% of the applicant pool at the three most selective Ivy League colleges from 2008 to 2012, they constituted only 17-20% of the students admitted. According to the SFFA, this disparity represents "intentional discrimination" that violates Title VI of the Civil Rights Act of 1964. Blum expresses optimism about this legal battle. "If the case reaches the Supreme Court," he says, "we will argue that the use of race in college admissions must cease."

The departure of long-time wideout Reggie Wayne, who was let go in free agency, marks a significant change. Although Wayne is still considering a return to the NFL, he will not be rejoining the Colts, leaving a void that will undoubtedly be felt by the team. For the first time since 2001, Reggie Wayne will not be a part of the Indianapolis Colts, and for the first time since 1996, neither Marvin Harrison nor Reggie Wayne will be on the team. T.Y. Hilton, the team's young star receiver, is poised to fill the void on the field. However, in 2015, Hilton will not only be the primary wideout for Andrew Luck's prolific passing offense but will also assume a more substantial leadership role. With the departure of his mentor and close friend, Reggie Wayne, Hilton has no choice but to step into a leadership role. The only wide receivers on the roster with more experience than Hilton are Andre Johnson and Vincent Brown, both of whom were signed during this offseason. Given that Brown is fighting for a roster spot while Hilton is coming off a Pro Bowl season and is undoubtedly the team's number one receiver, he is naturally suited for a leadership role. It appears he intends to embrace it, which bodes well for younger receivers like Donte Moncrief and Duron Carter. Another player set to take on a larger leadership role in 2015 is safety Mike Adams. With the exit of Reggie Wayne and Cory Redding in free agency, Adams recognizes the need for leadership and is eager to contribute. He told Kevin Bowen that he aims to elevate his leadership this year. The departure of leaders like Wayne and Redding will undoubtedly alter the dynamics of the 2015 Colts. However, with emerging leaders like T.Y. Hilton and Mike Adams, a solid core of existing leaders, and the addition of veterans like Andre Johnson and Frank Gore, the Colts do not seem to be lacking in leadership for the upcoming season - a positive development.

Legal action was initiated against these countries earlier this month, and the Commission has threatened to revoke Poland's voting rights if they fail to comply with EU demands. Dimitris Avramopoulos, the EU's migration commissioner, expressed hope that the countries would reconsider their positions, stating, "There is still an opportunity to return to normalcy." Interestingly, the Commission is not pursuing a case against Austria, another country that has declined to accept migrants. This may be due to Austria's status as a net contributor to the EU's budget, while the Czech Republic, Hungary, and Poland are all net recipients. At present, none of the countries appear willing to yield, and their cases may eventually be brought before the European Court of Justice once the relocation scheme concludes. Avramopoulos has indicated that the need for migrant relocation will persist even after the scheme ends, and it remains to be seen which country will ultimately give in...
Hate crimes have once again drawn attention in South Carolina following a tragic incident where a suspected white male, alleged to be the shooter, fatally shot nine individuals at a historically significant black church in Charleston on Wednesday evening. The state, lacking a hate crimes law, has 19 active hate groups, among which are two Ku Klux Klan chapters. A hate crime, as defined by the Hate Crime Statistics Act, is an act motivated by prejudice towards race, gender or gender identity, religion, disability, sexual orientation, or ethnicity. This can encompass various offenses such as murder, forcible rape, aggravated assault, simple assault, intimidation, arson, and property damage or destruction. The federal authorities have announced their intent to investigate the Wednesday attack as a hate crime. Among the 19 active hate groups in South Carolina are white nationalists, Ku Klux Klan, Neo-Nazi, black separatist, neo-confederate, and anti-LGBT groups. The nationwide count of hate groups has seen a decline in recent years, with the U.S. having 784 active hate groups in 2014, a decrease from its 2011 peak of 1,018 groups, according to the Southern Poverty Law Center. In 2007, 127 hate crimes were reported in South Carolina, according to the FBI, with the number rising to 153 the following year. However, in 2013, the number dropped significantly to 51, as per FBI statistics. In July 2014, the KKK distributed leaflets to a South Carolina neighborhood bearing the message, "Save Our Land, Join the Klan," as reported by NBC News. Nearly half of the 5,922 hate crimes reported nationally in 2013 were racially motivated, making it the most common form of prejudice. Sexual orientation was the second most common, accounting for 20.8% of reported hate crimes, according to FBI statistics. Rev. Al Sharpton, president of the National Action Network, expressed his concern in a statement, questioning, "What has our society come to when people in a prayer meeting in the sacred halls of a church can be shot in what is deemed a possible hate crime?" She was kept on life-support at a B.C. hospital until doctors determined the fetus was viable enough for a caesarean section. On Monday, her husband Dylan announced the arrival of their son, Iver Cohen Benson, and Robyn's passing, on Facebook. Dylan Benson, a 32-year-old IT company employee, had started the "Baby Iver" fund on the crowd-funding website YouCaring.com shortly after his wife's hospitalization. He needed financial assistance to cover the costs associated with missing work due to single-parenthood and funeral planning. Initially, his goal was to raise $36,000. Dylan Benson expressed his gratitude for the outpouring of love, kind words, and support during this difficult time. He plans to use the additional funds for his son's care, education, and a new living space.
We find ourselves in an era marked by a profound shift in pesticide usage. It's almost as if we've collectively forgotten a time when chemicals were used with minimal regulation, a period spanning decades in the United States. This was the pre-Silent Spring era, preceding the Clean Water Act and the establishment of the Environmental Protection Agency. The enactment of the Clean Water Act and the creation of the EPA were significant milestones in shaping our current, much safer chemical environment. However, pesticides continue to persist, making their way from Midwestern farms into waterways and drinking supplies. A comprehensive study conducted by the US Geological Survey and published recently in Environmental Science and Technology provides insights from water samples taken between 1992 and 2011 at over 200 points along rivers and streams across the U.S. The study reveals that insecticides and herbicides were widespread. The positive takeaway is that the potentially hazardous levels of these chemicals have significantly decreased, attributed to the introduction of newer, safer pesticides and stricter regulations. According to the study, "Human-health benchmarks were much less frequently exceeded, and during 2002-2011, only one agricultural stream and no urban or mixed-land-use streams exceeded human-health benchmarks for any of the measured pesticides." On the downside, the presence of pesticide pollutants in urban streams has increased during the same period, rising from 53% to 90%. This increase is primarily due to two pesticides: fipronil, used to eliminate cockroaches and ants, and dichlorvos, which targets household pests such as aphids and mites. Both these chemicals, particularly their byproducts, are harmful to aquatic life at the detected levels. It's worth mentioning that the study did not monitor for certain popular pesticides, including Roundup, mainly due to testing costs. As Karen Ryberg, one of the study co-authors, told the New York Times, "There are constantly new pesticides coming out, and there's a lag time between deciding a pesticide will be around for a while, then developing a lab test to detect it, and then having enough data to analyze it. In science, that's a concern

In Caracas, Venezuela, due to an ongoing electricity crisis, public employees will now work only on Mondays and Tuesdays for at least two weeks. This decision was announced by President Nicolas Maduro, who explained that the government is taking this step to conserve energy, as the water level at the nation's largest dam has dropped significantly due to a severe drought, nearing its minimum operating level. Experts suggest that inadequate planning and maintenance are also contributing factors. Previously, over 3 million public workers were given Fridays off by the socialist administration, and on Monday, the country initiated daily four-hour power outages. The government is now extending these Friday holidays to grade school teachers. However, it seems that employees of public hospitals and state-run supermarkets will still be required to work. Venezuelans have expressed disbelief at the news, as most public workers will spend less time in the office. Workers will continue to receive their salaries for the days they are sent home. Some have been using their Fridays off to buy groceries and other essentials, while others have been using the time to watch TV and run air conditioning units, leading critics to question the effectiveness of the furlough as an energy-saving measure. Power outages have been a persistent issue in this oil-rich country. Despite President Hugo Chavez's promise in 2010 to address the problem, little progress has been made.

The ongoing Ebola outbreak, the most severe ever documented, has prompted Liberia to close many of its borders, prohibit public gatherings, and institute quarantines in certain communities as a means to curb the spread of the Ebola virus. As of now, there have been 1,201 confirmed, suspected, or probable instances of the disease in West Africa this year, resulting in over 670 deaths. Ebola, which lacks a vaccine or cure, has the potential to claim the lives of up to 90% of those infected. The virus is transmittable through contact with infected animals or other patients, with fruit bats, a common food source in West Africa, believed to be a carrier. Initial symptoms resemble the flu, but the virus can impair kidney and liver function, and in severe cases, damage blood cells, leading to both external and internal bleeding. This outbreak originated in south-eastern Guinea in February and reached Liberia in March and Sierra Leone in May. Last week, Nigeria reported its first probable case, and is now on high alert following the death of a Liberian man in its largest city, Lagos. An outbreak is deemed to have ended only after 42 days (twice the maximum incubation period) have passed without any new confirmed cases. Therefore, the current outbreak will persist until at least September. Subscribe to our daily newsletter to stay informed.
A team of Pakistani climbers has achieved the historic feat of reaching the summit of K2, the world's second tallest mountain, located in Pakistan close to the northern border with China. They reached the summit at 02:30 on Saturday (22:30 GMT on Friday). Mountaineers consider K2 more challenging to conquer than Mount Everest, the world's highest peak, and descending from the top is said to be more perilous. This expedition was undertaken by the Pakistani climbers on the 60th anniversary of the first successful ascent of K2, which was achieved by two Italians - Achille Compagnoni and Lino Lacedelli - on 31 July 1954. The current expedition, named K2 60 Years Later, consists of six Pakistani climbers: Hassan Jan, Ali Durani, Rahmat Ullah Baig, Ghulam Mehdi, Ali, and Muhammad Sadiq. Three Italians are also part of the group. Although individual Pakistani climbers have scaled K2 before, this is the first successful team attempt by Pakistani climbers. The BBC's Shahzeb Jillani in Islamabad notes that many climbers have lost their lives during the descent, making the return to base camp a challenging task. In June, an Italian organization supporting the Pakistani effort installed a weather station providing data to the climbers and researchers monitoring activity in high mountain regions.

Sydney Gholston found herself in a line at a Kentucky Walmart, her cart brimming with Thanksgiving turkeys. A kind-hearted elderly man, who turned out to be Jon Voight, engaged her in conversation from behind. As Gholston turned to face him, she was taken aback; it was none other than the renowned actor. Voight, who was in town filming a movie, inquired about the six frozen turkeys in her cart, remarking that she must have a large family. Gholston, aged 28, chuckled and disclosed that the birds were intended for feeding children at the Home of the Innocents, a local nonprofit shelter and pediatric convalescent center. Immediately upon hearing this, Voight reached into his wallet and offered to pay for her groceries. With his assistance, Gholston was able to bring the turkeys back to the Home, where they would feed approximately 70 of the 196 residents this Thanksgiving holiday. Meredith Pack, marketing manager for the Home of the Innocents, informed CBS News that some medically fragile children may not partake in the traditional Thanksgiving meal, while some residents may have other holiday arrangements.
