The initial detection of whirling disease in fish has been confirmed in Johnson Lake, located within Banff National Park. In response, Parks Canada has imposed restrictions on access to the lake, situated east of the Banff townsite, to curb the spread of the disease. This condition does not pose a threat to humans or other mammals, but it can have a detrimental effect on certain fish populations. Consequently, fishing and recreational activities have been prohibited. Whirling disease primarily affects trout and salmon, causing infected fish to exhibit a circular swimming pattern and succumb prematurely. The disease is attributed to the microscopic parasite Myxobolus cerebralis, which can be transmitted to other water bodies via gear, equipment, and materials used for swimming, paddling, boating, and fishing. Bill Hunt, the conservation manager at Parks Canada, emphasized the challenge of containing the disease due to the parasites' microscopic size. "The parasites are several times smaller than the diameter of a human hair, and these spores can persist in the mud for up to several decades," Hunt informed CBC News. To minimize the risk of disease transmission, Hunt advised against transporting fish between bodies of water and proper disposal of entrails. He also recommended cleaning, draining, and drying boats and equipment to prevent the spread of the disease. The Canadian Food Inspection Agency reported this as the first confirmed case of the disease in Canada. They are collaborating closely with Parks Canada and Alberta Environment and Parks (AEP) to ensure a unified response. Additional fish samples are being collected from other bodies of water within Banff National Park, while AEP is also testing fish downstream from the park. Any suspected cases should be reported to 1-855-336-BOAT.
A contentious situation has arisen between a property developer and the family of a deceased individual whose grave is located in the center of a construction site, resulting in an unusual spectacle. Local residents were compensated to relocate the graves of their family members to accommodate construction. However, one family, reportedly dissatisfied with the compensation for relocation, chose to resist. As a result, the sole grave stands on a mound of earth, elevated 10 meters above the ground, while construction continues around it. According to Britain's Daily Mail, the tomb is the ancestral burial site of a villager from nearby Longbao. The Sun newspaper reports that the developers are now offering approximately £100,000 ($160,675) to relocate the grave, including the headstone. Known as the 'nail grave' by Asian media outlets, this is the latest instance of resistance against land dispossession from Chinese people. Previous examples have included the construction of a freeway around a solitary house and a solitary house being left standing on a mound in the middle of a construction site.

Celebrating Indonesia's National Music Day, we're thrilled to introduce or reintroduce you to a captivating facet of our nation's musical history - the psychedelic rock scene of the 1970s. Due to Suharto's strict censorship, this genre, characterized by relentless fuzz, overtly political lyrics, strong rhythms, and a gritty low-fidelity, remained largely underground. Consequently, much of this music was lost and overlooked. However, in the new millennium, following Suharto's fall, music enthusiasts rediscovered these hidden gems, leading to the unearthing of archives and the dusting off of old records. As a result, a wealth of vintage Indonesian rock is now accessible to all. The most impressive compilation we've encountered is an album titled "Those Shocking Shaking Days," released by Now-Again Records. According to the album's official description: "The progressive music scenes in 1970s Indonesia were largely underground due to strict censorship imposed by the dictator Suharto. Those who performed music marked by relentless fuzz, over the top, politically charged lyrics, strong rhythms, and a cranky low-fidelity were truly rebellious." "Indonesia, known primarily for its coffee exports, is better recognized for the music it creates. This situation hasn't been rectified by the rough-hewn Indonesian bootlegs that have circulated the psychedelic landscape over the past five years." "Thanks to the tireless and expensive research of Canadian hip hop producer and Southeast Asian music specialist Jason Moss Connoy, and the trust placed in Now-Again Records by Indonesian rock legend Benny Soebardja as he traversed his homeland's islands securing the rights necessary for us to offer this anthology, we feel we can, in good spirits and conscience, shine the light on some of the most impressive organizations to offer their take on the psychedelic and progressive rock and funk sounds during the early shocking, shaking days of Suharto's regime." We'd like to extend our gratitude to Reddit user Flotack on r/Indonesia for this fantastic find!
Combat situations invariably present unforeseen hurdles. From Germany's deployment of mustard gas in World War I to North Vietnam's surprising effectiveness in utilizing their air defense system during the Vietnam War, the United States has consistently encountered unforeseen threats in battle that necessitated swift reactions. Troops on the ground are consistently adapting to evolving enemy strategies with the resources available to them. However, the part of the Defense Department responsible for training and equipping these troops has historically shown less adaptability. This may come as a surprise to many outside its premises: the Pentagon is often inadequately prepared to address urgent needs that arise during wartime. The Department of Defense has a commendable history of making astute, long-term acquisitions, as demonstrated by the significant qualitative advantage the United States holds over potential adversaries. Although the department still grapples with controlling military system costs, it has made significant strides in enhancing the taxpayer's purchasing power. The Pentagon has also, tragically necessitated, spearheaded advancements in medical technology, particularly in the areas of prosthetic limbs and the treatment of traumatic brain injuries and post-traumatic stress disorder. Yet, the same system that excels at anticipating future needs has proven less capable of swiftly providing technology and equipment to troops on the battlefield. Over the past five years, serving as undersecretary of defense for acquisition, technology, and logistics, and then as deputy secretary of defense, I have dedicated much time to addressing this shortcoming. With the Iraq war concluded and the war in Afghanistan winding down, it is crucial to comprehend what hindered the Pentagon from promptly meeting immediate demands during these conflicts, what lasting lessons can be gleaned from its attempts to become more responsive, and how to establish the appropriate institutions to guarantee success against future threats, where agility is paramount. The introduction of a new capability on the battlefield involves three primary stages: determining what is required, acquiring it, and deploying it effectively.

It's astonishing that knowledgeable, seasoned individuals, who have observed our current situation for years, continue to espouse the notion of "returning to growth." This idea, I believe, is no longer debatable. We live within a natural system, and it's widely accepted that this system is global, intricately interconnected, with all parts depending on each other. Humanity has reached a state of maturity, a level of saturation, as we've become global, spreading across the planet, interconnected on various levels. We've essentially hit a ceiling in terms of quantitative growth, a limit of expansion, even in terms of technological, cultural, and social development. We're like a fully grown organism that can no longer expand in the same way. Instead, we must focus on qualitative development. Yet, we persist in measuring everything quantitatively, anxiously waiting for the resumption of growth as if it's the only means of evolution. This is akin to a teenager or an adult who, instead of learning how to live as a mature individual, insists on staying a child, constantly measuring their growth by increments, waiting for an impossible goal, measuring their life and success by those same increments. We can no longer grow in the same way we once did. Now, we must "attend university," learn about the world around us, and understand how to exist harmoniously in this global, interconnected world, avoiding self-destructive behaviors driven by egoistic, subjective thinking. We must build a future that is mutually beneficial, sustainable, and in harmony with the natural system, rather than endangering ourselves by needlessly reinventing everything.

A recent study categorizes Eagles fans as emotionally stable, a term seldom associated with them. This refers to their consistent emotional responses, rather than being prone to frequent highs and lows. The researchers from Emory University, Mike Lewis and Manish Tripathi, analyzed Twitter data to gauge fan reactions to team wins and losses during the 2012 NFL regular season, focusing on happiness, sadness, and emotional stability. The happiest fans after a win were those of the New Orleans Saints, while the saddest after a loss were Pittsburgh Steelers fans. The fans with the fewest mood swings were those of the Dallas Cowboys. Despite Eagles' poor 4-12 record in the 2012 season, their fans might have shown stability due to potential relief after losses, such as the anticipation of getting rid of head coach Andy Reid. One possible explanation for the emotional stability of Eagles fans could be their forward-looking perspective. As the team continued to lose games, many fans seemed to focus on the upcoming season and a potential new head coach, rather than dwelling on recent losses. Emory University's analysis supports this notion, suggesting that Eagles fans in 2012 could be more accurately described as 'resigned', as they appeared to look forward to the next season rather than dwell on the most recent loss.

GIFs do not automatically animate to prevent the download of large files that are unnecessary. Opening a tweet individually will immediately start playing the GIF. North Korea, provoked by what it deems as escalating joint military exercises with the U.S. in the South, has declared that it will initiate a nuclear attack if it perceives a threat. Furthermore, North Korea has asserted its intention to carry out additional nuclear tests following its latest, fifth nuclear event, and continue ballistic missile testing. In recent months, the North has launched over twenty ballistic missiles, aiming to enhance its capacity to accurately deliver a payload. According to Lee Yong Pil, director of the Foreign Ministry's Institute for American Studies, as reported by NBC News, "The U.S. has nuclear weapons stationed off our coast, aiming at our country, our capital, and our leader, Kim Jong Un. We will not retreat as long as there's a nuclear threat from the U.S." Lee added, "If we sense that the U.S. intends to attack us, we will act first. We possess the technology. We need nuclear weapons to safeguard our nation, and our policy is to go nuclear." Lee also suggested that North Korea has the capability to launch a missile reaching the western coast of the U.S. However, American intelligence has yet to confirm this claim. Pyongyang has also discussed launching satellites into orbit using its new missile technology, a feat the West doubts North Korea can achieve. The regime has also spoken about space travel. In Oregon House, California, a suspect was fatally shot and two deputies were wounded in a shootout following a response to reports of an agitated man uprooting plants at a Rastafarian church's marijuana farm. At approximately 8:40 a.m., three deputies arrived at the remote farm in Oregon House, about 55 miles north of Sacramento, after being called to an unspecified disturbance. Upon arrival, a resident pointed out the suspect to two deputies. The suspect then fled up a hill and was lost from sight after about 100 yards near another residence. The deputies were granted permission to search the home, and the gunman opened fire on the two who entered, while the third deputy took up a position at the backdoor. The third deputy rushed inside twice to extract his colleagues to safety. The deputies were unaware of the shooter's fate, prompting SWAT teams to fire tear gas before entering and discovering the deceased individual. The sheriff stated that they had yet to identify the shooter or determine if the deputies were responsible for his death or if it was self-inflicted. Both wounded deputies were airlifted to a hospital and were in serious condition, though expected to recover following surgery. Heidi Lepp, leader of the Sugarleaf Rastafarian Church, received a call from church members living on the marijuana farm reporting a new worker's erratic behavior, plant destruction, and possession of a firearm. Lepp contacted the sheriff's office and instructed the farm's occupants to leave immediately. Lepp identified the suspect only as "Sawyer" and claimed he had been on the property for about a month. The property, owned by a branch of Lepp's church, spans between 20 and 40 acres and is considered a sacrament by the church, though it does not possess a permit for medicinal marijuana cultivation in Yuba County. The shooting took place a day after two police officers were shot and wounded in the central California city of Los Banos, some 200 miles south, during a struggle with a man who broke into his estranged wife's apartment. Police fatally shot the shooter in that incident.

Barbara Loden, a remarkable figure in American independent cinema, ventured into filmmaking after a successful stint on Broadway, winning a Tony, and brief appearances in Hollywood productions. However, these endeavors failed to provide the fulfillment she sought. Her desire for creative control led her to direct her sole feature film, Wanda (1970), which has since been recognized as one of the most impactful independent films ever made. Wanda tells the poignant story of a woman struggling to find her place in the world, a narrative that resonates deeply with me. The film's authenticity is intertwined with the real-world events that inspired it, such as the true story of Alma Malone, who experienced a similar ordeal of kidnapping, robbery, and imprisonment. Loden poured her life experiences into the film, making it a reflection of her own journey. Tragically, Loden passed away ten years later, having directed only one feature film. Wanda is a compelling and heart-wrenching story, both within the film and in the context of Loden's life. Loden was a trailblazer, and Wanda stands as a testament to her groundbreaking work. I highly recommend watching it. This film showcases themes such as divorce court, outlaws, in-laws, cheap motels, life on the run, and the sad fate of a once-beautiful girl. For further viewing, consider Housekeeping and Harlan County U.S.A. You may also find the Pennsylvania Anthracite History Museum's website informative. For a glimpse into Loden's life, watch her appearance on the Mike Douglas show. To learn more about Wanda, visit its page on IMDB.
Super WiFi trials, led by Microsoft and supported by the UK's largest TV providers, may prevent British mobile data enthusiasts from having to limit their usage. This enhanced wireless network operates within the 150MHz spectrum that terrestrial television avoids, often referred to as 'white spaces.' This unused frequency is maintained by networks abroad, including in the US, to prevent signal interference. However, Microsoft's Dan Reed emphasizes that spectrum is a finite natural resource. With limited alternatives for operators to exploit, this repurposed TV signal shows promise, particularly in urban areas like Cambridge, chosen for its mix of old and new buildings. This technology, which can deliver speeds of up to 16Mbps, is already being tested in Cambridge and is set to be rolled out by British Telecom in Scotland. Given these developments, it seems that this technology has a promising future in the UK. Unfortunately, the US seems to be facing delays in unraveling red tape for a homegrown build-out. In the historic settlement of Jamestown, Virginia, between 1607 and 1625, a group of early American colonists, faced with extreme hardships, resorted to cannibalism, as suggested by recent findings by scientists at the Smithsonian's National Museum of Natural History. During an excavation in 2012, the remains of a 14-year-old girl, later named "Jane," were discovered in Jamestown. Her skull showed signs of postmortem damage, and her bones were found alongside those of slaughtered animals in a trash pit. Researchers were able to date the bones to the winter of 1609-1610, a period infamously known as the "starving time" when hundreds of colonists perished. Archaeologist Bill Kelso, who led the excavation, noted the unusual nature of the discovery. The team sought further analysis from the Smithsonian’s National Museum of Natural History due to their expertise in the local contextual history. The girl's injuries indicate that the colonists may have resorted to cannibalism, a practice that has long been speculated but never conclusively proven. Documents from the time period suggest widespread cannibalism, but the latest findings seem to be the first concrete evidence to support these claims. Dr. Douglas Owsley of the Smithsonian explained that the postmortem treatment of Jane's body reflects the dire circumstances the colonists faced during the winter of 1609-1610. The bone fragments show unusual cutting and chopping patterns, indicating a lack of experience in butchering, but a clear intention to dismember the body for consumption. It remains unclear what caused Jane's death. A facial reconstruction of Jane will be displayed at the National Museum of Natural History starting May 3. An image of what she might have looked like, created using forensic facial reconstruction techniques, was published on the Smithsonian's website. This revelation was shared by the Jamestown Rediscovery Archaeological Project on YouTube on May 1, 2013. A correction was made to an earlier version of this story, stating that Jane's remains would be on display at the National Museum of Natural History.
Today marks the testing of a new C/C++ compiler: zapcc, developed by Ceemple Software and built upon a modified version of LLVM/clang. This innovative compiler features an advanced caching system and is compatible with Mac OS X, Linux, and Windows. For our tests, we'll be using significant software such as LMMS, a popular professional music production platform, to gather some meaningful compilation time statistics. The tests will be conducted on Linux Mint, using hardware equipped with an i5-5200U CPU and 8GB of RAM. First, we'll run tests with the unmodified clang provided by the system, followed by tests with zapcc. We've increased the default memory cache in the zapccs.config file from 1200 to 2000 for these tests, and users can also choose which files to exclude from caching. Here are the results for clang with 5 concurrent jobs: [clang output] Now, let's see the results with zapcc: [zapcc output] As you can see, there is a noticeable decrease in compilation time. We'll repeat the test with another source code, such as OpenCV, to verify if the time decrease is consistent. [clang output for OpenCV] [zapcc output for OpenCV] As you can see, the delta is significant once again! Zapcc could prove particularly valuable for projects like Qt4/5, which typically take several hours to complete the compilation of all components. In a professional context, the time-saving potential of zapcc is evident, as C++ projects often involve substantial codebases. However, due to the caching mechanism, it's essential to balance the settings according to the target hardware to manage logical and unavoidable memory usage increases. Since zapcc is based on clang/LLVM, it may be possible to port it to FreeBSD, a platform that is gaining popularity in the professional world. This could be a worthwhile consideration for future development. Labels: clang, linux, lmms, opencv, zapcc.
Pittsburgh (KDKA) - Authorities are investigating a local high school coach and several players after they are accused of taping an autistic teenager to a goal post. The alleged hazing incident transpired Sunday night at the soccer fields of Highlands High School. Sixteen-year-old Austin Babinsack claims he was left taped to the goal for approximately 15 minutes, while the students returned to the school to fetch another student. "I was quite shaken, I thought I was going to be stuck there for a long time," Austin told KDKA in an exclusive interview. An off-duty Pennsylvania State Trooper discovered him and assisted in his release. "He was terrified, he could have suffered harm, he could have had a heart attack due to the stress, he was screaming at the top of his lungs," Austin's mother, Kristy Babinsack, says. Babinsack states that Austin is autistic. "They taped my hands, my legs, all the way up to my waist, and then they attempted to take a photograph of it. I told them then, and they walked away disappointed," Austin said. Highlands School District has suspended coach Jim Turner, and two of the players for at least 5 days. "I'm just disappointed with the Highland soccer team, they should have been supervised better," a disappointed Austin's mother commented. The district issued the following statement about the incident, "Highlands School District does not take matters such as hazing and bullying lightly. The district issues strict disciplinary action on students who believe these actions are appropriate and harmless." Babinsack's mother says she is helping Austin understand that things may worsen before they improve, "watching my child go through it, and knowing there's nothing I can do right now to make him feel safe." "I believe the coach was aware, he wasn't there, but he knew it was happening, he knows that it's been going on. He's the adult, these are kids let's face it they're 17. We have to hold the adults accountable first before we can hold the kids accountable," his mother said. Babinsack states that Austin attended a school soccer game, and players ridiculed him and called him a snitch. Harrison Township police confirm they are investigating. Austin plans to return to school tomorrow.
We are embarking on a collaborative endeavor to author a comprehensive guide on GNU Guile, a Scheme language implementation. In essence, this book will serve as a repository of solutions, and I invite you to join me in this venture. By saying we are writing a book, I am referring to a collaborative effort between us. I am crowdsourcing this book, and I aim to compile 100 examples for it. Every few weeks, we will focus on a new theme, delving into Guile's capabilities to solve a specific category of problems. Each week will present a new challenge, a new script that needs to be written within the theme. If you choose to participate, you will have a couple of weeks to demonstrate your skills. It's important to note that you don't need to be an expert to contribute. These tasks should not be overly challenging. I'm not asking you to participate for the sake of recognition alone. Most of the tasks will come with a bounty for their completion, typically around 100 USD. This project is ambitious, and I cannot predict exactly how it will unfold.
A Utah-based electric vehicle manufacturer, the Nikola Motor Company, unveiled its initial offerings today. The first model is the utilitarian Nikola Zero, boasting a claimed range of 125 miles. While it's somewhat impressive, the main attraction is the Nikola One, a big rig that, in my opinion, could very well be the most stylish of its kind ever created. Despite the inherent challenges in designing a truck capable of hauling trailers, the Nikola One manages to exude an air of legitimacy and sophistication. The proposed specifications of the Nikola One are nothing short of extraordinary: it employs a turbine to maintain its 320 kWh battery pack, offering a staggering 1,200 miles of range between refueling. Buyers will have the option to choose from various versions that utilize different turbine fuels, and the interior features a large, Tesla-esque touchscreen in the center to manage various functions. However, it's essential to note that these vehicles are merely conceptual at this stage. Nikola merely unveiled renders of the Zero and One today, which can be reserved on their website for $750 and $1,500 respectively. The Zero will retail for $42,000, while the One will cost $375,000. Whether these vehicles will ever hit the market remains to be seen, as the path to producing electric vehicles is long and fraught with obstacles and failures. In essence, the Nikola One represents a potential game-changer in the world of self-driving big rigs. Its futuristic design, highlighted by a wraparound windshield, sets it apart from any truck currently on the road.
A Surrey resident, OBi Canuel, 36, has reached a standoff with the Insurance Corporation of British Columbia (ICBC) over his right to wear religious headgear in his driver's license photo. On Friday, he was informed that ICBC would not allow him to drive beyond the day unless he agreed to a photograph without headgear. Canuel had been content to wait for a change in policy, but had never encountered issues until now. When he visited an ICBC driver licensing office on Friday, staff issued him a one-day permit. As he needs to work, this is inconvenient, and he doubts the issue will be resolved over the weekend, leaving him temporarily unable to drive. Canuel, a Pastafarian minister in the Church of the Flying Spaghetti Monster, views ICBC's demands as an infringement on his rights under the Canadian Charter of Rights and Freedoms, which guarantees the freedom of religious expression. He believes these rights were established not only for mainstream religions but also for unconventional cases. Canuel advocates for everyone's right to express their religion within the bounds of the law, and he does not want anyone to feel ashamed or embarrassed about religious expression. Canuel's dispute began nearly a year ago when he attempted to have his license photo taken while wearing headgear, believing it was in accordance with ICBC policy. The policy states that ICBC acknowledges the right to religious expression and will not ask individuals to remove headgear that does not interfere with facial recognition technology, provided it is worn in conjunction with religious practice or necessary due to medical treatment. However, ICBC refused, stating in a later letter that there was no religious requirement preventing Canuel from removing his colander. Adam Grossman, a spokesperson for ICBC, declined to disclose whether the provincial insurer maintains a list of recognized religions or the criteria for accepting religious headgear. He stated in a written statement that ICBC will attempt to accommodate customers with head coverings if their faith prohibits their removal, but Canuel could not provide proof that his faith required him to wear the colander. Grossman also noted that Canuel is not wearing his headgear in videos posted on his YouTube account. For further information or to share other stories, readers can contact mrobinson@vanc
Three years ago, a disastrous shift occurred in economic policy, affecting both our region and Europe. Despite the financial crisis abating, economies on both continents remained deeply entrenched in recession, characterized by extremely high unemployment rates. Yet, inexplicably, the policy-making elite across the West collectively determined that unemployment was no longer a critical issue, and reducing budget deficits should be the primary focus. In my recent articles, I've contended that concerns regarding deficits are, in fact, overstated—and have illustrated the growing attempts by deficit hawks to perpetuate fear. Today, however, I'd like to discuss a different but related aspect of this situation: the urgent quest to identify instances where austerity measures have proven successful. The proponents of fiscal austerity—the austerians—not only made threats but also promises: austerity, they asserted, would prevent crises and usher in prosperity. It's important to note that the austerians are not devoid of romanticism; in fact, they've spent years searching for a shining example of effective austerity measures, which they affectionately refer to as "Mr. Goodpain." The search for this elusive success story began with a passionate relationship between the austerians and the Republic of Ireland. Following the bursting of its real estate bubble, Ireland swiftly implemented harsh spending cuts and was touted as the epitome of economic rectitude. Jean-Claude Trichet, the head of the European Central Bank, proclaimed Ireland as the role model for all European nations in debt. American conservatives were even more ardent in their praise. For instance, Alan Reynolds, a senior fellow at the Cato Institute, advocated that Ireland's policies should serve as a blueprint for the United States as well.

According to Barran Liebman's report, the Portland City Council has outlined proposed regulations for the upcoming Sick Leave Ordinance. The city will accept public comments in written form before finalizing the rules, which is expected to occur by November 1, 2013. Beginning January 1, 2014, Portland businesses with six or more employees must provide up to 40 hours of paid sick leave to employees who work a minimum of 240 hours annually. Employers with fewer than five employees are required to offer 40 hours of unpaid sick leave. This leave can be utilized for various purposes, such as an employee's personal mental or physical illness (including pregnancy, childbirth, and preventive medical care), caring for a family member with an illness, injury, or medical appointment, if the employee's workplace closes due to a public health emergency, or to care for a child whose school or daycare is closed for a similar reason. Additionally, leave may be taken for certain reasons related to domestic violence, harassment, sexual assault, or stalking. For comprehensive details on the proposed rules, please refer to the full article on the Barran Liebman website.
On October 4, the International Monetary Fund (IMF) published its latest World Economic Outlook, revealing disheartening economic news that went largely unreported by the broadcast networks. The IMF revised its global economic growth projections and country-specific estimates, with Bloomberg reporting a significant reduction in the projected U.S. growth rate. The IMF now anticipates a 1.6% growth for the U.S. in 2016, a 43% decrease from its forecast just a year ago (October 2015), which estimated a 2.8% growth for this year. The IMF has consistently downgraded its economic predictions throughout 2016, attributing the latest downgrade partly to the backlash against globalization and creeping protectionism. Despite this worrying announcement, CBS Evening News, NBC Nightly News, and ABC World News Tonight with David Muir chose to ignore it. The networks have also overlooked U.S. government reports concerning the country’s economic growth, such as the Commerce Department’s estimate of second quarter GDP growth, released on July 29, which was not reported by any of the three networks’ evening shows between July 29 and 31. On September 29, the final second quarter estimate was released, showing a "relatively weak" 1.4% growth, making the current expansion the weakest since 1949. However, the networks have generally avoided discussing this subject. If the IMF’s forecast holds true, the U.S. may experience a prolonged period of low-growth stagnation not seen since at least 1949.
Bitcoin, the leading cryptocurrency in the market, is conspicuously absent from both Google and Yahoo's currency conversion tools, despite its significant popularity. In contrast, Microsoft's search engine Bing, along with Oanda, one of the most widely utilized online currency converters, do list Bitcoin. However, neither of these platforms include other popular cryptocurrencies such as Litecoin or Dogecoin. Neither Google nor Yahoo has been forthcoming about the omission of cryptocurrencies from their converters. When questioned about Google's potential inclusion of Bitcoin in the near future, Jason Freidenfelds, Google's global communications and public affairs manager, declined to comment, stating that the company typically does not announce product launches in advance. When pressed about the reasons behind Google's exclusion of Bitcoin from its converter, Freidenfelds deflected, citing the company's focus on user feedback and constant updates to their services. A representative from Yahoo provided a similar, if more succinct, response, stating that they cannot comment on future plans. In contrast, Microsoft and Oanda were more than willing to discuss their decision to include Bitcoin in their conversion tools. A Microsoft spokesperson explained that the inclusion of Bitcoin caters to user interest in the cryptocurrency and showcases their agility in responding to emerging trends. Bing added Bitcoin to its converter on February 10, making it the first and only of the major search engines to do so. Courtney Gibson, vice president of trading at Oanda, was even more forthcoming, stating that they added Bitcoin to their converter last spring due to its potential as a financial innovation and their own history of introducing firsts to the foreign exchange market. Gibson further added that the inclusion of Bitcoin acknowledged the widespread interest in Bitcoin as a virtual payment system and responded to customer demand for it. When asked about Oanda's plans to include other cryptocurrencies in their converter, Gibson expressed a willingness to consider adding them as customer interest in additional cryptocurrencies emerges.
BlackBerry is maintaining a legal hold on the employment contract of its Senior Vice President of Software, Sebastien Marineau-Mes, preventing him from leaving the struggling company after being recruited by Apple last year. BlackBerry is unwilling to stand idly by while a former employee breaches his employment contract. It is regrettable that such action was necessary, but BlackBerry will take whatever steps are required to ensure that employees abide by their agreements. When BlackBerry enters into an agreement with an employee, as it did with Mr. Marineau-Mes, it expects that employee to honor his commitments, just as it expects to honor its own. The Ontario Superior Court of Justice has validated BlackBerry's stance, ruling that the employment contract and its terms are binding. According to reports from iMore, Marineau-Mes expressed his intention to leave BlackBerry in September of 2013 and was formally offered the position of VP of Core OS in December. He accepted and submitted his resignation letter on Dec. 23. However, BlackBerry subsequently sued Marineau-Mes for breach of contract, as the contract stipulated that the executive must provide at least six months' notice before departing the company. This contract was signed in September, during a period when BlackBerry imposed a freeze on all promotions. The court has ruled in favor of BlackBerry, mandating that the software executive serve out his full six-month notice period. In a statement to iMore, BlackBerry stated: "It is unclear at this time if Apple will wait the four months for Marineau-Mes and what the executive will do at BlackBerry in the interim."

Xlevus, a prominent member of the /r/VFIO community and developer, has transferred his virsh-patcher tool to The Passthrough POST's repositories on GitHub, signifying a substantial achievement for our VFIO automation project. For further reading, refer to: vfioselect: A Tool for Easily Binding Devices. The virsh-patcher tool simplifies the application of common adjustments, such as error 43 fixes or hugepages, via the command line interface. It can be installed on all distributions using pip, downloaded from our GitHub repository: pip install -U https://github.com/PassthroughPOST/virsh-patcher/archive/master.zip. Ensure you have a valid installation of Python and pypi/pip to set it up. Upon installation, you can use it by running: virshpatcher [FLAGS] [/path/to/target/VM/xml.xml], where [FLAGS] can be --error43, --hugepages, --host-passthrough or --patch, followed by the path of your XML patch file. The patches will be applied to the XML. As development continues, more native patches will be added to the tool, including performance optimizations, automatic hook-helper registration, and a “trimmer” to eliminate unnecessary default devices. We would like to express our gratitude to xlevus for contributing this valuable tool, as it helps us avoid redundant work and brings us closer to creating a fully automated VFIO deployment system. His contributions will greatly benefit the community. You can find him on GitHub or in our Discord server. We welcome testers for all of our VFIO-Tools projects, whether you're interested in hook-helper, vfio-select, or virsh-patcher. Don't hesitate to try them out and share your feedback. Our ultimate goal is to develop a user-friendly, graphical tweaking and configuration frontend, as well as a guest-side client for effortless changes to setup, inputs, and other aspects. However, large projects like these require a considerable amount of effort and time to bring to fruition. If you appreciate our work and wish to support us, consider becoming a Patron. The Wii U console is designed to accommodate only one touch-screen controller at a time, as confirmed by Nintendo's Shigeru Miyamoto. However, in scenarios where a game necessitates multiple touch-screen controllers, a Nintendo 3DS could potentially be used as an alternative. Miyamoto stated to News.com.au, "Our fundamental approach is that you can use one Wii U controller with the system. If we were to consider multiple controllers, it might be more practical for people to utilize their Nintendo 3DS and establish a connection for it." To date, multiplayer Wii U games have utilized up to four Wii Remote Plus controllers for additional players. By limiting the Wii U to one controller, costs for consumers are reduced, as spare touch-screen controllers, each equipped with a tablet-sized touch screen, would not be inexpensive. However, it remains uncertain if the Wii U's technical capabilities are sufficient to stream content to two controller screens simultaneously. Nintendo is currently investigating the feasibility of such a feature, as Miyamoto noted, "We are conducting research to determine if it would be possible for someone to bring their controller to a friend's house and play together on the Wii U."

All writers encounter a standstill at some point, a creative block that can be as debilitating as a physical roadblock. When this happens, what course of action should we take? Should we succumb to despair, akin to the characters in Requiem for a Dream? Or should we muster our resolve and face the challenge head-on, like John Wayne in the wild west? One strategy is brainstorming, a process that supposedly allows our creative minds to function non-linearly. An environment conducive to brainstorming is one that is chaotic and non-linear, where ideas can flow freely without the constraints of structure. In your attempts to find a "non-linear" approach, consider writing down random ideas and words that come to mind rather than forming complete sentences. Another obvious method to overcome writer's block is to draw inspiration from other authors. However, it's essential to tread carefully to avoid stepping over the line of copyright infringement. While online resources may provide clear-cut guidelines, the reality is that the boundaries are often subjective, and the courts tend to make decisions based on individual cases. One area where authors can find inspiration with minimal risk of copyright infringement is by studying history. History is a treasure trove of fascinating characters and cultures, some so evil they would make Sauron seem tame, and others so brave they would make Samwise Gamgee look like a coward. From the Chinese practice of foot-binding to the Aztecs' creation of animal-intestine balloon animals for their gods, history offers a glimpse into human identity and our collective journey. The best part about history is its vastness and accessibility. Authors can draw from any era or culture and put their unique spin on it without worrying about copyright issues. As the saying goes, "Those who do not study history are doomed to repeat it," but so are those who ignore its lessons.

As antibiotic-resistant bacteria continue to proliferate, scientists are persistently seeking novel sources of antibacterial drugs. A potential new bactericide has been discovered in the minuscule freshwater animal, Hydra. The protein identified by Joachim Grötzinger, Thomas Bosch, and their colleagues at the University of Kiel, hydramacin-1, is unique and clinically valuable due to its scarcity of resemblance with any other known antibacterial proteins, with the exception of two antimicrobials found in leeches. Hydramacin exhibited remarkable efficacy in laboratory experiments; it was able to eliminate a broad spectrum of both Gram-positive and Gram-negative bacteria, including clinically-isolated drug-resistant strains such as Klebsiella oxytoca (a common culprit of nosocomial infections). Hydramacin functions by adhering to the bacterial surface, encouraging the aggregation of nearby bacteria, and subsequently disrupting the bacterial membrane. Grötzinger and his team also determined the 3-D structure of hydramacin-1, which revealed a striking resemblance to a superfamily of proteins found in scorpion venom. Within this vast group, they propose that hydramacin and the two leech proteins belong to a newly designated family called the macins.

The popular dating application is seeking a method to monetize its free service, and native advertising appears to be the most viable option. Twitter announced in March that TweetDeck AIR, TweetDeck for Android, and TweetDeck for iPhone would be discontinued. Originally, they estimated a shutdown in early May, but they have now specified that the apps will be deactivated on May 7th. On this date, a blog post on TweetDeck will indicate that the apps will be removed from their respective app stores and will cease to function. Additionally, the Facebook integration for all TweetDeck products will also be terminated at this time. For now, TweetDeck for Mac and PC will continue to operate, and will align with the feature updates introduced in the Web and Chrome versions of the app. The Web editions will serve as the primary TweetDeck experience, and will receive new Twitter features more quickly. Twitter acquired TweetDeck in May 2011 in a deal worth $40M in cash and stock. TweetDeck was founded by Iain Dodsworth in 2008 and had received a total of $3.8m in funding before being acquired by Twitter. After the discontinuation of TweetDeck on iOS, popular Twitter app Tweetbot is expected to receive a significant increase in traffic from users leaving TweetDeck. On Android, Carbon and Hootsuite are popular alternatives. The theory often put forth to account for the wage disparity between men and women suggests that the issue lies with women not requesting pay raises. However, a recent study conducted on Australian women reveals that they are just as likely as their male counterparts to seek salary increases. The difference lies in the fact that men are more often granted these raises. The study, published this week by the Cass Business School in London, the University of Warwick, and the University of Wisconsin - Oshkosh, found that among individuals working comparable hours, men received a raise 20% of the times they asked, while women received a raise 16% of the times they asked. Approximately 70% of both men and women in the study sample reported having asked for a raise. Although the study did not propose solutions, Dr. Amanda Goodall, one of the study's authors, indicated in an interview that it narrowed the potential explanations for the disparities.
Six years ago, conservative commentator Ann Coulter defended her use of the term "retard" to describe President Barack Obama in a tweet, questioning whether the word was indeed offensive. During an interview on CNN's "Piers Morgan Tonight," she stated, "Perhaps Vice President Biden should be upset with me calling the president a retard, but not an actually disabled person." Coulter's tweet was in response to the third presidential debate between Obama and GOP nominee Mitt Romney. She had written, "I highly approve of Romney's decision to be kind and gentle to the retard." In the interview, she explained that she used the word because it's a synonym for "loser." The response to her tweet included numerous critical comments, as well as a viral blog post by Special Olympic athlete John Franklin Stephens. In his post, Stephens wrote, "Ms. Coulter, you aren't dumb and you aren't shallow. So why are you continually using a word like the R-word as an insult?" He further explained that as a man with Down syndrome, he had struggled with the public's perception that intellectual disabilities equate to being dumb and shallow. Stephens also appeared on "Piers Morgan Tonight" and stated, "The word retard is offensive, and I should not be a symbol for someone who is dumb and shallow. If they wanted to use me as a symbol, use me as a symbol for someone who fights adversity." Coulter argued that language police were dictating what words should and should not be used, and she denied that the term was offensive. She said, "It's offensive according to whom? Moron, idiot, cretin, imbecile, these were exactly like retard, once technical terms to describe people with mental disabilities. Changing the word doesn't change the definition. I was not referring to someone with Down syndrome. I was referring to the president of the United States." Coulter also suggested that those offended by the word had little ground, stating, "No disabled people are saying it, the spokesmen for the disabled." When pressed on whether the word bore a stigma similar to another offensive word - the n-word - she responded, "I wouldn't use the n-word because it's a curse word."

This is the Zijing Qingyuan Armored Spherical Cabin Electric Patrol Vehicle, showcased at the Security China exhibition in Beijing last month. Designed for anti-riot operations by police and paramilitary forces, this vehicle boasts a unique spherical cabin, providing a 360-degree panoramic view for the officers inside. Regrettably, it does not possess the ability to transform into a robot or a car, as depicted in the Transformers franchise. The Armored Spherical Cabin Electric Patrol Vehicle is armored to Level-A, a standard set by the Chinese Ministry of Public Security, offering protection against mot pistol bullets but not machine gun fire. The doors and windows are impressively thick and heavy, opening in a manner reminiscent of Aston Martin vehicles. The interior, while basic, is designed to accommodate two officers and is painted entirely in black. Power for the vehicle comes from an electric motor, but the company was unwilling to disclose its exact power output, only stating that the battery has a capacity of 15kW/h. The top speed is claimed to be 80 km/h, with a range of 120 km. The curb weight is surprisingly light at 1200 kg, with a maximum load capacity of 300 kg. The turning radius is 4.5 meters. The vehicle can be equipped with smoke grenade launchers, which can be mounted on the front fenders, just behind the indicator light. Officers can also aim their guns through the window holes. Only the two lower windows have wipers. A camera on top of the roof appears small and vulnerable. The Armored Spherical Cabin Electric Patrol Vehicle is manufactured by Suzhou Zijing Qingyuan New Energy Vehicle Technology Corporation, a company based in Suzhou, Jiangsu Province. This corporation is a joint venture between the automotive department of Tsinghua University and the Suzhou Automotive Research Institute (web), another Tsinghua-owned entity. The company specializes in creating electric vehicles for law enforcement services and had three other intriguing vehicles on display at the exhibition. In Nature Cell Biology, a team of researchers detailed the identification of a protein named disabled-2 (Dab2), which initiates the mechanism that liberates cancer cells from the primary tumor, enabling them to metastasize and form new tumors in distant locations. This process, known as epithelial-mesenchymal transdifferentiation (EMT), has long been recognized for its role in the release of epithelial cells from the solid tumor's surface and their subsequent transformation into transient mesenchymal cells, capable of establishing new tumors. This transformation is often lethal in breast, ovarian, pancreatic, and colon-rectal cancers. Ge Jin, who holds joint appointments at the Case Western Reserve University School of Dental Medicine and the Lerner Research Institute at the Cleveland Clinic, embarked on a quest to comprehend the EMT process's origins. By working backward from EMT, the researchers identified transforming growth factor-ß (TGF-ß) as the catalyst for Dab2 protein formation. It was this protein, Dab2, that instigated the EMT process. When the researchers inhibited Dab2, EMT did not occur. "This is a crucial gap in our understanding of cancer," Jin remarked. Most tumors originate from epithelial cells and display epithelial markers on their surface. The EMT process commences when some of these cells detach from the surface and undergo a transformation into fibrous mesenchymal cells, which can migrate. "EMT is the most critical step in this process," said Jin. He was part of a six-member research team, led by Philip Howe from the Department of Cancer Biology at the Lerner Research Institute, and their findings were supported by the National Cancer Institute. The research team investigated the biological mechanisms underlying cancer spread using animal models and cancer cells. "It's a complex cascade process," Jin explained. "If we can decipher the signaling pathway for regulating EMT, we can develop drugs to delay or halt EMT cells and manage tumor progression." Beyond cancer, Jin suggested that the discovered process might shed light on how other diseases advance.
Digital subchannels outperform top cable brands in terms of audience reach and household ratings, as indicated by a recent report from Katz Media Group. This report reveals that as cord-cutting and cord-shaving lead to a decrease in subscribers for most cable channels, the disparity in coverage between them and more accessible digital subchannels widens. Katz discovered that the top eight networks available on digital subchannels, including MeTV, Grit, Antenna TV, Laff, Escape, This TV, Bounce TV, and Create, have a broader reach than leading cable networks such as Food Network, CNN, Discovery Channel, and TBS. The report also highlighted that in Nielsen live-plus-seven household ratings, the top digital network, MeTV, ranked 20th among all cable and broadcast networks, surpassing cable channels like A&E, FX, Lifetime, TLC, Bravo, and MTV. Stacey Schulman, executive VP of strategy and analytics for Katz Media Group, noted that digital networks are often perceived as a lower-tier option for advertising investment, but they are actually performing at par or even exceeding cable networks that are regularly considered for investment. The report, published on Monday, also showed that digital networks have experienced audience growth during a period of relative stagnation for both cable and broadcast. From May 2016 to May 2017, the average Nielsen live-plus-seven household share increased by 42% for digital networks. In contrast, it grew only 2% for cable and decreased 4% for broadcast over the same period. Digital subchannels came into existence following the transition of broadcast TV from analog to digital transmission in 2009. Most subchannels are managed by local broadcast stations, and the airtime on them is usually leased to digital networks. Many of these networks attract audiences with schedules centered around library programming, such as MeTV, which specializes in classic series like "Alf" and "The Andy Griffith Show," often catering to specific genres.
This paper offers a comprehensive critique of the incentives-access binary in copyright discussions. Traditionally, copyright theory has been built on the premise that copyright serves a dual purpose: incentivizing creators to produce cultural works and facilitating public access to these works. This article contends that the prevailing copyright theory tends to overlook the potential for creating a copyright system that can financially support authors without restricting access to creative works. The Internet's abundance suggests that fostering greater access to cultural works to promote learning, sharing, and creative expression should be a primary objective of copyright policy. This paper explores various models for supporting and organizing cultural production without exclusivity, such as crowdfunding, tips, levies, restitution, and service-based models. Currently, each of these models falls short of presenting a unified and compelling vision of copyright's two primary functions: the instrumental (how cultural production can be funded) and the ethical (how authors can be fairly compensated). This paper proposes three areas for future research to assess the feasibility of alternative copyright models: (1) developing a more robust theory of fairness in copyright remuneration, (2) conducting more empirical studies on commons models of cultural production, and (3) critically examining the non-economic harm that exclusivity in copyright might prevent.

Las Vegas - The Virtuix Omni aspires to achieve for the lower body what the Oculus Rift accomplished for the eyes: making immersive virtual reality accessible to users. This device is a 360-degree treadmill that enables users to walk and run in a virtual reality environment while remaining securely stationary. Similar to the Rift, the Omni was initially crowdfunded, garnered significant attention over the past few years, and is set to be delivered to early backers later this year. I had the opportunity to try it at CES 2015. The Omni can be best described as a body cage with a large, shallow bowl of "walking" space, encircled and supported by arms forming a waist-high ring around the user. Slip-on shoes equipped with sensors glide on the bowl's surface, while a harness maintains the user's balance and posture. The demo took me through a shooting gallery with the Oculus Rift, requiring me to sprint through corridors and shoot targets with a gun-shaped controller. The version of the Omni I used was a pre-production model, and only had the forward-walking function integrated into the demo. However, the final version that will be shipped to users will allow for movement in all directions. Walking on the Omni feels unusual at first due to the almost non-existent friction between the shoes and the floor. After some adjustment, I managed to find a relatively comfortable walking pace, but initially, I had to move like I was being pursued by a Scooby-Doo monster, spinning my legs in place while bongos played in my head. The harness proved essential in this situation, keeping me centered on the waist-high ring of the Omni, preventing me from being propelled forward or backward as I moved. I eventually found the right balance to move quickly without appearing to flail around in an inner tube. The sensation of skating on a waxed floor in socks did not disappear, but despite the slippery movement, I advanced with reliable control in the demo. On occasion, the sensors detached from my feet (due to the pre-production model and my enthusiastic running style), so I couldn't compare my score in the demo to others. However, those minutes of shooting definitely felt like something I

Analyzing Amazon's S3 Buckets: As promised, here's an analysis of the data I gathered using my Bucket Finder tool. I ran it with a list of common names from Packet Storm, which contained 2,268 names. The results are as follows: Buckets: - Don't Exist: 1,206 - Private: 848 - Public: 131 This indicates that most of the names tried do not exist, but 5% do and are public. If the same return is true for Packet Storm's larger word lists (over 100,000 words), we could potentially identify over 5,000 public buckets for investigation. Files: Of the public buckets found, this is the breakdown of the files found in them: - Private: 6,016 - Public: 9,683 - Total: 15,699 This suggests that approximately one-third of users who make their buckets public still put private files in them. This could imply that users are deliberately choosing what files to share and what to keep private, or it could be due to certain applications requiring public buckets but creating files within them as private. File Types: Based on file extension, here's a breakdown of the public file types I found: - Images: jpg, png, gif, tiff, psd, bmp - 7,086 - Web: html, css, js - 1,377 - Videos and Music: mp3, mp4, flv, mov, avi, wmv, m4v, aa, mpg - 436 - Documents: pdf, doc, xls, ppt - 80 - Archives: rar, zip, gz - 57 - SQL: sql - 1 - Other: 646 I found that most people are using S3 to store images, with many personal photo collections. I also encountered sensitive documents, such as MOD training requisition forms, company accounts, and other personal data that should not have been online. The videos didn't reveal much interesting, while the music category had a few people sharing large mp3 collections.
In the past year, a significant number of errors in obtaining search warrants have been identified, leading to innocent individuals being wrongly targeted in investigations related to sexual offenses. This disconcerting revelation comes from the annual report of the Interception of Communications Commissioner, Sir Stanley Burnton, submitted to the Prime Minister. The errors, which involve some of the most invasive powers the state can employ against its citizens, have led to unacceptable consequences, including the separation of children from their parents and the questioning of innocent people as suspects in child sexual exploitation cases. For instance, two children were separated from their parents over a weekend due to an error in the documentation, which led to the police raiding the wrong address. It was later discovered that the parents were innocent. Furthermore, digital devices belonging to innocent individuals have been forensically examined by the police, according to Burnton. The primary cause of these errors lies in incorrect entries made into software that assists police in determining the location of specific IP (internet protocol) addresses. However, Burnton cautions investigators against relying on IP addresses, as they are frequently reassigned by internet service providers. These errors, Burton emphasizes, are particularly concerning in cases involving child sex exploitation, with far too many instances reported. He notes that out of the total number of applications, 0.004% were serious errors committed by those authorized to use intrusive powers, not just the police. As a result of these errors, innocent individuals have been treated as suspects, detained, or had their homes and devices searched on seven occasions. In other instances, two innocent individuals were arrested and questioned under caution by officers investigating child sexual exploitation due to similar IP address errors. Misinterpretations of communications data led to the wrong person being detained and questioned in an investigation into a pedophile ring. In a murder investigation, officers obtained a telephone number but recorded it incorrectly in a database, leading to contact with the wrong person.

North America's burgeoning marijuana industry shows few signs of slowing down, with a Canadian university now offering a comprehensive course on growing and selling cannabis. Kwantlen Polytechnic University in Metro Vancouver will provide students with a 14-week course, covering topics from cultivation to navigating the intricate legal landscape of Canada's marijuana industry. The course, titled "Introduction to Professional Management of Marijuana for Medical Purposes in Canada," will be led by Tegan Adams, a business development manager at Experchem Laboratories. The course will be divided into two parts, with the first focusing on plant production and facility management, and the second on marketing, sales, and drug development. The course fee is $3,000. According to Metro News, the university's executive director, Jim Pelton, explained that the production aspect of the course resembles what one might find in the manufacturing industry rather than flower cultivation. The Canadian National Medical Marijuana association played a significant role in developing the course. Canada currently has 25 licensed marijuana growing establishments. Elsewhere, marijuana education is also making its way into the academic sphere. In July, the Northeastern Institute of Cannabis was established in Massachusetts and is now accepting student applications. Upon successful completion, students will receive a "cannabis industry certification." In February, Anne Arundel Community College in Lanham, Md., introduced a course focused on business opportunities in the emerging marijuana-related industry. The class, titled "Entrepreneurial Opportunities in Emerging Markets: Marijuana Legalization," was launched. Tim Cook, Apple's CEO, unveiled a $1 billion fund on May 3, aimed at fostering advanced manufacturing jobs within the United States. In an interview with CNBC, Cook explained that this initiative would serve as a catalyst, as the creation of manufacturing jobs would in turn generate more service-related jobs. The announcement follows repeated requests from President Trump for American corporations to bring manufacturing jobs back to domestic soil. However, Cook did not specify whether Apple would establish a large-scale manufacturing operation in the U.S. to produce its products, as the majority of Apple's products are currently manufactured in China due to lower operating costs. Apple's $1 billion fund could be perceived as part of a strategy to align with the Trump administration, potentially securing favorable conditions for its business operations. Issues of concern for Apple and other corporations include the suspension of expedited H-1B visa processing and the possibility of more favorable conditions to encourage U.S. firms to repatriate foreign-held revenue. Over 93% of Apple's $256.8 billion cash reserves are held overseas. In addition to the manufacturing fund, Cook discussed other initiatives. Apple is exploring ways to expand its workforce, developer community, and domestic manufacturing capabilities. The company is also developing programs to encourage more Americans to learn coding and software creation, with details to be announced over the summer. Cook emphasized that a company's role is to embody values, and part of that involves giving back to the community. He cited Apple's efforts in environmental conservation, renewable energy usage, and job creation as examples of its philanthropic endeavors. Cook revealed that the plan for Apple's $1 billion fund is already in motion, with further details to be disclosed later this month. Other tech companies, such as Amazon and Intel, have also recently invested in creating domestic job opportunities. Amazon aims to create 100,000 new full-time positions by summer 2018, while Intel is investing $7 billion in an Arizona chip plant.
The Royal Canadian Mounted Police (RCMP) in New Brunswick are leveraging social media in their efforts to locate a suspected child abuser and child pornographer. In an unprecedented step, the police are encouraging the public to share images of the suspect on social media platforms. As Const. Jullie Rogers-Marsh explains, "Our aim is to disseminate his image to as many people as possible, in the hope of identifying him, and potentially identifying the victim as well." The suspect is identified through a video where a man is seen sexually abusing a girl believed to be around three years old. The video, initially posted online in 2005, has been a subject of investigation by multiple police agencies across North America. Investigators believe the video was produced in North America and that the girl is now likely between the ages of 10 and 12. The video was brought to the attention of the New Brunswick RCMP during an unrelated investigation. Although they are now spearheading the investigation, they cannot confirm whether the suspect and victim are local. Rogers-Marsh notes, "The video suggests it was taken in North America, but they could be from anywhere." Jean Sauvageau, an associate professor in the Department of Criminology and Criminal Justice at St. Thomas University, highlights that while police often seek public assistance, this scale is unusual. He cautions that while it could aid the investigation, it could also lead to false reports, unnecessary frenzy on social media, and potential false accusations. The suspect is described as a white male with brown hair, a distinctive circular mark on his right forearm, and a ring on his left hand. Anyone with information is asked to contact the police. This report is filed by CTV Atlantic's Andy Campbell.

Nestle, a prominent confectionery company, plans to eliminate nearly 300 jobs and relocate the production of the Blue Riband chocolate biscuit to Poland, according to unions. The majority of these job cuts will impact the company's sites in York and Newcastle, as well as a limited number in Halifax, West Yorkshire, and Girvan, Ayrshire. The GMB and Unite unions have voiced their disapproval of this decision, with the GMB stating that Nestle should "export chocolate, not jobs." The company is reportedly planning to cut 143 jobs in York, 110 at Fawdon, 15 in Halifax, and seven in Girvan. Tim Roache, GMB general secretary, expressed his discontent, stating, "It's unacceptable to move the production of a quintessential British brand like Blue Riband to Poland. Nestle is endangering the livelihoods of their employees and their families for the sake of increased profits." Roache further added, "These factories should be exporting chocolate, not jobs. The Government should intervene before it's too late and reassure workers across the country that this isn't the beginning of a Brexit-induced job loss trend." Nestle responded, stating, "These proposals could result in a reduction of 298 roles, primarily at York and Fawdon, through 2017 and 2018. The changes include amended and standardized shift patterns at each factory, and the transfer of Blue Riband production to a Nestle factory in Poland. This would streamline and focus Fawdon's operation." The company continued, "These proposals are being made to ensure these sites operate more efficiently and remain competitive in a rapidly changing environment. A 45-day consultation with trade unions and employee representatives will commence as soon as possible." Julia Long, Unite national officer, vowed, "We will strive to save as many jobs as possible and urge Nestle to reconsider these plans. Nestle should invest in its UK operations and keep production here in the UK." Derrick Gordon, the first openly gay player in NCAA Division I men's basketball, who played as a guard for the University of Massachusetts, has decided to transfer to another school for his final season in college. A network of mentors supported Gordon during his journey to this point, helping him through his groundbreaking status as the first openly gay male player in Division I basketball. Gordon, a 6-foot-2 guard, started his career at Western Kentucky and averaged 9.8 points and 4.9 rebounds per game this past season for the Minutemen. Last April, he publicly announced his sexuality. "I am grateful for the support I have received from the coaches and my teammates," Gordon stated. "Leaving UMass has nothing to do with my sexuality; instead, everyone has been incredibly supportive throughout my situation." Last season, UMass made it to the NCAA tournament, but this year, they finished with an overall record of 17-15 and a conference record of 10-8 in the Atlantic 10. Gordon explained his decision, stating, "This is a personal choice for me to pursue my dreams. I want to place myself in the best position to succeed and to win as many games as possible, and I hope to find a place where I can expand my role and make a meaningful contribution to the team."

As the US elections draw near, the White House is preparing for a seamless transition between administrations, with one key task being the transfer of the President's social media accounts. This includes the handover of the @POTUS Twitter account, established in May 2015 and boasting over 11 million followers, whose tweets will be erased to allow the incoming president to commence their social media campaign afresh from January 20. Similar procedures will apply to the Presidential Facebook page, Instagram account, as well as the White House’s YouTube, Medium, and Tumblr accounts. The Obama administration will partner with the National Archives and Records Administration (NARA) to preserve all content created during his tenure. This content will be accessible online through new handles such as @POTUS44 on Twitter, and the current WhiteHouse.gov site will also be archived and viewable at ObamaWhiteHouse.gov (not yet live). The administration also plans to make its archived content downloadable for public use and is soliciting ideas on how to make it easily accessible. President Obama, with his personal Twitter handle boasting about 78.5 million followers, may not be overly concerned about losing social media influence upon leaving office. It remains to be seen how the next president will employ technology to engage with the public in the coming years, hopefully avoiding any controversy associated with private email servers. For more information about the White House’s archival process and how it plans to make its content available from January 20, follow @WHWeb on Twitter. You can also read more about the digital transition in the social media age on The White House's website. Additionally, Microsoft is set to reveal more details about its VR headset plans in December.

In this review, I'm discussing my observations while using GS (Gnome Shell) in Ubuntu, contrasting it with the Vanilla Gnome experience. Although I'm using an older stylesheet, it's not just about LightDM or GDM. The File Manager, File Previewer (Sushi), Scroll bars, among other elements, contribute to a distinct experience. Even after installing GS in Ubuntu, the overall feel is significantly different. Please note that this isn't a comprehensive review; there are several aspects I haven't covered, and some features, like Pin Unlocking, are still missing or may not be functioning correctly. Notifications under Shield also couldn't be tested due to crashing issues. Regarding the login and lock screens, GDM and the Gnome Shell Lock Screen are separate modules, both of which can be customized through themes. However, the blue curtain with the large white time may not appeal to many users. The Gnome Shell Lock Screen features a new lock screen with a curtain effect and pin un-locker, although the pin un-locker isn't yet functional. At the moment, the curtain can only be slid up using a mouse, not a shortcut. It's worth mentioning that, despite the strong association between Ubuntu and Gnome, the relationship seems to be strained. Issues such as incompatibilities with Compiz/Clutter, problems with LightDM and GDM, discussions about removing Nautilus, and the un-maintained systemD are just a few examples. In conclusion, it's currently impossible to achieve a Vanilla Gnome experience in Ubuntu, and this situation isn't ideal for either party.
This article hails from our partner's archive. Born in 1896, Walter Breuning's life narrative mirrors the ascendancy of modern America. Breuning, who passed away on Thursday at the age of 114, resided in Montana and was only 26 days younger than Besse Cooper of Georgia, who presently holds the record for the oldest living person. He could recollect events as far back as the turn of the century, when his father narrated tales of engaging Southerners during the Civil War. Originally from Minnesota, Breuning began working for the railroad at the tender age of 16 and enlisted for World War I at 20, although he was never summoned for duty. In 1919, the year women gained the right to vote, Breuning purchased his first automobile and lamented about the alarming noise that scared horses away. The Great Depression struck, and though he considered himself fortunate to maintain employment, Breuning regarded President Franklin Roosevelt's enactment of Social Security as the nation's most significant accomplishment. By the time America entered World War II, Breuning was too old to participate, and by the time the Beatles released their debut album, the rail veteran had retired. The advent of computers transformed the railroad industry, and despite many of his colleagues losing their jobs in the process, the lifelong clerk viewed the machines as a positive development.

Michigan has chosen to compensate Jim Harbaugh's top three football assistants with annual salaries of $1 million each. This makes Michigan the first public institution, subject to Freedom of Information Act requests, to pay three assistant coaches such substantial amounts. Defensive coordinator Don Brown and offensive coordinator Tim Drevno have been retained with contracts worth over $10 million combined for the next five years. Passing coordinator Pep Hamilton was enticed away from the Cleveland Browns with a four-year deal worth $4.25 million. Details of these contracts were obtained by The Associated Press via an FOIA request. Brown's contract specifies that he will earn $1 million annually for the first four years, increasing to $1.4 million in 2021. He is eligible for retention bonuses of $300,000 in April of this year and next year, and $400,000 in April 2019 and 2020. Drevno's deal is worth $1 million per year, plus a $150,000 signing bonus this month. Athletic director Warde Manuel offered contracts to Brown and Drevno in December, before the Wolverines lost to Florida State in the Orange Bowl. Hamilton's offer was extended on January 9th. Hamilton, who was an associate head coach for the Browns last season, replaced Jedd Fisch who left to become UCLA's offensive coordinator. Hamilton's salary will be $1 million for the first three years of his deal, rising to $1.25 million in 2020. He will receive a $150,000 signing bonus and is eligible for retention bonuses of $450,000 in April 2018 and $250,000 the following year. Both Drevno and Brown have been part of Harbaugh's staff during his two seasons at Michigan. Brown was hired last year. Michigan announced on Monday that it will hold three of its spring practices in Rome, just days after the NCAA banned schools from combining spring break and football practices, as Harbaugh did last year in Florida.

In 1975, David Bowie received a Kirlian photography machine from UCLA's parapsychology lab, which he used to capture images of peoples' "auras." This machine generates a high-voltage field to a photographic plate, resulting in a glowing corona discharge image of whatever is positioned on the plate. The color, shape, and intensity of the image are influenced by various factors, including humidity, grounding, oil and sweat on the skin, and, in the case of people, drug consumption. Given Bowie's fascination with the occult and unusual phenomena, he found the idea of photographing his "aura" intriguing. As reported by The Daily Grail, Bowie experimented with Kirlian photography, and some of the resulting images were featured in the program for his 1976 tour in support of Station to Station. Moreover, he used the technique to explore the effects of drugs on his body. He compared two Kirlian photographs of his fingertip, one taken before consuming cocaine and the other after. Bowie was so captivated by the image that he included it in the Earthling (1997) booklet and used it as the cover art for the "Little Wonder" single.

Most individuals who rely daily on laptops and smartphones for charging likely use their laptops to power their phones. To simplify this process and minimize the number of cables carried, Intel is experimenting with inductive charging. By simply placing your phone near the laptop, it can charge. As reported by The Verge, Intel's novel all-in-one PC design incorporates inductive charging for the keyboard, with aspirations to extend this feature to ultrabooks, enabling them to recharge phones. Demonstrated using an Acer Aspire laptop, the wireless charger is sleek enough to not significantly increase the ultrabook's profile, and it can charge compatible phones when in close proximity. A confirmation sound and screen notification signal successful charging. The aim is to reduce the frequency of carrying a phone charger, though it may necessitate a more robust power source for the laptop. However, before we hail this as a more environmentally friendly solution due to fewer cords, we need to understand the efficiency and embodied energy of the transmitter (often referred to as a "special bump") on the laptop's side and the receiver on the phone. Given the likely larger size compared to a simple USB cord, we suspect it may consume more energy. Additionally, it remains unclear whether inductive charging will completely replace cords, as a commenter on The Verge article notes: "It's great for charging phones, but when I connect my phone to my laptop, I usually do so to access storage. If I anticipate prolonged laptop use, I leave it plugged in to charge, while also utilizing the phone's storage." Could inductive charging be a greener method for charging phones? It's plausible, and the concept is intriguing. However, we're not quite at that point yet.
