Noam Chomsky, an intellectual and self-proclaimed libertarian socialist, told BBC News that the Republican Party is the most dangerous organization in history due to their lack of action against climate change. When asked about the comparison to entities like Kim Jong Un of North Korea or ISIS, Chomsky questioned whether ISIS was actively attempting to undermine the prospects for human civilization. He did not mention that ISIS is embroiled in a civil war and is seeking to overthrow the governments of at least Syria and Iraq, nor did he acknowledge the atrocities ISIS has committed, such as beheadings and religious persecution. Experts estimate that ISIS militants have killed over 33,000 people. Chomsky, however, argues that the Republicans are more dangerous because they are not only failing to address climate change, but are actively trying to speed up the process towards environmental catastrophe. "What does it mean to say we're not doing anything about climate change, but we're trying to accelerate the race to the precipice," he said. Chomsky, a professor emeritus at the Massachusetts Institute of Technology, has a history of criticizing American imperialism. He opposed the Vietnam war in the 1960s and 70s and considered the collapse of the Soviet Union a victory for socialism, not capitalism.

I stumbled upon a small table at an estate sale and couldn't resist purchasing it. Unfortunately, in my haste, I neglected to thoroughly inspect it for major repairs, overlooking a damaged foot that was quite noticeable. Fortunately, Bondo, my trusty repair solution, came to the rescue once again. The foot required several layers of Bondo to restore its structure and level it with the other feet. In a by-election four months following his victory as Progressive Conservative Party leader, Patrick Brown has successfully secured a seat in the Ontario legislature, previously held by longtime MPP Garfield Dunlop. Dunlop vacated his seat in Simcoe North this summer to pave the way for Brown's candidacy. After clinching the party leadership in May, Brown relinquished his federal seat in the nearby riding of Barrie. During his leadership race, Dunlop was a vocal critic of Brown. However, upon resigning his seat for the leader, Dunlop adopted a more conciliatory tone and endorsed Brown in Simcoe North. Leveraging his campaign organization and canvassing skills that propelled him to victory over caucus favorite Christine Elliott in the leadership race, Brown spent the summer preparing for the by-election. Preliminary results indicate Brown garnered over 50% of the vote, defeating Liberal candidate Fred Larsen, who had previously lost to Dunlop in the two prior elections. NDP candidate Elizabeth Van Houtte, a social work professor at Lakehead University, also participated in the election.

By examining the primary factors leading to job losses due to our EU membership, I aim to provide a cautious assessment of the number of jobs potentially lost as a result. The primary contributor to job loss is in the manufacturing sector. High energy costs have led to the shutdown of petrochemical plants, aluminum smelters, steel mills, and other energy-intensive industries. This has resulted in our inability to meet our own energy demands, necessitating imports from France via the interconnector. If we had energy prices comparable to the US, thanks to increased domestic production of oil, gas, and shale gas, and German-style coal-fired power stations, we could potentially see a 15% increase in manufacturing jobs, equating to approximately 450,000 additional jobs. Additionally, we would witness more jobs in the energy sector, potentially around 10% more or 50,000 additional jobs. The agricultural and fishing sectors have been hampered by quotas and the regulations of the Common Agricultural Policy (CAP) and Common Fisheries Policy. Implementing domestic policies could potentially add 10% or 30,000 jobs to these sectors. Summing up these figures, we arrive at an estimate of over 500,000 more jobs if the UK had greater control over its industrial policies, energy production, and business regulations. There could also be additional gains in the services sector, which is the largest area in our labor market.
The 16th annual Opening Our Doors Festival returns on Monday, October 9, offering over 80 free activities for Boston residents to enjoy. Highlights include special performances from the Huntington Theatre Company and gallery walks through renowned art institutions such as the Gardner Museum and Museum of Fine Arts. Community organizations, youth performers, and artists will showcase their talents across various locations, providing a unique opportunity to experience the cultural richness of the Fenway Cultural District. Families, young adults, and college students can expect activities tailored to their interests, with performances like the Harry Potter Soundtrack Orchestra and Berklee's all-male a capella group, the CharlieChords, scheduled for the Krentzman Quad. The American Therapy Booth, an interactive art installation by Julie Ann Otis, is another not-to-be-missed event. Attendees can participate in live drawing sessions while sharing their experiences as Americans. The installation is nonjudgmental and does not take political sides. For theater enthusiasts, the Huntington Theatre Company will host an open house, allowing attendees to view performances from Merrily We Roll Along and speak with the theater's managing director about the upcoming 2017-2018 season. Despite a forecast of rain, the Fenway Alliance assures that all activities will proceed as planned, with indoor alternatives available for outdoor events. The festivities will commence at the Christian Science Plaza at 10 a.m. Executive Director of the Fenway Alliance and founder of Opening Our Doors, Kelly Brilliant, expresses pride in maintaining the event as a free day for everyone, despite economic divisions. She believes it is a special opportunity to come together as a community without financial barriers. Join us for Opening Our Doors on Monday, October 9, from 10 a.m. to 4 p.m. For more information, visit fenwayculture.org.
Video footage from CCTV cameras captures the instant three young girls from South Auckland schools stepped onto a bustling road, only to be hit by a car. According to the authorities, the incident occurred close to the Otahuhu police station on Great South Road around 9 a.m. The victims, aged 5 and 10, were en route to school when the accident happened. Currently, they are receiving medical care in the hospital. The CCTV footage reveals the girls preparing to cross Great South Road. As they stepped out, they found themselves in the path of an approaching vehicle. Sergeant Matthew Child of Counties Manukau Police stated that preliminary reports suggest the vehicle was moving within the speed limit or even slower, was proceeding with the traffic flow, and had a green light. He added that the female driver had recently dropped off her own children at a primary school and was heading home at the time of the accident. Police emphasize that, given the busy nature of the road, the girls should have been supervised by an adult while crossing.

David Marcus, currently the Head of Messenger at Facebook, is set to join Coinbase's Board of Directors. As Vice President of Messaging Products at Facebook, Marcus brings valuable experience in creating significant, trustworthy mobile-first products at scale. His expertise will broaden and deepen the Coinbase board, aiding the company's leadership team as they strive to become the most popular and secure platform for buying and selling digital currencies. Before his role at Messenger, Marcus served as the President of PayPal, overseeing the payments company's global expansion and product strategy. Under his leadership, PayPal reclaimed its technology and product-centric focus, regained the trust of developers and small businesses, and acquired Braintree, the parent company of the popular P2P payment app, Venmo, boosting the company's overall growth. Marcus joined PayPal following the acquisition of his previous startup, mobile payments company Zong, and led the Mobile products division before assuming the top position at the company. Marcus' insights and experience in introducing groundbreaking products to the market will prove invaluable to Coinbase as it continues to grow. His understanding of both the payments and mobile sectors will guide Coinbase in its mission to create a truly global, open financial system that offers opportunities to people worldwide. Brian Armstrong, CEO and co-founder of Coinbase, expressed his enthusiasm, stating, "I’ve been captivated by cryptocurrencies since 2012, and I’ve seen how Coinbase has been working to democratize access to this new asset class. I believe that what the company is working on has the potential to significantly alter lives worldwide, and I'm excited to collaborate with Coinbase and its leadership team to bring this vision to fruition." David Marcus, Vice President of Messaging Products at Facebook, shared his sentiments, stating, "I've been intrigued by cryptocurrencies since 2012, and I've witnessed how Coinbase has been making strides in democratizing access to this new asset class. I'm convinced that what the company is doing has the potential to dramatically impact lives globally, and I'm eager to work with Coinbase and its leadership team to help make this vision a reality."

The Canadian Army announced the delivery of the first Textron Tactical Armoured Patrol Vehicle (TAPV) to the 5th Canadian Division at Gagetown, New Brunswick. Six vehicles are initially received for operator and maintainer training. Over a 17-month span, a fleet of 500 TAPVs will be distributed among seven bases and 24 units. The Canadian Army aims to achieve full operational capability by mid-2020, following the completion of training for all operators and user trials confirming operational readiness. The TAPVs from Textron will be delivered in two variants: General Utility and Reconnaissance. Equipped with remote weapons stations, these vehicles enable gunners to aim and fire from the interior. The remote weapons stations are outfitted with both a 40-mm automatic grenade launcher and a C6 machine gun, as the army specified. The 5th Canadian Division has shared photos to publicize the arrival of the initial vehicles.

A photograph of a Philadelphia firefighter, John Deluisi, has sparked controversy due to its content. Some individuals are labeling the image as insensitive and racist, while Deluisi himself has apologized for what he considers a poor joke. He states, "I am deeply disappointed in myself and I'm genuinely sorry." Deluisi admits that he was intoxicated when he took the picture and tagged an African American colleague at the Philadelphia Fire Department. The image depicts Deluisi holding a burning tiki torch, wearing a Confederate flag hat, and captioned with the statement, "headed to Virginia." This post was published shortly after the city of Charlottesville experienced violent clashes between neo-Nazi white nationalists and protesters. Deluisi explains that the picture was a joke between friends, prompted by another post referencing Charlottesville. However, he acknowledges that the joke went too far. The post has since been removed, but not before offending many residents who finance Deluisi's salary. Philadelphia Mayor Jim Kenney has expressed his concern, labeling the post as "deeply disturbing." The Philadelphia Fire Department has initiated an investigation that may lead to disciplinary action. Deluisi is concerned that the post may impact his nearly 20-year career as a firefighter. He admits, "I am an idiot. I am genuinely sorry. Perhaps I get carried away on Facebook and post something foolish. I thought he would understand the joke, but it was incredibly stupid."

He added, "I will get to know Johnson better and decide if he is someone I could support." However, Romney ruled out both entering the race himself and voting for Hillary Clinton, the probable Democratic Party nominee. When asked about his decision, he responded, "My duty is to convey my beliefs about the potential nominee of the party to the American people." He continued, "I have expressed my views openly and clearly, and those who made the decision chose a different path. That's their right. Lee Kleinman initially expressed support for the fee-based ordinance on Friday, but five days later, he announced he would focus more on his own district, which does not have the same waste issues as others. This shift in focus came as a surprise to some of his southern sector colleagues. Kleinman questioned the need for him to improve conditions at Southwest Center Mall, where shoppers may want plastic bags, if the community is content with the current conditions. He suggested his efforts should be directed towards North Dallas redevelopment projects. Vonciel Jones Hill, who has previously voiced opposition to any ban or bag tax, was not present for the vote. Monica Alonzo also voted against the ordinance without comment. Following the vote, the American Progressive Bag Alliance issued a statement, expressing concern that the new bag fee would jeopardize 4,500 Texas jobs and negatively impact consumers. The alliance's executive director, Lee Califf, described the vote as an example of environmental myths and junk science driving poor policy in the plastic bag debate. The legality of Dallas' new bag "ban" or tax is uncertain, as Attorney General Greg Abbott is expected to weigh in on the matter following a request by state Rep. Dan Flynn of Canton on behalf of the Texas Retailers Association. Dallas City Attorney Warren Ernst stated that the city is prepared to defend the legality of the ordinance if it is the council's will to pass it. Jerry Allen expressed doubt, stating there is a significant amount of uncertainty. Council members opposed to the ordinance argue that Dallas needs to focus more on enforcing its litter laws. Council member Jordan pointed out that the city spends $4 million annually on trash pick-up, yet still faces litter issues. In the end, council member Scott Griggs noted that this is just the first step in addressing the larger issue of trash, with the city and council needing to tackle Styrofoam and other waste-related problems in the future.
A 23-year-old individual, identified as Jared Kelly from Papakura, has been prohibited from owning animals for five years and fined over $850 after admitting to neglecting his dog to the point of near starvation in the Papakura District Court. The dog, a boxer/staffordshire terrier mix, was discovered by an SPCA inspector in June of the previous year, chained up with no shelter. The animal was so malnourished that its bones were visible and it had no strength to bark. The dog was also reported to be infested with severe fleas, worms, and had overgrown claws, in addition to having open sores on its front legs and rump. Kelly confessed to the SPCA that he had lost interest in the dog and had considered having it euthanized. He subsequently surrendered the dog to SPCA Auckland. Bob Kerridge, executive director of SPCA Auckland, described the situation as deeply sad, stating, "This is a heart-wrenching case where an animal that relied entirely on its owner for affection and care was left chained up, without food or shelter, simply because the owner had 'lost interest' and neglected their responsibilities." Kerridge added that losing interest in an animal did not grant anyone the right to neglect it to the point of starvation. Tragically, the dog had to be humanely euthanized due to behavioral problems that made it impossible to responsibly rehome it. Kerridge believes that these issues likely stemmed from the neglect the dog had endured.

Russia has agreed to aid India in constructing at least ten additional nuclear power plants, as announced by Indian Prime Minister Narendra Modi following a meeting with Russian President Vladimir Putin. On Thursday, the two nations signed a series of significant energy accords. In addition, Russia will remain India's primary defense supplier, according to Modi. Putin's visit to Delhi occurs amidst India's energy crisis and Russia's efforts to strengthen ties with Asia in response to Western sanctions. During their discussions, the leaders outlined an ambitious vision for nuclear energy, with the new reactors to be built over the course of the next two decades. Under the agreement, nuclear components will be produced domestically in India. A $1 billion joint venture to support hydroelectric power projects in India has also been agreed upon, as reported by Reuters. Meanwhile, Russian oil producer Rosneft has signed a deal to supply India with 10 million tonnes of oil annually. Putin earlier expressed his country's intent to export more oil and gas to Asia due to complications in the European market. The South Stream gas pipeline project to Europe was recently canceled due to concerns about potential breaches of EU competition rules. Additionally, the ongoing crisis in Ukraine has led to a rift between Russia and the West, with Russia facing sanctions from the US, EU, and several other countries. Despite recent lost contracts to the US and Europe, Russia will continue to be a significant defense supplier to India, our correspondent in Delhi reports. One of several defense deals includes a plan by Russia to manufacture its most advanced military helicopter in India. Historically, Russia and India have been close allies, but their relationship has been strained in recent years. India is reportedly displeased with Russia for selling attack helicopters to Pakistan, while Russia has been disappointed with India for choosing French Rafale fighters and American Apache attack helicopters over Russian defense products. Later today, Putin will meet with business leaders and attend a diamond conference in Delhi. The two countries are expected to sign an agreement aimed at improving bilateral diamond trade. India desires to encourage Russia to export more uncut diamonds directly, as Russia is the world's leading producer of rough diamonds and India is the global center for cutting and polishing gemstones. The Punjab and Haryana High Court has issued a show cause notice to the Senior Superintendent of Police (SSP) of Kapurthala district, inquiring why contempt proceedings should not be initiated against him. This action stems from the SSP's alleged failure to act on a complaint against self-proclaimed 'godwoman' Sukhwinder Kaur alias Radhe Maa. The notice was issued by a single bench of Justice Daya Chaudhary, following a complaint filed by Phagwara resident Surinder Mittal. The case will be heard on October 13. As reported by Krishan Singh Dadwal, the complainant's counsel, the high court has directed the Kapurthala SSP to explain why contempt proceedings should not be initiated due to the intentional disregard of a previous court order. In 2015, Surinder Mittal lodged a complaint against Radhe Maa, accusing her of hurting religious sentiments, threats, and other offences under the Indian Penal Code (IPC). When no action was taken by the police, Mittal approached the high court, seeking appropriate directions. Previously, the high court had directed the Kapurthala SSP to investigate the allegations against Radhe Maa, determine if any cognizable offence was committed, and take appropriate action. However, despite reminders about the court order, no action was taken on the complaint by the police. Consequently, the complainant had to approach the high court again, this time filing a contempt petition.

For the subsequent five years, China's authorities have imposed a ban on the construction of government buildings as part of an initiative to demonstrate the country's ruling Communist Party's commitment to combating corruption and the misuse of public funds. This directive, jointly issued by the general offices of the Communist Party's central committee and the State Council (China's cabinet), was announced on Tuesday, as reported by the official Xinhua News Agency. Throughout China, imposing and extravagant government buildings, adorned with oversized offices and luxurious lighting, are often the most striking structures in towns, frequently eliciting public disapproval. President Xi Jinping has spearheaded a movement to eliminate excess, formality, and waste among high-ranking officials, a campaign that has been met with criticism from ordinary citizens. According to Xinhua, the directive mandates a complete halt to the construction of official buildings, as well as the construction of ostentatious structures designed as training centers, hotels, or government motels. Some government agencies have constructed such buildings in seaside resorts and scenic spots as perks for their officials and employees, who can stay there for free or at significantly reduced rates. These buildings sometimes operate as profit-making ventures open to the public. Liu Shanying, a politics researcher at the Chinese Academy of Social Sciences in Beijing, stated, "Some office buildings consume a substantial amount of money, with operating costs and expenses on dining and entertainment, all funded by government funds, making it a form of corruption." Liu Shanying considers the five-year construction ban a significant step in the fight against corruption. The ruling also requires officials holding multiple positions to maintain only one office, and for the offices of those who have retired or are on leave to be returned in a timely manner. The directive encourages party and government bodies to practice frugality and ensure that government spending is directed towards economic development and improving public welfare. However, officials will still be allowed to allocate funds for restoring government offices, as reported by Xinhua. Previously, there have been restrictions on constructing new government buildings, but some departments and localities have constructed government office compounds in violation of regulations.
